ADOPTING ORDINANCES AND RESOLUTIONS
RESOLUTION NO. 7-96
   A RESOLUTION TO ADOPT THE REVISED ASHLEY TOWN CODE RECENTLY PREPARED BY
HOOSIER CODIFICATION SERVICES, INC.
NOW THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED by the Town Council of the Town of Ashley,
Indiana:
That the Ashley Town Code, recently revised and recodified by Hoosier
Codification Services, Inc. is hereby adopted. Further, that the Ashley Town
Code of Ordinances previously used, shall be retired and the same shall no
longer have any force or affect.
PASSED AND ADOPTED by the Town Council of the Town of Ashley, Indiana, this 9th
day of September, 1996.
                                                                                    
                                    DON A. FARRINGTON, President
                                    and Trustee
                                                                                    
                                    RANDY L. McENTARFER, Trustee
                                                                                    
                                    RICHARD C. SCHIFFLI, Trustee
ATTEST:
                                    
KAREN M. McENTARFER
Clerk-Treasurer
Presented by me to the President of the Town Council of the Town of Ashley,
Indiana, this 9th day of September, 1996
                                                                                    
                                    KAREN M. McENTARFER
                                    Clerk-Treasurer
Approved and signed by the following members of the Town Council, Town of
Ashley, Indiana.
                                    Don A. Farrington, President
                                    Randy L. McEntarfer, Councilperson
                                    Richard C. Schiffli, Councilperson
ORDINANCE NO. 98-02
   AN ORDINANCE ENACTING AND ADOPTING A SUPPLEMENT TO THE TOWN OF ASHLEY CODE
OF ORDINANCES AND DECLARING AND EMERGENCY
   WHEREAS, American Legal Publishing Corporation of Cincinnati, Ohio, has
completed the 1997 supplement to the Code of Ordinances of the Town of Ashley,
which supplement contains all ordinances of a general and permanent nature
enacted since the prior supplement of the Code of Ordinances of the Town of
Ashley; and
   WHEREAS, American Legal Publishing Corporation has recommended the revision
or addition of certain sections of the Code of Ordinances which are based upon,
or make reference to, sections of the Indiana Code; and
   WHEREAS, it is the intent of the Town of Ashley Town Council to accept
updated sections in accordance with the changes of the law of the State of
Indiana; and
   WHEREAS, it is necessary to provide for the usual daily operation of the
municipality and for the immediate preservation of the public peace, health,
safety, and general welfare of the municipality that this ordinance take effect
at an early date;
   NOW THEREFORE, BE ORDAINED by the Town Council, Town of Ashley, State of
Indiana:
Section 1. That the 1997 supplement to the Code of Ordinances of the Town of
Ashley as submitted by American Legal Publishing Corporation of Cincinnati,
Ohio, and as attached hereto, be and the same is hereby adopted by reference as
if set out in its entirety..
Section 2. Such supplement shall be deemed published as of the date of its
adoption and approval by the Town of Ashley Town Council and the Clerk of the
Town of Ashley is hereby authorized and ordered to insert such supplement into
the copy of the Code of Ordinances kept on file in the office of the Clerk.
Section 3. This ordinance is declared to be an emergency measure necessary for
the immediate preservation of the peace, health, safety and general welfare of
the people of this municipality, and shall take effect at the earliest date
provided by law.
Section 4. BE IT FURTHER ORDAINED that this ordinance is in full force and
effect from and after its passage by the Town Council of the Town of Ashley,
Indiana, this 8th day of June, 1998.
   5   (Supplement 4/99)
PASSED AND ADOPTED by the Town Council of the Town of Ashley, Indiana, this 8th
day of June, 1998.
                                                                                    
                                    Don A. Farrington, President
                                                                                    
                                    Randy L. McEntarfer, Trustee
                                                                                    
                                    Richard C. Schiffli, Trustee
ATTEST:
                                    
Karen M. McEntarfer
Clerk-Treasurer
Presented by me to the President of the Town Council, of Ashley, Indiana, this
8th day of June, 1998.
                                                                                    
                                    KAREN M. MCENTARFER
                                    Clerk-Treasurer
VOTING:                           AYE                     NAY

ORDINANCE NO. 99 - 02
   AN ORDINANCE ENACTING AND ADOPTING A SUPPLEMENT TO THE CODE OF ORDINANCES
FOR THE TOWN OF ASHLEY, INDIANA, AND DECLARING AN EMERGENCY
WHEREAS, American Legal Publishing Corporation of Cincinnati, Ohio has
completed the 1998 supplement to the Code of Ordinances of the Town of Ashley,
which supplement contains all ordinances of a general and permanent nature
enacted since the prior supplement to the Code of Ordinances of the Town of
Ashley; and
WHEREAS, American Legal Publishing Corporation has recommended the revision or
addition of certain sections of the Code of Ordinances which are based on or
make reference to sections of the Indiana Code; and
WHEREAS, it is the intent of the Town of Ashley Town Council to accept updated
sections in accordance with the changes of the law of the State of Indiana; and
WHEREAS, it is necessary to provide for the usual daily operation of the
municipality and for the immediate preservation of the public peace, health,
safety and general welfare of the municipality that this ordinance take effect
at an early date;
NOW, THEREFORE, BE ORDAINED by the Town Council, Town of Ashley, State of
Indiana:
SECTION 1. That the 1998 Supplement to the Code of Ordinances of the Town of
Ashley as submitted by American Legal Publishing Corporation of Cincinnati,
Ohio, and as attached hereto, be and the same is hereby adopted by reference as
if set out in its entirety.
SECTION 2. Such supplement shall be deemed published as of the date of its
adoption and approved by the Town of Ashley Town Council and the Clerk of the
Town of Ashley is hereby authorized and ordered to insert such supplement into
the copy of the Code of Ordinances kept on file in the office of the Clerk.
SECTION 3. This Ordinance is declared to be an emergency measure necessary for
the immediate preservation of the peace, health, safety and general welfare of
the people of this municipality, and shall take effect at the earliest date
provided by law.
SECTION 4. BE IT FURTHER ORDAINED that this ordinance is in full force and
effect from and after its passage by the Town Council of the Town of Ashley,
Indiana, this  14  day of  June,1999.
                                                                
   DON A. FARRINGTON, President

completed the 2000 supplement to the Code of Ordinances of the Town of Ashley,
which supplement contains all ordinances of a general and permanent nature
enacted since the prior supplement to the Code of Ordinances of the Town of
Ashley; and
   WHEREAS, American Legal Publishing Corporation has recommended the revision
or addition of certain sections of the Code of Ordinances which are based on or

   WHEREAS, it is the intent of the Town of Ashley Town Council to accept

Indiana; and

municipality and for the immediate preservation of the public peace, health,
safety and general welfare of the municipality that this ordinance take effect
at an early date;
   NOW, THEREFORE, BE ORDAINED by the Town Council, Town of Ashley, State of
Indiana:

completed the 2002 supplement to the Code of Ordinances of the Town of Ashley,

municipality and for the immediate preservation of the public peace, health,
safety and general welfare of the Town of Ashley that this ordinance take

completed the [2004] supplement to the Code of Ordinances of the Town of
Ashley, which supplement contains all ordinances of a general and permanent

   WHEREAS, American Legal Publishing Corporation has recommended the revision

Indiana; and

safety and general welfare of the Town of Ashley that this ordinance take
effect at an early date;

ORDINANCE NO. 2006-06
AN ORDINANCE ENACTING AND ADOPTING A SUPPLEMENT TO THE CODE OF ORDINANCES FOR
THE TOWN OF ASHLEY, INDIANA, AND DECLARING AN EMERGENCY
   WHEREAS, American Legal Publishing Corporation of Cincinnati, Ohio, has
completed the 2006 supplement to the Code of Ordinances of the Town of Ashley,
which supplement contains all ordinances of a general and permanent nature
enacted since the prior supplement to the Code of Ordinances of the Town of
Ashley; and
   WHEREAS, American Legal Publishing Corporation has recommended the revision
or addition of certain sections of the Code of Ordinances which are based on or
make reference to sections of the Indiana Code; and
   WHEREAS, it is the intent of the Town of Ashley Town Council to accept
updated sections in accordance with the changes of the law of the State of
Indiana; and
   WHEREAS, it is necessary to provide for the usual daily operation of the
municipality and for the immediate preservation of the public peace, health,
safety and general welfare of the Town of Ashley that this ordinance take
effect at an early date;
   NOW, THEREFORE BE ORDAINED by the Town Council, Town of Ashley, State of
Indiana:
SECTION 1.   That the 2006 Supplement to the Code of Ordinances of the Town of

SECTION 2.    Such supplement shall be deemed published as of the date of its

SECTION 3.   This Ordinance is declared to be an emergency measure necessary

SECTION 4.    BE IT FURTHER ORDAINED that this ordinance is in full force and

ORDINANCE NO. 2007-03
AN ORDINANCE ENACTING AND ADOPTING A SUPPLEMENT TO THE CODE OF ORDINANCES FOR
THE TOWN OF ASHLEY, INDIANA, AND DECLARING AN EMERGENCY
   WHEREAS, American Legal Publishing Corporation of Cincinnati, Ohio, has
completed the 2006 supplement to the Code of Ordinances of the Town of Ashley,
which supplement contains all ordinances of a general and permanent nature
enacted since the prior supplement to the Code of Ordinances of the Town of
Ashley; and
   WHEREAS, American Legal Publishing Corporation has recommended the revision
or addition of certain sections of the Code of Ordinances which are based on or
make reference to sections of the Indiana Code; and
   WHEREAS, it is the intent of the Town of Ashley Town Council to accept
updated sections in accordance with the changes of the law of the State of
Indiana; and
   WHEREAS, it is necessary to provide for the usual daily operation of the
municipality and for the immediate preservation of the public peace, health,
safety and general welfare of the Town of Ashley that this ordinance take
effect at an early date;
   NOW, THEREFORE BE ORDAINED by the Town Council, Town of Ashley, State of
Indiana:
SECTION 1.   That the 2007 Supplement to the Code of Ordinances of the Town of
Ashley as submitted by American Legal Publishing Corporation of Cincinnati,
Ohio, and as attached hereto, be and the same is hereby adopted by reference as
if set out in its entirety.
SECTION 2.    Such supplement shall be deemed published as of the date of its
adoption and approved by the Town of Ashley Council and the Clerk of the Town
of Ashley is hereby authorized and ordered to insert such supplement into the
copy of the Code of Ordinances kept in the office of the Clerk.
SECTION 3.   This Ordinance is declared to be an emergency measure necessary
for the immediate preservation of the peace, health, safety and general welfare
of the people of the Town of Ashley, and shall take effect at the earliest date
provided by law.
SECTION 4.    BE IT FURTHER ORDAINED that this ordinance is in full force and
effect from and after its passage by the Town Council of the Town of Ashley,
Indiana, this 9th day of April, 2007.
                  Randy L. McEntarfer /s/       
                  Randy L. McEntarfer, President
                  Richard C. Schiffli /s/       
                  Richard C. Schiffli, Vice-President
                  Paul E. Kennedy /s/    
                  Paul E. Kennedy, Trustee
ATTEST:
Karen McEntarfer /s/             
Karen McEntarfer, Clerk-Treasurer
Presented by me to the President of the Town Council of Ashley, Indiana, this
9th day of April, 2007.
                  Karen McEntarfer /s/       
                  Karen McEntarfer, Clerk-Treasurer
VOTING:                     AYE          NAY
Randy L. McEntarfer                X
Richard C. Schiffli                X
Paul E. Kennedy                   X

if set out in its entirety.
SECTION 2.   Such supplement shall be deemed published as of the date of its
adoption and approved by the Town of Ashley Council and the Clerk of the Town
of Ashley is hereby authorized and ordered to insert such supplement into the
copy of the Code of Ordinances kept in the office of the Clerk.
SECTION 3.   This Ordinance is declared to be an emergency measure necessary
for the immediate preservation of the peace, health, safety and general welfare
of the people of Town of Ashley, and shall take effect at the earliest date
provided by law.
SECTION 4.   BE IT FURTHER ORDAINED that this ordinance is in full force and
effect from and after its passage by the Town Council of Town of Ashley,
Indiana, this  9th  day of  August , 2021.

CHAPTER 1
GENERAL PROVISIONS
Sec.
1-1   Code Citation and Designation.
Sec.
1-2   Effective Date of Code; Repeal of General Ordinances in Conflict; Savings
Clause
Sec.
1-3   Definitions
Sec.
1-4   Code Application.
Sec.
1-5   interpretation of Each Component Part of the Code.
Sec.
1-6   Repeal Shall Not Revive Ordinances.
Sec.
1-7   Effective Date of Ordinances.
Sec.
1-8   Severability of Code.
Sec.
1-9   General Penalties.
Sec.
1-10   Town Seal.
Sec.
1-11   Codification.
Sec. 1-1   Code Citation and Designation.
   a.   The ordinances contained in the following chapters, articles, and
sections shall constitute and be designated as the "Ashley Town Code", and may
be cited as the "Town Code" or, in the provisions which follows, as "this
Code".
   b.   Due to the proximity of the Towns of Ashley and Hudson, and the
cocooation of the respective Town Boards, the laws of both Towns have been
codified into one code book entitled "Ashley and Hudson Town Codes", with the
individual Codes separated within the publication.
Sec. 1-2   Effective Date of Code; Repeal of General Ordinances in Conflict;
Savings Clause.
   All of the provisions of this Code shall be in full force and effect from
the date of passage and the filing of this Code in the offices of the Clerk-
Treasurer, and all ordinances of a general and permanent nature in force at
that time are hereby repealed from and after said date.
   Such repeal shall not affect any offense or act committed or done or any
penalty or forfeiture incwred or any contract or right established or occuriing
before said effective date; nor shall it affect any ordinance accepting gifts
and dedications of real estate; nor any ordinance or resolution promising or
guaranteeing the payment of money by the Town or authorizing the issue of bonds
of said Town; or other evidence of the Town's indebtedness, or any contract or
obligation assumed by said Town; nor shall said repeal affect the
administration ordiiances or resolutions of this Code; nor shall it affect
transfer and appropriation ordinances; nor shall it affect any ordinance
concering annexation or dis-annexation of territories to or from the Town, or
any ordinances changing or concerning names of streets, or opening and closing
streets, or ordinances commonly known as zoning map amendments; nor shall it
affect any ordinance accepting, releasing or abandoning easements; nor shall it
affect any right, easement or fianchise, conferred by any person or
corporation; nor shall it affect any prosecution, suit or proceeding pending on
said date, except that the proceeding thereof shall conform as far as possible
to the provisions of this Code. 1
 
Notes
1 1   Adoptions of Ordinances and Resolutions and publication of a Town Code
  see: L C., §§ 36-5-2-10, 36-5-2-10.2, 36-1-5-3 - 36-1-5-6, 36-4-6-1 4.
Sec. 1-3   Definitions.
   In the construction of this Code and of all ordinances, the following
definitions shall be applied:
   a.   Board means the Town Council of the Town, except where the context
clearly indicates otherwise.
   b.   Clerk-Treasurer means the Clerk and Fiscal Officer of the Town of
Ashley.
   c.   Code means the Ashley Town Code.
   d.   Computation of Time means the time within which an act is to be done,
as herein provided, and shall be computed by excluding the first day and
including the last. If the last day be Sunday, it shall be excluded.
   e.   County means Steuben and DeKalb Counties, State of Indiana.
   f.   Et Seq. is the Latin Phrase meaning "and following".
   g.   Gender means words used in the masculine gender shall include feminine
and neuter.
   h.   I. C. shall refer to state law found in the Indiana Code.
   i.   May is permissive.
   j.   Month means a calendar month.
   k.   Must and shall are each mandatory.
   l.   Oath includes an affirmation of declaration in all cases in which, by
law, an affirmation may be substituted for an oath, and in such cases the words
"swear" and "sworn" shall be equivalent to the words "affirm" and affirmed".
   m.   Owner, applied to a building or land, includes any part owner, joint
owner, tenant in common, joint tenant, tenant by the entirety, of the whole or
a part of such building or land.
   n.   Person means any individual, firm, corporation, association, fiduciary,
or governmental entity.
   o.   Personal property includes every kind of property except real property.
   p.   Preceding and following mean next before and next after, respectively.
   q.   Property includes real and personal property.
   r.   Public place means any street or highway, sidewalk, park cemetery,
school yard or open space adjacent thereto and any lake or stream.
   s.   Real property shall include lands, tenements, and hereditaments.
   t.   Reasonable time means in all cases where any provision shall require
any act to be done in a "reasonable time" or "raasonable notice" to be given
any person, such reasonable time or notice shall be deemed to mean such time
only as may be necessary in the prompt execution of such duty or compliance
with such notice.
   u.   Sidewalk means any portion of the street between the curb line and the
adjacent property line, intended for the use of pedestrians, excluding
parkways.
   v.   Signature or Subscription includes a mark when the person cannot write.
   w.   State means the State of Indiana.
   x.   Street means to embrace streets, avenue, boulevards, roads, alleys,
viaducts and all other public highways in the Town.
   y.   Tenant - the words "tenant" or "occupant" apply to a building of land
and shall include any person holding a written or oral lease of, or who
occupied the whole or a part of such building or land, either alone or with
others.
   z.   Town means the Town of Ashley, Indiana, or the area within the
territorial limits of the Town of Ashley, Indiana, and such territory, if any,
outside the Town over which the Town has jurisdiction or control by virtue of
any constitutional or statutory provision.
   aa.   Written includes printed, typewritten, or otherwise reproduced in
permanent visible form.
   bb.   Year means a calendar year.
Sec. 1-4   Code Application.
   This Code shall refer only to the omission or commission of acts within the
territorial limits of the Town of Ashley and to that territory outside this
Town, if any, over which the Town has jurisdiction or control by virtue of any
constitutional provision or law.
Sec. 1-5   Interpretation of Each Component Part of the Code.
   a.   Each chapter is comprised of "articles" which address subject matter
classifications within the chapter. Articles may then be divided into
"divisions" which further define the particular topic.
   b.   Each section of this Code shall be numbered consecutively by chapter.
The number shall consist of two (2) component parts separated by a dash, the
figure before the dash referring to the chapter number and the figure after the
dash referring to the position of the section within the chapter.
   c.   The decimal system shall be used for all additions or amendments to
this Code. When a chapter or section is to be added, the new chapter or section
shall be given a decimal character.
Sec. 1-6   Repeal Shall Not Revive Ordinances.
   The repeal of an ordinance shall not repeal the repealing clause of an
ordinance or revive any ordinances which have been repealed thereby.
Sec. 1-7   Effective Date of Ordinance.
   Unless otherwise expressl provided, an Ordinance shall take effect when
passed according to Indiana Code, § 36-4-6-14(a) or 36-4-56-14(c); however, an
Ordinance prescribing a penalty or forfeiture for a violation must be published
pursuant to Indiana Code, §§ 36-4-6-14(b) or 36-4-6-14(c).
Sec. 1-8   Severability of Code.
   If any part, section, subsection, sentence, clause or pbrase of this Code is
for any reason declared to be unconstitutional or otherwise invalid, such
decision shall not affect the validity of the remaining portions of this Code.
Sec. 1-9   General Penalties.
   a.   Any person violating any of the provisions or failing to comply with
any of the mandatory requirements of this Code shall be guilty of an ordinance
violation.  2
   b.   Every day a violation of this Code is committed or permitted to
continue shall constitute a separate offense  3
   c.   Except in cases where different punishment is prescribed by a specific
section of this Code, any person convicted of an ordinance violation shall be
punished by a fine of not more than two thousand five hundred dollars
($2,500.00).  4
   d.   The Town may bring a civil action to enjoin any person from:
      1.   Violating any ordinance regulating or prohibiting a condition or use
of property; or
      2.   Engaging in conduct without a license if an ordinance requires a
license to engage in the conduct. 5
 
Notes
2 2 I.C., § 34-4-324 addresses ordinance violations.
3 3 I.C. § 94-1-127.1, addresses Class C infractions.
4 4 I.C. § 361-3-8, provides that the maximum penalty allowed is $2,500.00
5 5 I.C. § 36-1-4-4, addresses injunctions.
Sec. 1-10   Town Seal.
   a.   The Clerk-Treasurer shall be the custodian of the Town's Seal and affix
it to such documents and instruments as required.
   b.   The Town Seal of Ashley shall be as follows - It shall be in a disc
circular in form on the margin of which shall be the words: "Ashley, Indiana",
and in the center thereof, the word "Seal".
Sec. 1-11   Codification.
   a.   The Ashley Town Code consisting of Chapter 1 through Chapter 12,
inclusive, which is on file in the Office of the Clerk-Treasurer was adopted
and enacted as the Town Code of Ashley on September 14, 1987. (Ord. No. 87-8, §
1, 9-14-87)
   b.   Any and all additions or amendments to such Code, when passed in such
form as to indicate the intention of the Town Board (now Town Council) to make
the same apart thereof, shall be deemed to be incorpated in such Code, so that
reference to the Town Code of Ashley shall be understood and intended to
include such additions and amendments. (Ord. No. 8-87, § 4, 9-14-87)
   c.   Two (2) copies of the Ashley Town Code shall be kept on file in the
office of the Clerk-Treasurer, preserved in looseleaf form. It shall be the
express duty of the Clerk-Treasurer, or someone authorized by him, to insert in
their designated places all amendments or ordinances which indicate the
intention of the Town Board (now Town Council) to make the same a part of such
Code when the same shall have been printed or reprinted in page form and to
extract from such Code all provisions which may be from time to time repealed
by the Town Board (now Town Council). These copies of such Code shall be
available to all persons desiring to examine the same and shall be considered
the official Code of the Town of Ashley. (Or& No. 87-8, § 5, 9-14-87)
   d.   It shall be unlawful for any person, firm or corporation to change or
amend by additions or deletions, any part or portion of such code, or to insert
or delete pages or portions thereof, or to alter or tamper with such Code in
any manner whatsoever which will cause the Code, any ordinance, or the law of
the Town of Ashley to be misrepresented thereby. Any person, firm or
corporation violating this section shall be punished as provided in Section 1-
9 of such Code. (Ord. No. 87-8, § 6, 9-14-87)
   e.   It is declared to be the intention of the Town Board (now Town Council)
that the sections, paragraphs, sentences, clauses and phrases of such Code are
severable and if any phrase, clause, sentence, paragraph, section, article,
division, or chapter of such Code shall be declared unconstitutional or invalid
by the valid judgment or deiee of a court of competent jurisdiction, such
unconstitutionality or invalidity shall not affect any of the remaining
phrases, clauses, sentences, paragraphs, sections, article, division, and
chapter of such Code. (Ord. No. 87-8, § 7, 9-14-87)
   f.   Whenever in this Section or in such Code an act is prohibited or is
made or declared to be unlawful or an offence, or whenever in this ordinance or
in such Code the doing of any act is required or the failure to do any act is
declared to be unlawful, the violation of any such provision of this ordinance
or of such Code shall be punished by a fine not exceeding two thousand five
hundred dollars ($2,500.00) except where otherwise provided. The fine assessed
for the violation of any ordinance requiring a license may be a sum equal to
the amount required by the ordinance to be paid for such license. (Ore No. 87-
8, § 8, 9-14-87)
      In addition to the penalties hereinabove provided, any condition caused
or permitted to exist in violation of any of the provisions of such Code shall
be deemed a public nuisance and may be by the Town abated as provided by law,
and each day such condition shall continue to be regarded as a new and separate
offense (Ore No. 87-8, § 9, 9-14-87)

ARTICLE 1. THE TOWN CLERK-TREASURER
Sec. 2-1   Term of Office of Clerk-Treasurer.
   a.   The Town Clerk-Treasurer is an elected position whose term of office is
for four (4) years, beginning at noon on January 1st after his or her election
and continuing until a successor is elected and qualified. 1
   b.   The Town Clerk-Treasurer shall be elected by the voters of the whole
Town. 2
 
Notes
1   I.C., § 36-5-6-3, addresses the Clerk-Treasurer's term of office.
2   I.C., § 36-5-6-4, addresses the election of the Clerk-Treasurer.
Sec. 2-2   Powers and Duties.
   a.   The Town Clerk-Treasurer may administer oaths, takes depositions, and
takes acknowledgments of instruments as required by law. 3
   b.   The Town Clerk-Treasurer is the Clerk of the Town Council and whenever
the Town Council has an even number of members, the Clerk-Treasurer is an ex-
officio member for the purpose of casting the deciding vote to break a tie. 4
   c.   The Town Clerk-Treasurer may perform all duties prescribed by law,
which include but are not limited to the following:
      1.   receive and care for all Town monies, and pay them out upon order of
the Town Council;
      2.   keep accounts of all Town monies;
      3.   file monthly reports with the Town Council showing all receipts and
disbursements of the Town Treasury for the preceding month;
      4.   maintain records which are open for inspection by the Town Council;
      5.   collect fines resulting from ordinance violations;
      6.   issue all licenses; and
      7.   attend all Town Council meetings and maintain a recording of its
preceedings. 5
      8.   make investments of the Town's accounts and funds in a manner
consistent with responsible business practices and according to the Indiana
State Board of Accounts. (Res. No. 4-2004, 4-12-04)
      9.   establish a policy for writing off uncollectable debts owed to the
Town. Such policy shall be established by the Clerk-Treasurer according to
responsible accounting practices and the standards of the Indiana State Board
of Accounts. (Res. 5-2004, 4-12-04)
 
Notes
    I.C., § 36-5-6-5, authorizes the Clerk-Treasurer to administer oaths and
3 related powers. Editor's Note: During the 1996 Recodification the terms “Board
  of Trustees” were replaced with “Town Council”.
4   I.C., § 36-5-2-8, set forth the Clerk-Treasurer's role to the legislative
  body (Town Council).
5   I.C., § 36-5-6-6, sets forth the powers and duties of the Town Clerk-
  Treasurer.
Sec. 2-3   Compensation of Clerk-Treasurer.
   The compensation for the services of the person holding the office of Clerk-
Treasurer shall be fixed by the Town Council. 6
 
Notes
6   I.C., § 36-5-3-2, addresses compensation for the Town Clerk-Treasurer.
Sec. 2-4   Deputies and Employees.
   a.   The Clerk-Treasurer may appoint the number of deputies and employees
authorized by the Town Council.
   b.   Deputies and employees so hired serve at the pleasure of the Clerk-
Treasurer. 7
 
Notes
7   I.C., § 36-5-6-7, authorizes the Clerk-Treasurer to appoint deputies and
  employees.
Sec. 2-5   Credit Card.
   The Clerk-Treasurer shall obtain a credit card through the Garrett State
Bank and shall retain said credit card at her offices.
   Town department heads may make a request from time to time to utilize said
credit card for budgeted items.
   All such purchases shall be made as approved by the Clerk-Treasurer.
(Ord. 2021-01, 4-11-21)
Sec. 2-6   Electronic Funds Transfer and Online Banking.
   1.   Automatic Clearing House (ACH) Transactions: ACH transactions are
hereby authorized for the Clerk-Treasurer to make specific payments via ACH.
Authorized payments are payroll, bond payments, payments for monthly bills, and
payments from any funds received via ACH.
   2.   Electronic Funds Transfer (EFT) Including Online Transfers: Online
transfers are hereby authorized for the purpose of transferring funds to the
Accounts Payable Checking account from the General checking account as it
relates to services in the process of paying claims or invoices where no claim
is required.
   3.   The Clerk-Treasurer is required to maintain adequate documentation of
the above-referenced transactions for future audits, as provided by law.
(Res. 05-2022, §§ 1-3, 8-8-22)
Article 2. TOWN MARSHAL.
Sec. 2-7   Appointment, Compensation, Tenure of Town Marshal.
   a.   The Town Council shall appoint a Town Marshal and shall fix his
compensation. 8
   b.   The Town Marshal serves at the pleasure of the Town Council and is
subject to the minimum basic training requirements. 9
   c.   The Town of Ashley exercises it's right of Home Rule powers by
providing police protection for the Town through its Town Marshal. (Ord. No.
83-1, § 1, 3-14-83)
 
Notes
8   I.C., § 36-5-7-2, authorizes the Board of Trustees to appoint a Town Marshal
  and I.C., § 36-5-3-2, addresses his compensation.
9   I.C., § 36-5-7-3, addresses tenure, training and removal procedures.
Sec. 2-8   Powers and Duties of the Town Marshal.
   The Town Marshal is the chief police officer and has the powers of other law
enforcement officers as set forth in Indiana Code, § 36-5-7-4 as it may be
amended from time to time.
Sec. 2-9   Deputy Marshals. 10
   a.   The Town Council may authorize the appointment of deputy marshals
pursuant to Indiana Code, § 36-5-7-6, as it may be amended from time to time.
   b.   The designation Deputy Marshall shall become a position with the Police
Department of the Town of Ashley. (Ord. No. 94-10, § 1, 3-14-94)
   c.   The Deputy Marshall of the Town of Ashley shall be, and is fully
authorized and empowered to act on behalf of and in the name of the Town of
Ashley, as its agent to accept pension liability, pursuant to I. C., § 5-10.2-
3-1 and further to execute and deliver documents related to the Public
Employees Retirement Fund of Indiana. This resolution will remain in full force
and effect until modified or rescinded by subsequent resolution and receipt
thereof in writing by the Director of PERF. (Res. No. 95-11, 9-11-95)
   d.   The position of Chief Deputy Town Marshal is made part of the Police
Department. (Ord. No. 2007-12, § 2, 8-23-07)
 
Notes

Sec. 2-10   Police Department - Reporting of Hours.
   The Ashley Police Department will report their hours segregated as to
"Stand-By Time or On-Call Time" and then Work Time in any report generation.
(Res. No. 92-01, 5-13-92)
Sec. 2-11   Police Department - Residency Restrictions.
   1.   All police officers of the Town of Ashley must live within twenty (20)
miles of the Town limits of the Town of Ashley, Indiana.
   2.   Unless the Ashley Town Marshal or the Ashley Town Council determines an
emergency exists, no police vehicle shall be taken home by police officers when
off duty if they reside more than five (5) miles from the Town limits of the
Town of Ashley.
   3.   All current police officers shall have one year from February 10, 2014
to come into compliance and all newly hired police officers shall have one year
from the date of their hire to come into compliance with this section. (Ord.
No. 2014-1, 2-10-14)

Sec. 2-29   Allocation Basis For Economic Development Funds.
   a.   Insofar as any State or Federal statute, rule; or regulation does not
mandate the system of allocating tax exempt status to Economic Development
Facility projects which have been the subject of inducement resolutions after
the date of this ordinance and to the extent that any future State or Federal
Statute, rule or regulation shall limit the overall amount of Economic
Development Facility financings which the Town may issue and to the further
extent to which any project shall consume a portion of such allocation and the
overall amount of projects induced during such period exceeds such allocations,
then the following criteria shall be applied in determining the allocation
thereof.
   b.   The projects for the duration of any one allocation period shall be
divided into four (4) categories as follows:
      1.   This category shall have first allocation priority.
      2.   This category shall be allocated funds after all projects in
allocation A have been funded.
      3.   This category shall be allocated funds after all projects in
allocation B have been funded.
      4.   This category shall be allocated funds after all other projects have
been funded.
   The allocation determinations shall be good only for the allocation period
in which the project was induced, after such period has expired the project if
it has not been closed will compete again for allocation in the next allocation
period. The category rank is to be assigned to each project at the time of
inducement and each applicant must agree in writing to abide by the terms of
this Ordinance.
   c.   The classification of projects into the four (4) categories is to be
determined by reference to a point system derived as follows as indicated
hereafter. For the purpose of determining the amount of employment to be
generated for purpose of determining the eligibility for the award of points,
the projected level of employment at the end of the third year of operations
will be used.
   d.   Criteria:
      1.   Facility is to be the main home office of the company or is the
expansion of an applicant which already has its home office in the Town (3
points).
      2.   Amount to be induced has a ratio to number of jobs of not more than
five thousand dollars ($5,000.00) per job created or retained (5 points) of not
more than ten thousand dollars ($10,000.00) per job created or retained (3
points).
      3.   The overall new investment of applicant in plant, facility, and
equipment which will not be subject to tax abatement is greater than 5% of the
amount of financing to be induced (4 points).
      4.   The project is to be or was instrumental to the town in obtaining
State or Federal grant funds which will assist in attracting additional
industrial projects to the Town or will assist in acquiring or constructing
public improvements of benefit to the Town beyond the location of the plant in
said Town (5 points).
      5.   The project will employ not less than 20 nor more than 200 employees
(2 points).
      6.   The project will be under construction within 90 days after
inducement and the bond issue is projected to close within 120 days and the
applicant has a commitment to purchase the bonds on agreed terms (4 points).
      7.   The applicant proposes to engage in a business which will promote
diversification in said Town (the Town reserves the right to change whether any
certain type of business promotes diversification during the course of any
allocation period and may but is not obligated to determine during the course
of any allocation period that any certain type of business will no longer be
awarded points under this criteria during that allocation period provided,
however, any such change shall not affect any point award already made during
that allocation period) (5 points).
      8.   The applicant has agreed to make substantial contributions toward
public improvements needed by the Town for the benefit of others in addition to
the applicant (5 points).
      9.   The applicant has agreed to landscape the facility site in a manner
which will enhance the general surrounding area which agreement is referenced
by the application letter (5 points).
      10.   The proposed facility is to be located within the corporate
boundaries of the Town or the Company has requested annexation and annexation
is legally and economically feasible (5 points).
   e.   Category rankings to be as follows:
      1.   Class A - pts. or better ......................28
      2.   Class B - pts. or better ......................20
      3.   Class C - pts. or better ......................15
      4.   Class D - pts. or less .........................14
   f.   Any induced project which is not substantially constructed and the bond
issue is not closed within nine months of the date of inducement is to be
penalized by subtraction of five (5) points from the points assigned at
inducement and will have its category reduced if appropriate.
   g.   Allocation amongst projects within the same category are to be made on
a first to close basis; if more than one bond issue closes on the same date
within the same category, then the allocation shall be made upon a first to
have been induced basis. (Ord. No. 84-1, 3-2-834)
Sec. 2-30 Region III - A Development and Planning Commission.
   a.   The Region III - A Development and Planning Commission is empowered to
provide community development technical assistance to the Town of Ashley at the
Town's request.
   b.   The Commission serves as the liaison to and provides technical
assistance between the Town Board of Trustees and the Indiana Department of
Commerce with respect to Small Cities Community development Block Grant
Programs.
   c.   The Town of Ashley desires to have the Commission serve as its liaison
with the Indiana Department of Commerce and to continue to provide technical
assistance since it began rendering service in 1975 to the Community. (Res. No.
82-5, 5-10-82)

obligations and privileges authorized under I. C. 36-7-14-1 et seq., and I.C.

amended.
   b.    The town hereby accepts all the obligations and responsibilities set
forth according to said statute.
   c.   The Ashley Redevelopment Commission shall annually report at the first
regularly scheduled meeting in January of each year to the Town Council. (Ord.
No. 98-01, 2-9-98)

Sec. 2-34   Fire Department.
   a.   Section
2-51 of this Code addresses the Firefighter's Fund.
   b.   Guidelines for Disciplinary Interface between the Town of Ashley, Town
Council and the Town of Ashley Fire Department.
      1.   All members of the Town of Ashley Fire Department shall have
independent personnel files maintained at the Clerk-Treasurer's office.
      2.   A copy of documentation regarding any and all disciplinary actions
for any member of the Town of Ashley Fire Department shall be promptly
forwarded to the Clerk-Treasurer of the Town of Ashley for inclusion in the
Clerk-Treasurer's personnel file.
      3.   The Town Council of the Town of Ashley shall approve all major
disciplinary actions regarding members of the Town of Ashley Fire Department.
      4.   Major disciplinary actions shall include incidents involving the
following:
         a)   Any action that could be classified as a potential misdemeanor;
and
         b)   Any action that could be classified as a potential felony; and
         c)   Any accident involving a vehicle owned by the Town of Ashley; and
         d)   Any traffic offense or violation involving a vehicle owned by the
Town of Ashley; and
         e)   Any operation of vehicles and/or equipment owned by the Town of
Ashley while under the influence of alcohol and/or drugs; and
         f)   Any unauthorized use of vehicles or equipment owned by the Town
of Ashley.
      5.   Disciplinary proceedings involving all other types of activities
shall be defined as minor disciplinary activities, and shall be administered by
the officers of the Ashley Fire Department. The officers of the Ashley Fire
Department shall also provide a copy of documentation regarding such minor
disciplinary activity to the Clerk-Treasurer of the Town of Ashley. (Res. No.
06-99, §§ 1 - 5, 6-14-99)

Sec. 2-42   Storm Water Management Department.
   a.   Indiana Code, § 8-1.5-5-1 is hereby adopted addressing the matter of
storm water management. Indiana Code, § 8-1.5-5-1 et seq., and all amendments
thereto are operative as to the Town of Ashley.
   b.   Pursuant to Indiana Code, § 8-1.5-5-1, a Department of Storm Water
Management is hereby created for the purpose of providing for the collection,
disposal and drainage of the storm and surface water of the Town of Ashley.
Pursuant to Indiana Code, § 8-1.5-5-4, the Storm Water Management Department,
as established hereunder, shall consist of a Board of three (3) directors,
appointed by, and serving at the pleasure of the Town Council of the Town of
Ashley. Members of the Board are not entitled to a salary for serving upon such
Board, but they are entitled to reimbursement for necessary expenses incurred
by the Board member in the performance of official duties. The Storm Water
Management Department Board shall have the authority to exercise those powers
as set forth in Indiana Code, § 8-1.5-5-1 et seq.
   c.   The terms of the individual directors of the Storm Water Management
Department shall be staggered. The term of the first director shall end on
December 31, 2003; the term of the second director shall end on December 31,
2004; and the term of the third director shall end on December 31, 2005. All
successor terms will be for three (3) years, with no more than two (2)
directors from the same political party serving at the same time. Directors may
be removed at any time by the Town Council of the Town of Ashley when, in the
judgment of the Town Council, such removal is in the best interests of the
Storm Water Management Department.
   d.   Pursuant to Indiana Code, § 8-1.5-5-5 a special taxing district for the
purpose of providing for the collection and disposal of storm and surface water
of the district in a manner that protects the public health and welfare and for
the purpose of levying special benefit taxes for the purpose of storm water
collection and disposal.
   e.   The territory of the Storm Water Management Department and the special
taxing district established hereunder shall be and is all of the territory now
or hereafter included within the corporate limits of the Town of Ashley.
   f.   The acquisition, construction, installation, operation and maintenance
of facilities and land for the storm water system may be financed through the
proceeds of special taxing district bonds of the storm water district; the
assumption of liability incurred to construct the storm water system being
acquired; service rates; revenue bonds; or any other available funds. The
Board, after approval by the Town Council of the Town of Ashley, may assess and
collect user fees from all of the property of the storm water district for the
operation and maintenance of the storm water system. (Ord. No. 2002-06, §§ 1-6,
6-10-02)
Sec. 2-43   Local Planning Team.
   a.   A Local Planning Team is hereby established and appointed as required
by the Wellhead Protection Plan.
   b.   A  Local Planning Team, as established hereunder, shall consist of
three (3) or more members, appointed by, and serving at the pleasure of the
Town Council of the Town of Ashley. Members of the Local Planning Team are not
entitled to a salary for serving upon such team, but are entitled to
reimbursement for necessary expenses incurred by the team member in the
performance of official duties.
   c.   The terms of the individual Local Planning Team members shall be
staggered. The term of the first team member shall end on December 31, 2003;
the term of the second team member shall end on December 31, 2004; the term of
the third team member shall end on December 31, 2005; and the term of the
fourth team member shall end on December 31, 2006. All successor terms will be
for three (3) years. Team members may be removed at any time by the Town
Council of the Town of Ashley when, in the judgment of the Town Council, such
removal is in the best interests of the Local Planning Team or the Wellhead
Protection Plan. (Res. No. 06-2002, §§ 1-3, 5-13-02)
Sec. 2-44   Fire Department Advisory Board.
   a.   There is created an Ashley Fire Department Advisory Board.
   b.   The Board will consist of three members approved by the Town Council,
and each member shall serve a two year term.
   c.   The Advisory Board shall consider and respond to all issues as
periodically requested by the Town Council. (Res. No. 02-2012, 2-13-12)

ARTICLE 5. FUNDS ESTABLISHED.
Sec. 2-46   Cumulative Capital Improvement Fund. 18
   a.   In accordance with the requirements of applicable State law, there is
created a special fund to be known as the Cumulative Improvement Fund of the
Town of Ashley, into which the cigarette taxes allotted to the Town of Ashley
shall be deposited.
   b.   The fund shall be a cumulative fund and all monies deposited into
improvements as hereinafter defined and none of such monies shall revert to the
general fund or be used for any purpose other than capital improvements.
   c.   The term "capital improvements" means the construction or improvement
of any property owned by the Town of Ashley, Indiana, including but not limited
to street, thorough-fares, and sewers, and the retirement of general obligation
bonds of the said Town of Ashley issued, and the proceeds used for, the purpose
of construction capital improvements. The term "capital improvements" shall not
include salaries of any public officials or employees except those which are
directly chargeable to a capital improvement. (Ord. Nb. 65-9. §§ 1, 2, 7-19-65)
 
Notes
18 I.C., § 36-9-16-1, et seq., addresses cumulative capital improvement funds.

Sec. 2-50   Cumulative Capital Development Fund.
   a.   There is re-established an Ashley Cumulative Capital Development Fund.
(Ord No. 86-7, § 1, 7-14-1986; Ord. No. 88-4A, § 1, 7-11-88; Ord. No. 89-11, §
1, 9-11-89; Ord. No. 92-11, § 1, 10-12-92; Ord. No. 95-09, § 1, 8-14-95)
   b.   An ad valorem property tax levy will be imposed and the revenues from
the levy will be retained in the Ashley Cumulative Capital Development Fund.
(Ord. No. 86-7, § 2, 7-14-86; Ord. No. 88-4A, § 2, 7-11-88; Ord. No. 89-11, §
2, 9-11-89; Ord. No. 92-11, §2, 10-12-92; Ord. No. 95-09, §2, 8-14-95)
   c.   The maximum rate of levy under Subsection (b) will not exceed
      1.   . 15 per $100 Assessed Valuation for 1996.
      2.   .15 per $100 Assessed Valuation for 1997.
      3.   .15 per $100 Assessed Valuation for 1998. (Ord. No. 95-09, § 3,8-14-
95)
   d.   The Ashley Cumulative Capital Development Fund is re-established for
the years 1996, 1997, and 1998. (Ord. No. 95-09, § 4, 8-14-95)
   e.   The funds accumulated in Ashley Cumulative Capital Development Fund
will be used for capital improvements, fireflghting building, equipment, police
radio, and general improvement fund as described in /. C, § 38-8-14 and /. C. §
36-9-17. (Ord. No. 88-4A, § 4, 7-11-88; Ord. No. 89-11, § 4, 9-11-89; Ord. No.
95-09, § 5, 8-14-95)
   f.   Notwithstanding Subsection V, funds accumulated in the Ashley
Cumulative Capital Development Fund may be spent for purposes other than the
purposes stated in Subsection 'd\ if the purpose is to protect the public
health, welfare or safety in an emergency situation which demands immediate
action. Money may be spent under the authority of this section only after the
Town Board (now Town Council) issues a declaration that the public health,
welfare or safety is in immediate danger that requires the expenditure of money
in the fund. (Ord. No. 88-4A, § 6, 7-11-88; Ord. No. 89-11, § 5, 9-11-89; Ord.
No. 95-09, § 6, 8-14-95)
   g.   This fund takes effect upon approval of the State Board of Tax
Commissioners. (Ord. No. 88-4A, § 6, 7-11-88; Ord. No. 89-11, § 6,9-11-89; Ord.
No. 95-09, §7, 8-14-95)

   (c)   The Accident Report Fund shall be dissolved and all funds contained in
the fund shall be diverted into the Law Enforcement Continuing Education Fund.
(Ord. No. 93-10, §3, 10-11-93) 19
   (d)   The Fire Arms Training Fund shall be dissolved and all funds contained
in the fund shall be diverted into the Law Enforcement Continuing Education
Fund. (Ord. No. 93-10, § 4, 10-11-93)

Sec. 2-55.8   ARP Fund.
   1.   There is created a new fund within the Clerk-Treasurer’s Office that
should be entitled “ARP Grant Fund,” and the Clerk-Treasurer has issued a fund
number of 176 with respect to these funds and which funds shall be non-
reverting.
   2.   The purpose of the funds is to be used for only the following reasons
as set forth in § 603(C) of the ARP in accordance with U.S. Treasury guidance:
      A.   To respond to the public health emergency with respect to the
Coronavirus Disease 2019 (COVID-19) or its negative economic impacts, including
assistance to households, small businesses, and nonprofits, or to aid the
impacted industries such as tourism, travel and hospitality;
      B.   To respond to workers performing essential work during the COVID-19
public health emergency by providing premium pay to eligible works of the
metropolitan city, non-entitlement unit of local government or county that are
performing such essential, or by providing grants to eligible employers that
eligible workers who perform essential work;
      C.   For the provision of government services to the extent of the
reduction in revenue of such metropolitan city, non-entitlement unit of local
government, or county due to the COVID-19 public health emergency relative to
revenues collected in the most recent full fiscal year of the metropolitan
city, non-entitlement unit of local government or county prior to the
emergency; or
      D.   To make necessary investments in water, sewer or broadband
infrastructure as approved by the U.S. Treasury.
   3.   The funds shall be appropriated by the Town’s fiscal body (the Town
Council) before use.
   4.   All expenditure of funds shall be approved by the Town Council with any
and all claims to be paid from the Town’s ARP Fund.
   5.   The Town Council will establish the plan, conditions and rules upon
which the funds are to be requested and used.
   6.   Any unused funds shall be paid back to the United States Treasury when
required.
   7.   The Clerk-Treasurer shall keep accurate and complete financial records
of the receipt and expenditure of any and all funds deposited and paid from
this new Fund.
   8.   No money received in the ARP Fund shall be used for any type of deposit
into any pension fund.
(Ord. 2021 02, 6-14-21)
Sec. 2-55.9   MVH Restricted Fund.
   1.   There is created a new fund within the Clerk-Treasurer’s Office that
shall be entitled “MVH Restricted Fund,” and the Clerk-Treasurer has issued a
fund number of 2203 with respect to these funds.
   2.   The purpose of the funds is to allocate more than fifty percent (50%)
of the distribution from the MVH Account to the MVH Restricted Fund as outlined
in I.C. Code 8-14-1-4(b) and I.C. Code 8-14-1-5 for distribution to be used for
construction, reconstruction, and preservation of the unit’s highways.
   3.   Funds received in the distributions for 2021 will be transfer from the
MVH Fund to the new MVH Restricted Fund in the amount of $21,000.
   4.   The funds shall be appropriated by the Town’s fiscal body (the Town
Council) before use.
   5.   All expenditure of funds shall be approved by the Town Council and any
and all claims to paid from the MVH Restricted Fund.
   6.   The Clerk-Treasurer shall keep accurate and complete financial records
of the receipt and expenditure of any and all funds deposited and paid from
this new Fund.
(Res. 01-2022, 4-11-22)
ARTICLE 6. TOWN MEMBERSHIPS AND INTERLOCAL COOPERATION.

   (a)   The Town Council is authorized to budget and appropriate funds to
provide memberships for the Town of Ashley, its elected and appointed
officials, and its boards, departments, or agencies in local, regional, state,
and national associations of a civic, educational, or governmental nature which
have as their purpose the betterment and improvement of municipal operations.
   (b)   The Town Council is authorized to budget and appropriate funds to pay
the expenses of duly authorized representatives to attend the meetings and
functions of organizations to which the Town belongs.

ARTICLE 7. VIOLATIONS COLLECTION BUREAU.
Sec. 2-59   Creation of Ordinance Violations Bureau.
   There shall be created an Ordinance Violations Bureau for the Town of
Ashley. (Ord. No. 96-14, § 1, 12-30-96)
Sec. 2-60   Clerk-Treasurer Designated Violations Clerk.
   The Clerk-Treasurer of the Town of Ashley, or his or her designee, is the
Violations Clerk and shall be empowered to administer the Violations Bureau.
(Ord. No. 88-06, § 1, 9-12-88; Am. Ord. No. 96-14, § 1, 12-30-96)
Sec. 2-61   Payment of Fines.
   The Clerk-Treasurer, or his or her designee, shall accept written
appearances, waivers of trial, admissions of violation and payment of civil
penalties of not more than fifty dollars ($50.00). (Ord. No. 90-03, § 1, 5-14-
90; Am. Ord. No. 96-14, § 2, 12-30-96)
Sec. 2-62   Fee and Fine Schedule.
   a.   The Town Council of the Town of Ashley adopts the recommendation of the
Plan Commission of the Town of Ashley in relation to adopting a consistent fee
and fine schedule for violations of zoning ordinances, and further establishes
a consistent fee and fine schedule for all other ordinance violations.
   b.   Violations of ordinances with Schedule A fines shall be assessed a fine
of seventy-five dollars ($75.00) for the first day and one hundred fifty
dollars ($150.00) for each subsequent day the violation continues, which shall
constitute a separate violation.
   c.   Violations of ordinances with Schedule B fines shall be assessed a fine
of two hundred fifty dollars ($250.00) for the first day and four hundred
dollars ($400.00) for each subsequent day the violation continues, which shall
constitute a separate violation.
   d.   Violations of ordinances with Schedule C fines shall be assessed a fine
of five hundred dollars ($500.00) for the first day and seven hundred fifty
dollars ($750.00) for each subsequent day the violation continues, which shall
constitute a separate violation.
   e.   Violations of ordinances with Schedule E fines shall be assessed a fine
of one thousand dollars ($1,000.00) for the first day and two thousand five
hundred dollars ($2,500.00) for each subsequent day the violation continues,
which shall constitute a separate violation.
(Ord. No. 90-03, § 2, 5-14-90; Am. Ord. No. 96-14, § 3, 12-30-96; Am. Ord. No.
2006-13, §§ 1 - 5, 10-9-06)
Sec. 2-63   Waiver of Court Costs.
   All ordinance violations subject to this procedure are not to have Court
costs fees imposed even if the Town has to enforce the ordinance by proceeding
in Court. (Ord. No. 88-06, § 4, 9-12-88)
Sec. 2-64   Proceeds to be Deposited in General Fund.
   Proceeds from the Violations Bureau shall be placed into the General Fund of
the Town of Ashley, Indiana, unless otherwise designated within the specific
ordinance subject to this article. (Ord. No. 96-14, § 4, 12-30-96)
Sec. 2-65   through Sec. 2-69 Reserved for Future Use.
ARTICLE 8. FIRE HALL LEASING PROCEDURES.
Sec. 2-70   Terms.
   Any individuals or organizations using the Fire Hall shall hereinafter be
referred to as the Lessee and the Town shall hereinafter be referred to as the
Lessor. (Res. No. 11-2001, § 1, 7-16-01)
Sec. 2-71   Document Required.
   The Lessee shall execute such documents as required by the lessor to
establish an understanding of the parties. (Res. No. 11-2001, § 2, 7-16-01)
Sec. 2-72   Security Deposit; Rental Fee.
   The Lessee shall, upon requesting the use of the Fire Hall, provide payment
of a security deposit in the amount of $50.00. The rate to rent the Fire Hall
shall be $75.00 per day. (Res. No. 11-2001, § 3, 7-16-01; Res. No. 04-2015, 12-
14-15)
Sec. 2-73   Times for Leasing the Fire Hall.
   The Lessee shall use the Fire Hall at only those times designated by the
Lessor.
(Res. No. 11-2001, § 4, 7-16-01)
Sec. 2-74   Responsibilities of Lessees.
   The lessee shall be responsible for cleaning the Fire Hall and returning the
Hall to the same condition in which it was received. Failure to do so will
result in a $25.00 per hour cleaning charge to be paid from the deposit, and
further collection if necessary. (Res. No. 11-2001, § 5, 7-16-01)
Sec. 2-75   Damage or Loss Requirements.
   The Lessee shall be responsible for any and all loss or damage to the Fire
Hall or items located in the Fire Hall during lessee's use of the same. (Res.
No. 11-2001, § 6, 7-16-01)
Sec. 2-76   Gratuities.
   The Lessee may donate the security deposit, or any portion thereof, to the
Lessor as a gratuity for the use of the Fire Hall. (Res. No. 11-2001, § 7, 7-
16-01)
Sec. 2-77   Rights of Lessor.
   The Lessor reserves the right to make determinations as to the parties to
whom the Lessor shall Lease the premises. (Res. No. 11-2001, § 8, 7-16-01)
Sec. 2-78 through Sec. 2-84 Reserved for Future Use.
ARTICLE 9. PERSONNEL AND EMPLOYMENT POLICIES.
Sec. 2-85   Introduction.
   a.   The Town of Ashley Town Council has developed this Article for
establishment of employment procedures. This Article is also intended to
educate the Town's full-time, part-time and volunteer work force regarding the
Town's standards and expectations for said individuals. This Article is
designed to acquaint the reader with the Town rather than to give all the
answers and cover all the possible situations and circumstances of one's
employment.
   b.   This Article is subject to change on an ongoing basis. It is not
intended to establish a contractual relationship between the Town and the
Town's full-time, part-time and volunteer employees. Said employees are
considered at-will employees. (Ord. No. 2000-20, 12-21-00)
Sec. 2-86   General Provisions.
   a.   When the words “employee” or “employees” are used within this Article,
they are intended to be inclusive of Town full-time employees, part-time
employees, volunteers, superintendents, department heads, reserve law
enforcement officers, fire department personnel and law enforcement officers.
   b.   Full-time employees shall be defined as working a minimum of forty (40)
hours per week.
   c.   Employees are expected to understand that they are public servants, and
are to reflect a positive image of the Town in their attitude and comments
regarding the Town, its businesses and citizens. They are in addition expected
to cooperate with each other in providing for and carrying out their respective
responsibilities for serving the public. (Ord. No. 2000-20, 12-21-00)
Sec. 2-87   Organizational Chart.
[https://export.amlegal.com/media/6fea84ce56dab1c3435c9a832097f5a73c1e2c26/
IMAGES/0-0-0-1158.jpg]
 
(Ord. No. 2000-20, 12-21-00; Res. No. 15-2001, 10-8-01)
Sec. 2-88   Employment Procedure.
   a.    The Department Head hiring an employee shall request approval from the
Town Superintendent and the Town Council prior to adding any position or prior
to replacing an employee.
   b.   The Town Clerk-Treasurer shall advertise availability of the position.
However, then current employees may be used to fill a position without
advertisement.
   c.   Applications shall be accepted for a designated time as determined by
the Town Council.
   d.   Applicants shall complete a form for employment designated by the Town
Clerk-Treasurer. The Clerk-Treasurer shall receive completed applications and
shall in turn deliver them to the Town Superintendent and appropriate
Department Head.
   e.   The Town Superintendent and Department Head shall review said
applications, and shall schedule and conduct interviews, as they deem
appropriate. Results of the initial evaluation and interviews shall be then
forwarded by the Town Superintendent and Department Head to the Town Council.
   f.   The Town Council shall review all information as to prospective
employees and may conduct additional interviews as they deem appropriate or
accept any recommendations of the Town Superintendent and Department Head. The
Town Council shall extend offers of employment contingent upon negative drug
and alcohol screening.
   g.   The Town Clerk-Treasurer shall schedule drug and alcohol screening in
keeping with the current drug-testing policy. The Town Clerk-Treasurer shall
notify the applicant of test results. Should test results be negative the Town
Clerk-Treasurer shall notify the applicant of the initial date of employment.
(Ord. No. 2000-20, 12-21-00)
Sec. 2-89   Equal Employment Opportunity.
   The Town is committed to a policy of equal employment opportunity. The Town
will recruit, select, promote, train, compensate and discipline individuals in
full compliance with applicable laws prohibiting discrimination based on race,
color, religion, national origin, age, sex, marital status, veteran status or
disability in an effort to provide fair and equal treatment to all employees
and job applicants. (Ord. No. 2000-20, 12-21-00)
Sec. 2-90   Time Sheets.
   a.   To ensure an orderly and punctual delivery of payroll, time sheets
shall be maintained by all employees on a form provided by the Town Clerk-
Treasurer. Time sheets shall be used to monitor the hours of work performed by
all employees.
   b.   Time sheets shall be completed daily, and delivered by Town employees
on the Town's first working day of every week, no later than 8:30 a.m. Delivery
of the time sheets shall be to the Town Superintendent, and in the absence of
the Town Superintendent, time sheets shall be delivered to the Town Clerk-
Treasurer.
   c.   Should employees attend the weekly 6:30 a.m. meeting, time sheets shall
be delivered to the Town Superintendent at said meeting in lieu of the 8:30
a.m. instruction set forth at paragraph (b) above.
   d.   Should employees be on a scheduled vacation at time of time sheet being
due, said time sheet shall be completed by said employee(s) in advance of
vacation.
   e.   Failure to comply with the requirements of this section may jeopardize
a punctual delivery to the employee of their payroll check by the Town Clerk-
Treasurer. (Ord. No. 2000-20, 12-21-00)
Sec. 2-91   Drug and Alcohol Policy.
   a.   Purpose. It is the policy of Town that its employees be free of illegal
substance and alcohol abuse. Consequently, the use of illegal drugs by
employees is prohibited. Further, employees shall not use alcohol or engage in
prohibited conduct as defined herein. The overall goal of this policy is to
ensure a drug-free and alcohol-free environment and to reduce accidents,
injuries, and fatalities.
   b.   Consequences of Policy Violation. Any employee who becomes unqualified
or engages in prohibited conduct as the same is defined herein, is subject to
immediate termination from employment. The Town Council may, at its discretion,
and at the request of the employee, keep the employee's position open while
such employee receives treatment for alcohol or illegal substance abuse and/or
addiction. Said treatment plan shall be approved in advance by the Town
Council. The Town Council may also take action against the employee up to and
including termination.
   c.   Prohibited Conduct. The following shall be considered "prohibited
conduct" for purposes of this policy:
      1.   No employee shall report for duty or remain on duty while having an
alcohol concentration of .04 or greater.
      2.   No employee shall be on duty or operate a motor vehicle while the
employee possesses alcohol.
      3.   No employee shall manufacture, distribute, dispense or possess a
controlled substance at the workplace.
      4.   No employee shall use alcohol while performing safety-sensitive
functions.
      5.   No employee shall perform safety-sensitive functions within four (4)
hours after using alcohol.
      6.   No employee required to take a post-accident drug or alcohol test
shall use alcohol for eight (8) hours following the accident or until he or she
undergoes a post-accident drug or alcohol test, whichever occurs first.
      7.   No employee shall refuse to submit to a post-accident, random,
reasonable suspicion, return-to-duty, or follow-up alcohol or drug test.
      8.   No employee shall report for duty or remain on duty when the
employee uses any controlled substance, except when use is pursuant to the
instructions of a physician who has advised the employee that the substance
does not adversely affect the employee.
   d.   Refusal to Test. Refusal to submit to the types of drug and alcohol
tests employed by the Town will be grounds for refusal to hire employee/
applicants and to terminate employment of existing employees. A refusal to test
is defined as conduct that would obstruct the proper administration of a test.
Refusing to sign step 2 of the alcohol form is considered a refusal to test. A
delay in providing a urine, breath or saliva specimen could be considered a
refusal. If an employee cannot provide a sufficient quantity of urine or
breath, a physician of the Town's choice will evaluate him. If the physician
cannot find a legitimate medical explanation for the inability to provide a
specimen (either breath or urine), it will be considered a refusal to test. In
that circumstance the employee has violated one of the prohibitions of the
regulations.
   e.   Types of Tests. The Town has implemented six (6) circumstances for drug
and alcohol testing;
      1.   Pre-employment;
      2.   Post-accident testing;
      3.   Random testing;
      4.   Reasonable suspicion testing;
      5.   Return-to-duty testing; and
      6.   Follow-up testing.
   f.   Pre-Employment Testing. All applicants for driving positions must
submit to urine drug tests and breath alcohol tests.
   g.   Random Testing.
      1.   The Town conducts random drug and alcohol testing. The Town or its
agents will submit all employees' names to random selection system. The random
selection system provides an equal chance for each employee to be selected each
time random selection occurs. Random selections will be reasonably spread
throughout the year. The Town will select, at a minimum, 25 percent (25%) of
the average number of employees in each calendar year for random testing.
Random selection, by its very nature, may result in employees being selected in
successive selections or more than once a calendar year. Alternatively, some
employees may not be selected in a calendar year.
      2.   If an employee is selected at random, for either drug or alcohol
testing, a Town official will notify the employee. Once notified, every action
the employee takes must lead to a collection. If the employee engages in
conduct that does not lead to a collection as soon as possible after
notification, such conduct may be considered refusal to test.
   h.   Post-Accident Testing.
      1.   The employee must submit to drug and alcohol testing any time he or
she is involved in an accident . Following any accident, the employee must
contact the Town Superintendent, Clerk- Treasurer or Town Council President as
soon as possible. The employee shall then follow the instructions of the Town
representative contacted.
      2.   Any time a post-accident drug or alcohol test is required, it must
be performed as soon as possible following the accident. If no alcohol test can
be made within eight (8) hours, attempts to perform an alcohol test shall
cease. If no urine collection can be obtained for purposes of post-accident
drug testing within thirty-two (32) hours, attempts to make such collection
shall cease.
      3.   In the event that federal, state, or local officials conduct breath
or blood tests for the use of alcohol and/or urine tests for the use of
controlled substances following an accident, these tests may meet the
requirements of this section, provided the tests conform to applicable federal,
state, or local requirements. The Town may request testing documentation from
such agencies, and may ask the employee to sign a release allowing the Town to
obtain such tests results.
      4.   In the event an employee is so seriously injured that the employee
cannot provide a sample of urine, breath or saliva at the time of the accident,
the employee must provide necessary authorization for the Town to obtain
hospital records or other documents that would indicate the presence of
controlled substances or alcohol in the employee's system at the time of the
accident.
   i.   Reasonable Suspicion Testing. Reasonable suspicion for requiring a
employee to submit to drug and/or alcohol testing shall be deemed to exist when
an employee manifests physical or behavioral symptoms or reactions commonly
attributed to the use of controlled substances or alcohol. Such employee
conduct must be witnessed by at least one (1) supervisor. Should a supervisor
observe such symptoms or reaction, the employee must submit to testing.
   j   Authorization for Previous Test Records. The Town may obtain certain
drug and alcohol testing records from employee's previous employers for the
previous two (2) years. The Town will verify that no prior employer of the
employee has records indicating a violation of any rule pertaining to
controlled substance or alcohol use within the previous two (2) years. As a
condition of employment, the employee shall provide the Town with a written
authorization for all previous employers within the past two (2) years to
release such drug and alcohol testing records as the regulations require.
   k.   Drug Urinalysis.
      1.   Drug testing will be performed through urinalysis. Urinalysis will
test for the presence of drugs and/or metabolites of the following controlled
substances, including but not limited to:
         (a)   Marijuana;
         (b)   Cocaine;
         (c)   Opiates;
         (d)   Amphetamines; and
         (e)   Phencyclidine (PCP).
      2.   The urinalysis procedure starts with the collection of a urine
specimen. Urine specimens will be submitted to a certified laboratory for
testing. The laboratory will report all laboratory results to the Town
Superintendent and the Town Clerk-Treasurer.
      3.   Individual test results for applicants and employees will be
released to the Town and will be kept strictly confidential unless consent for
the release of the test results has been obtained. Any individual who has
submitted to drug testing in compliance with this policy is entitled to receive
the results of such testing upon written request to the Town Clerk-Treasurer
within fifteen (15) days from the date of said results being delivered to the
Town.
   l.   Alcohol Tests. The Town will perform alcohol testing using a breath-
testing device or a saliva-based testing device, and may be provided through a
vendor or agent. A technician who is certified will operate the device and
trained on the specific device he or she will be operating. The employee shall
report to the alcohol-testing site as notified by the Town. The employee shall
follow all instructions given by the alcohol technician. Employees with tests
indicating a blood alcohol content (BAC) of .04 or greater are considered to
have engaged in prohibited conduct, which may result in disciplinary action up
to and including termination. (Ord. No. 2000-20, 21-21-00)
Sec. 2-92   Travel Policy.
   a   Transportation.
      1.   All travel must have the prior approval of the Town Council.
      2.   Municipally-owned vehicles are to be utilized if at all possible.
      3.   Departure times shall be approved by Department Heads in advance.
      4.   No alcoholic beverages are permitted in vehicles owned or rented on
behalf of the Town.
      5.   To be eligible for reimbursement, receipts are required for all
expenditures, including tolls and parking fees.
      6.   Personal vehicle use must have prior Town Council or Department Head
approval.
      7.   If personal vehicles are used, mileage reimbursement is $0.57 per
mile.
      8.   Mileage will be determined on point-to-point computer software
program. In the event of any mileage controversies, the software utilized by
the Town shall determine the mile reimbursement due.
      9.   All purchases or expenditures made without a supporting receipt are
the responsibility of the person making such purchase or expenditure.
   b.   Meals.
      1.   Meal reimbursement allowance is thirty dollars ($30.00) per
employee, per day. No gratuities or alcohol will be reimbursed.
      2.   Only Town employees, as defined in the employee manual, will receive
reimbursement for meals.
      3.   Reimbursement for meals will only be made for the actual amount of
purchase, or the meal allowance, whichever is less. A receipt for each meal
must be presented at time of request for reimbursement.
      4.   All purchases or expenditures made without a supporting receipt are
the responsibility of the person making such purchase or expenditure.
   c.   Accommodations.
      1.   All required overnight stays must have prior approval of the Town
Council.
      2.   The room allowance is one hundred twenty-five dollars ($125.00) per
day. If multiple resources are attending the same event, room(s) must be
shared.
      3.   The Department Heads will schedule accommodations.
      4.   No in-room movie expense will be reimbursed.
      5.   Only Town employees, as defined in the employee manual, will receive
reimbursement for room allowances.
      6.   Reimbursement for rooms will only be made for the actual amount of
the expenses or the room allowance, whichever is less. A receipt for the
accommodation expense must be presented at time of request for reimbursement.
      7.   All purchases or expenditures made without a supporting receipt are
the responsibility of the person making such purchase or expenditure.
(Ord. No. 2000-20, 12-21-00) (Am. Res. No. 09-2001, 6-11-01; Am. Res. 01-2015,
9-14-15)
Sec. 2-93   Gratuities and Tips.
   The receipt of gratuities and gifts is not permitted by Town employees. An
exception to this policy would include advertising material with nominal value
(i.e. hats, pens and the like) and edible items for employee group enjoyment
(i.e. cookies, candy, nuts and the like). Should an employee be offered a
gratuity or tips not permitted herein, or have a question as to the
appropriateness of a gratuity or tip, said employee should graciously refuse
the same.
(Ord. No. 2000-20, 12-21-00)
Sec. 2-94   Time Away From Work Place.
   a.   The provisions of this section with respect to sick leave, funeral
leave, vacation leave, personal leave, holiday leave and jury duty apply
exclusively to full-time employees.
   b.   The Clerk-Treasurer shall maintain a system for tracking employees days
of absence due to sick leave, funeral leave, vacation time, personal leave,
holiday leave and jury duty. In the event that a dispute arises as to time away
from work place, the Clerk-Treasurer's records shall be deemed to be accurate
and official.
   c.   Except for police officers, all sick leave, funeral leave, vacation
leave, personal leave, holiday leave and jury duty leave shall be paid based
upon an eight (8) hour work day for all employees, regardless of the number of
hours for which they are scheduled or are regularly scheduled. Should an
employee work a partial day, said employee shall receive payment for the number
of hours actually worked and shall receive sick, funeral, vacation, personal,
holiday or jury duty pay, if available, for the difference between the time
worked and an (8) hour work day. No overtime pay shall be earned for instances
of leave.
Police officers shall be paid based upon an eight and one-half (8.5) hour day
for all sick leave, funeral leave, vacation leave, personal leave, holiday
leave and jury duty leave. If a Police Department employee works a partial day,
said Police Department employee shall receive payment for the number of hours
actually worked and shall receive sick, funeral, vacation, personal, holiday or
jury duty pay, if available, for the difference between the time worked and an
eight and one-half (8.5) hour work day. No additional overtime pay shall be
earned for instances of leave.
   d.   Lunch Break. All non-police officers are permitted to have a one-half
(.5) hour unpaid lunch break during periods of time that they are scheduled to
work more than five (5) hours in one (1) day.
All police officers are permitted to have a one-half (.5) hour paid lunch break
during periods of time that they are scheduled to work more than five (5) hours
in one (1) day. Said pay shall be made to police officers as they shall be “on-
call” during said lunch break.
   e.   Sick Leave.
      1.   Sick leave is to be used for employee absence due to employee
illness.
      2.   In no event shall sick leave be permitted until the Town has
employed an individual for a period of six (6) continuous months. Employees
shall be entitled to receive (6) six days of sick leave per calendar year. The
beginning of the calendar year marks the time the (6) six days are established
for sick leave. Sick leave received by a new employee shall be pro-rated for
the month of the year in which the six-month probationary period ends.
      3.   In order to receive sick leave pay an employee is required to call
the Department Head no later than 8:30 a.m. every day an employee is sick. In
the absence of the Department Head the employee shall report sickness to the
Town Superintendent no later than 8:30 a.m. In the absence of the Town
Superintendent the employee shall report sickness to Town Clerk-Treasurer no
later than 8:30 a.m. The Department Head or Town Superintendent shall provide a
written report to the Town Clerk-Treasurer of the sickness.
      4.   Should an employee be sick more than two (2) consecutive days, a
Medical Doctor's written verification of the illness and medical requirement to
miss work shall be delivered to the Clerk-Treasurer immediately upon the
employee's return to work in order to receive sick leave pay.
