ARTICLE 1. GENERAL POWERS.
Sec. 6-1   Town Authority to Regulate.
   A Town may regulate, conduct or use or possession of property which might
endanger the public health, safety, or welfare of its citizens.
Sec. 6-2   Sounds and Emissions into the Air. 2
   A Town may regulate the generation of sounds and the introduction of any
substance or odor into the air.
 
Notes
2 2   I.C., § 36-8-2-8, authorizes a Town to regulate sounds and substances into the
  air.
Sec. 6-3   Control Over Animals. 3
   A Town may regulate the control of animals, and may establish animal
shelters.
 
Notes
3 3   I.C., § 36-8-2-6, authorizes a unit to control animals, and to establish,
  operate, and maintain animal shelters.
Sec. 6-4   through Sec. 6-6 Reserved for Future Use.
ARTICLE 2. FAIR HOUSING.
Sec. 6-7   Policy.
   It is the policy of the Town of Ashley to provide, within constitutional
limitation, for fair housing throughout the town. (Res. 1-97, § 1, 4-14-97)
Sec. 6-8   Definitions.
   a.   "Dwelling" means any building, structure, or portion thereof which is
occupied as, or designed or intended for occupancy as, a residence by one or
more families, and any vacant land which is offered for sale or lease for the
construction or location thereon of any such building, structure, or portion
thereof.
   b.   "Family" includes a single individual.
   c.   "Person" includes one or more individuals, corporations, partnerships
associations, labor organizations, legal representatives, mutual companies,
joint-stock companies, trusts, unincorporated organizations, trustees, trustees
in bankruptcy, receivers, and fiduciaries.
   d.   "To rent" includes to lease, to sublease, to let and otherwise to grant
for a consideration the right to occupy the premises owned by the occupant.
   e.   "Discriminatory Housing Practice" means an act that is unlawful under
Sections 4, 5, or 6, and as defined in the Fair Housing Amendments Act of 1988,
and the Title VIII of the Civil Rights Act of 1968.
Sec. 6-9   Unlawful Practice.
   Subject to the provisions of subsection (b) and section 7, the prohibitions
against discrimination in the sale or rental of housing set forth in section 3
shall apply to:
   a.   All dwellings except as exempted by subsection (b).
   b.   Nothing in section 4 shall apply to:
      1.   Any single-family house sold or rented by an owner where the private
individual owner does not own more than three such single-family houses at any
one time; provided that in the sale of such single-family house by a private
individual owner not residing in the house at the time of sale or who was not
the most recent resident of such house prior to the sale, the exemption shall
apply only to one such sale within any twenty-four month period. The private
individual owner may not own any interest in, nor have owned or reserved on his
behalf, title to or any right to all or a portion of the proceeds from the sale
or rental of any such single-family house unless such house is sold or rented.
         (a)   without the use in any manner of the sales or rental facilities
or services of any real estate broker, agent or salesman, or any person in the
business of selling or renting dwellings, or of any employee or agent of any
such broker, agent or salesman, or person and
         (b)   without the publication, posting or mailing, after notice of
advertisement or written notice in violation of section 4(c) or this
resolution, but nothing in this proviso shall prohibit the use of attorneys,
escrow agents, abstracters, title companies and other such professional
assistance as necessary to perfect or transfer this title, or
      2.   Rooms or units in dwellings containing living quarters occupied or
intended to be occupied by no more than four families living independently of
each other, if the owner actually maintains and occupies one of such living
quarters as his residence.
   c.   For the purpose of subsection (b), a person shall be deemed to be in
the business of selling or renting dwellings if he has, within the preceding
twelve months, participated as:
      1.   Principal in three or more transactions involving the sale or rental
of any dwelling or any interest therein, or
      2.   Agent, other than in the sale of his own personal residence, in
providing sales or rental facilities or services in two or more transactions
involving the sale or rental of any dwelling or any interest therein, or
      3.   The owner of any dwelling unit designed or intended for occupancy
by, or occupied by, five or more families. (Res. 1-97, §3, 4-14-97)
Sec. 6-10   Discrimination in the Sale or Rental of Housing.
   As made applicable by section 3 and except as exempted by sections 3(b) and
7, it shall be unlawful:
   a.   To refuse to negotiate for the sale or rental of, or otherwise make
unavailable, a dwelling to any person because of age, race, color, religion,
sex, national origin, disability, or families with children.
   b.   To discriminate against any person in the terms, conditions, or
privileges of sale or rental of dwelling, or in the provision of services or
facilities in connection therewith, because of age, race, color, religion, sex
national origin, disability, or families with children.
   c.   To cause to be made printed, or published any notice, statement or
advertisement, that indicates any intention to preference, limitation, or
discrimination based on age, race, color, religion, sex, national origin,
disability, or families with children.
   d.   To represent to any person because of age, race, color, religion, sex,
national origin, disability, or families with children that the dwelling is not
available for inspection, sale or rental when such dwelling is in fact so
available.
   e.   For profit, to induce or attempt to induce any person to sell or rent
any dwelling by representations regarding the entry or perspective entry into
the neighborhood of a person or persons of a particular age, race, color,
religion, sex, national origin, disability, or families with children. (Res. 1-
97, § 4, 4-14-97)
Sec. 6-11   Discrimination in the Financing of Housing.
   It shall be unlawful for any bank, building and loan association, or other
corporation, association, firm or enterprise whose business consists in whole
or part in making of commercial real estate loans, to deny a loan or other
financial assistance to a person for the purpose of purchasing, construction,
improving, repairing, or maintaining a dwelling, Such discrimination shall
include the fixing of the amount, interest rate, duration or other terms or
conditions of such loan or other financial assistance, because of the age,
race, color, religion, sex, national origin, disability, or families with
children status, or of any person associated with him in connection with the
loan or other financial assistance or the present or prospective owners,
lessees, tenants, or occupants of the dwelling or dwellings. Nothing contained
in this section shall impair the scope or effectiveness of the exception
contained in section 3(b). (Res. 1-97, § 5, 4-14-97)
Sec. 6-12   Discrimination in the Provision of Brokerage Services.
   It shall be unlawful to deny any person access to or membership or
participation in any multiple-listing service, real estate brokers
organization, or other service, organization or facility relating to the
business of selling or renting dwellings, or to discriminate against him in the
terms or conditions of such access, membership, or participation, on account of
age, race, color, religion, sex, national origin, disability, or families with
children status. (Res. 1-97, § 6, 4-14-97)
Sec. 6-13   Exemption.
   Nothing in this resolution shall prohibit a religious organization,
association, or society, or any nonprofit institution or organization operated,
supervised or controlled by or in conjunction with a religious organization,
association, or society, from limiting the sale, rental or occupancy of
dwellings which it owns or operates for other than commercial purpose to
persons of the same religion, or from giving preference to such persons, unless
membership in such religion is restricted on account of age, race, color, sex,
national origin, disability, or families with children status. Nor shall
anything in this resolution prohibit a private club no to open to the public,
which as an incident to its primary purpose or purposes provides lodgings which
it owns or operates for other than a commercial purpose, from limiting the
rental or occupancy of such lodgings to its members or from giving preference
to its members. (Res. 1-97, § 7, 4-14-97)
Sec. 6-14   Administration.
   a.   The authority and responsibility for administering this Act shall be in
the Chief Executive Officer of the Town of Ashley.
   b.   The Chief Executive Officer may delegate any of these functions duties,
and powers to employees of the Town or to boards of such employees, including
such functions, duties, and powers with respect to investigating, conciliating,
hearing, determining, ordering, certifying, reporting or otherwise acting as to
any work, business, or matter under this resolution. The Chief Executive
Officer shall by rule prescribe such rights of appeal from the decisions of his
hearing examiners to other hearing examiners or to other officer of the Town,
to boards of officers or to himself, as shall be appropriate and in accordance
with the law.
   c.   All executive departments and agencies shall administer their programs
and activities relating to housing and urban development in a manner
affirmatively to further the purposes of this resolution and shall cooperate
with the Chief Executive Officer to further such purposes. (Res. 1-97, § 8, 4-
14-97)
Sec. 6-14.1   Education and Conciliation.
   Immediately after the enactment of the resolution, the Chief Executive
Officer shall commence such educational and conciliatory activities as-will
further the purposes of this Resolution. He shall call conferences of persons
on the housing industry and other interested parties to acquaint them with the
provisions of this resolution and his suggested means of implementing it, and
shall endeavor with their advice to work out programs of voluntary compliance
and of enforcement. (Res. 1-97, § 9, 4-14-97)
Sec. 6-14.2   Enforcement.
   a.   Any person who claims to have been injured by a discriminatory housing
practice or who believes that he will be irrevocably injured by a
discriminatory housing practice that is about to occur (hereafter "person
aggrieved") may file a complaint with the Chief Executive Officer. Complaints
shall be in writing and shall contain such information and be in such form as
the Chief Executive Officer requires. Upon receipt of such a complaint, the
Chief Executive Officer shall furnish a copy of the same to the person or
persons who allegedly committed or is about to commit the alleged
discriminatory housing practice. Within thirty days after receiving a
complaint, or within thirty days after the expiration of any period of
reference under subsection (c), the Chief Executive Officer shall investigate
the complaint and give notice in writing to the person aggrieved whether he
intends to resolve it. If the Chief Executive Officer decides to resolve the
complaints, he shall proceed to try to eliminate or correct the alleged
discriminatory practice by informal methods of conference, conciliation, and
persuasion. Nothing said or done in the course of such informal endeavors may
be made public or used as evidence in a subsequent proceeding under this
resolution without the written consent of the persons concerned.
   b.   A complaint under subsection (a) shall be filed within one hundred and
eighty days after the alleged discriminatory housing practice occurred.
Complaints shall be in writing and shall state the facts upon which the
allegations of discriminatory housing practice are based. Complaints may be
reasonably and fairly amended at any time. A respondent may file an answer to
the complaint against him and with the leave of the Chief Executive Officer
which shall be granted whenever it would be reasonable and fair to do so, many
amend his answer at any time. Both complaints and answers shall be verified.
   c.   If within thirty days after a complaint is filed the Chief Executive
Officer has been unable to obtain voluntary compliance with this Resolution,
the person aggrieved may, within thirty days thereafter, file a complaint with
the Secretary of the Department of Housing and Urban Development. The Chief
Executive Officer will assist in this filing.
   d.   If the Chief Executive Officer has been unable to obtain voluntary
compliance within thirty days of the complaint, the person aggrieved may,
within thirty days thereafter, commence a civil action in any appropriate court
to enforce the rights granted or protected by this resolution. If the court
finds that a discriminatory housing practice has occurred or is about to occur,
the court may enjoin the respondent from engaging in such practice or order
such affirmative action as may be appropriate.
   e.   Wherever an action filed by an individual shall come to trial, the
Chief Executive Officer shall immediately terminate all efforts to obtain
voluntary compliance. (Res. 1-97, § 10, 4- 14-97)
Sec. 6-14.3   Investigations; Giving of Evidence.
   a.   The Chief Executive Officer shall seek to have access at all reasonable
times to premises, records, individuals and other possible sources of evidence
and may examine, record, and copy such materials and take and record the
testimony or statements of such persons as are reasonably necessary for the
furtherance of the investigation. The Chief Executive Officer may seek
subpoenas to compel his access to, or the reproduction, of such materials; the
appearance of such persons; or he may seek to issue interrogatories in the
district in which the investigation is taking place. The Chief Executive
Officer may administer oaths.
   b.   Upon written application to the courts, a respondent is entitled to
seek the issuance of a reasonable number of subpoenas if approved by the court.
   c.   In case of refusal to obey a subpoena, the Chief Executive Officer may
petition for its enforcement in the municipal or state court for the district
in which the person to whom the subpoena was addressed resides, was served, or
transacts business.
   d.   Any person who willfully fails or neglects to attend and testify or to
answer any lawful inquiry or to produce records, documents, or other evidence
if in his power to do so, in obedience to the subpoena or lawful order of the
courts, shall be fined as determined by the courts, or imprisoned as determined
by the courts, or both. Any person who, with intent to mislead the Chief
Executive Officer, shall make or cause to be made any false entry or statement
of fact in any report, account, record, or other document submitted to the
Chief Executive Officer, shall make or cause to be made any false entry or
statement of fact in any report, account, record, or other document submitted
to the Chief Executive Officer pursuant to a subpoena or other orders or shall
willfully neglect or fail to make or cause to be made full, true, and correct
entries in such reports accounts, records, or other documents, or shall
willfully mutilate. alter, or by any other means falsify any documentary
evidence, shall be fined and/or imprisoned as determined by the courts.
   e.   The Town Attorney shall conduct all litigation in which the Chief
Executive Officer participates as a party or as amicus pursuant to this
resolution. (Res. 1-97, § 11, 4-14-97)
Sec 6-14.4   Enforcement by Private Persons.
   a.   The rights granted by sections 3, 4, 5, and 6 may be enforced by civil
rights actions in State or local courts of general jurisdiction. A civil action
shall be commenced within one hundred eighty days after alleged discriminatory
housing practice occurred. The court shall continue such civil case brought
pursuant to this section or section 10(d) from time to time-before bringing it
to trial if the court believes that the conciliation efforts of the Chief
Executive Officer are likely to result in satisfactory settlement of the
discriminatory housing practice complained of and which forms the basis for the
action in court. Any sale, encumbrance, or rental consummated prior to the
issuance of any court order issued under the authority of this resolution, and
involving a bona fide purchaser, encumbrancer, or tenant without actual notice
of the existence of the filing of a complaint or civil action under the
provision of this resolution shall not be affected.
   b.   The court may grant as relief, as it deems appropriate, any permanent
or temporary injunction, temporary restraining order, or other order, and may
award to the plaintiff actual damages, to the prevailing plaintiff, provided,
that in the opinion of the court the plaintiff is not financially able to
assume said attorney's fees. (Res. 1-97, § 12, 4-14-97)
Sec 6-14.5   Interference, Coercion, or Intimidation.
   It shall be unlawful to coerce, intimidate, threaten, or interfere with any
person in the exercise or enjoyment of, or on account of his having exercised
or enjoyed, or on account of his having aided or encouraged any other person in
the exercise or enjoyment of, any right granted or protected by section 3, 4,
5, or 6. This section may be enforced by appropriate civil action. (Res. 1- 97,
§ 13, 4-14-97)
Sec. 6-14.6   Separability of Provisions.
   If any provision of this resolution or the application thereof to any person
or circumstances is held in valid, the remainder or the resolution and the
application of the provision to other persons not similarly situated or to
other circumstances shall not be affected thereby. (Res. 1-97, § 14, 4-14- 97)
Sec. 6-14.7   Prevention of Intimidation in Fair Housing Cases.
   Whoever, whether or not acting under cover of law, by force or threat of
force willfully injures, intimidates or interferes with, or attempts to injure,
intimidate or interfere with:
   a.   Any person because of his age, race, color, sex, religion, national
origin, disability, or families with children and because he is or has been
selling, purchasing, renting, financing, occupying or contraction or
negotiating for the sale, purchase, rental, financing or occupation of any
dwelling, or applying for or participating in any service, organization, or
facility relating to the business of selling or renting dwellings; or
   b.   Any person because he is or has been, or in order to intimidate such
person or any other person or any class of persons from:
      1.   participating, without discrimination on account of age, race,
color, religion, sex, national origin, disability, or families with children in
any of the activities, services, organizations or facilities described in
subsection 15(a); or
      2.   affording another person or class of persons opportunity or
protection so to participate; or
   c.   any citizen because he is or has been, or in order to discourage such
citizen or any other citizen from lawfully aiding or encouraging other persons
to participate, without discrimination on account of age, race, color, religion
sexy national origin, disability, or families with children in any of the
activities, services, organizations or facilities described in subsection 15
(a), or participating lawfully in speech or peaceful assembly opposing any
denial of the opportunity to participate shall be fined as determined by the
courts, or imprisoned as determined by the courts. (Res. 1-97, § 15, 4-14-97)
ARTICLE 3. SPECIFIC REGULATIONS.
Sec. 6-15   False Fire Alarms Prohibited.
   Any person who shall make a false alarm of fire shall be fined in any sum
not exceeding twenty-five dollars ($25.00).
Sec. 6-16   Discharge of Firearms Prohibited.
   a.   It shall be unlawful to discharge within the Town of Ashley, Indiana,
any firearms, airgun, BB gun, pellet gun, or similar weapon capable of
expelling a projectile with deadly force, or any toy gun projecting lead or
other missile, except in a regularly established shooting gallery; provided
that this Section shall not be construed to prohibit any officer of the law
from discharging a firearm in the performance of his or her duty; nor to any
citizen from discharging a firearm when lawfully defending person or property.
   b.   Any person violating this section shall be fined ten dollars ($10.00)
for each violation. (Ord. No. 66-1, §§1, 2, 8-8-66)
Sec. 6-17   Loitering and Loud and Raucous Noises Prohibited. 4
   a.   It shall be unlawful for any person to be a member of a disorderly
crowed, or any crowd gathered for an unlawful purpose, within the limits of the
Town of Ashley. (Ord. No. 74-8, § 1, 9-9-75) 5
   b.   It shall be unlawful for any person to operate loud vehicles inside the
limits of the Town of Ashley, Indiana. (Ord. No. 74-8, §2, 9-9-74; Ord. No.
2005-13, § 1, 9-12-05)
   c.   It shall be unlawful for any person to create loud noises or sounds
inside the limits of the Town of Ashley, Indiana. (Ord. No. 74-8, § 3, 9-9-74;
Ord. No. 2005-13, § 1, 9-12-05)
   d.   It shall be unlawful to disturb the peace and quietude of the Town of
Ashley, Indiana with loud noises or sounds.
      1.   Noises and sounds heard two hundred fifty feet (250') from the
source emitting such noise or sound shall be considered to be in violation of
this Section. (Ord. No. 2005-13, § 1, 9-12-05)
   e.   Any person who violates any provision of this Section shall be subject
to a Class A fine as set forth in Section
2-62. (Ord. No. 74-8, § 4, 9-9-74; Ord. No. 2005-13, § 1, 9-12-05; Am. Ord. No.
2006-18, §§1, 2, 12-11-06)
 
Notes
  4   The U.S. Supreme Court held in the case of Kovacs v. Cooper, 336 U.S. 77,
4 that "loud and raucous noises" was a phrase sufficiently definite and clear, and
  thus enforceable.
5 5   I.C., § 35-45-1-1, addresses offense against public order.
Sec. 6-18   Junk Yards Prohibited.
   a.   As used in this Section, the term "junk yard" shall include any lot,
part of lot, or parcel of land used for the storage, keeping, or abandonment of
junk, including but not limited to scrap metal, vehicles, machinery, or parts
thereof. (Ord. No. 93-08, § 1, 9-13-93)
   b.   No person shall establish or maintain or permit to be established or
maintained on premises owned, leased, or occupied by him or her within the Town
of Ashley, Indiana, any junk yard. (Ord. No. 63-6, § 2, 7-15-63, Ord. No. 93-
08, § 2, 9-13-93)
   c.   Any person who violates any provision of this Section shall be subject
to a Class B fine as set forth in Section
2-62. (Ord. No. 93-08, § 3, 9-13-93; Ord. No. 2005-09, § 1, 8-8-05; Am. Ord.
No. 2006-18, §§1, 2, 12-11-06)
   d.   The Town Marshal or his or her designee is hereby authorized by the
Town Council of the Town of Ashley, Indiana to address violations of this
Section according to the procedures set forth herein without further
authorization of the Town Council of the Town of Ashley. The Town Marshal or
his or her designee shall be authorized to cause written notice to abate to be
served upon the owner of the property in question, granting that owner a
minimum of ten (10) calendar days in which to remove the junk yard. This notice
shall be served by the Town Marshal or his or her designee, by certified mail
to the owner, or by a “notice” placard conspicuously posted on the property.
Such written notice or placard shall contain the following information:
      1.   The address of the property;
      2.   The date of the notice;
      3.   The address and telephone number of the Town Marshal; and
      4.   A warning that if the public nuisance is not removed within ten (10)
calendar days of posted notice (twelve (12) calendar days if written notice is
mailed), the Town will abate the nuisance and seek recovery of the actual costs
involved in the removal of the nuisance, and will assess fines as allowed by
this Section.
   The Town Marshall or his or her designee, after posting a notice to abate,
shall serve the owner of the property with a copy of the notice by first class
United States mail, postage prepaid. Any failure to accept or receive such
written notice or removal of such posted notice shall not constitute a defense
to any action to enforce the provisions of this Section. (Ord. No. 93-08, § 4,
9-13-93; Ord. No. 2005-09, § 1, 8-8-05)
Sec. 6-19   Curfew Regulations. 6
   a.   Curfew for Minors - No person under fifteen (15) years of age shall
remain in or upon any of the streets, alleys, or public grounds in the Town
after the hour of 11:00 p.m. and before 5:00 a.m., unless accompanied by a
parent, guardian, or other person having legal custody or control of the minor
person, or unless the child is in the performance of an errand or duty for the
parent, guardian, or other person having legal custody or control of the minor
person, or unless the employment of the minor person makes it necessary for him
to be upon the streets, alleys or public places during the prohibited hours.
(Ord. No. 88-12, § 1, 1-9-89)
   b.   Parental Responsibility:
      1.   No parent, guardian, or other person having legal custody or control
of any person under fifteen (15) years of age shall allow a minor person to go
or be in or upon any of the streets, alleys, or public places in the Town
during the prohibited hours unless there exists reasonable necessity therefore
      2.   It shall be the duty of the Town Marshal, upon the arrest of any
person described in Subsection (a) where the parents or guardians have refused
to become responsible for the violation of this Chapter by minor persons, to
inquire into the facts of such arrest and the conditions of the minor person,
and if it appears that the minor person is in want of parental care, then he
shall notify the DeKalb County or Steuben County (whichever is applicable)
Department of Public Welfare. (Ord. No. 88-12, § 2, 1-9-89)
   c.   Town Marshal to Enforce:
      The Town Marshal is authorized to arrest any person violating this
Section provided, however, that the arrested person shall not be placed in
confinement. (Ord. No. 88-12, § 3, 1-19-89)
   d.   Penalty:
      Any person violating any provision of this Section shall, upon
conviction, be fined a sum not exceeding twenty-five dollars ($25.00). (Ord.
No. 88-12, § 4, 1-19-89)
 
Notes
  6   I. C., § 31-6-4-2, addresses curfew regulations, and permits Towns to
6 advance the curfew time by not more than one (1) hour for public safety
  reasons.
Sec. 6-20   Garbage and Refuse Regulations.
   a.   It shall be unlawful for any person to dispose of any garbage, refuse,
sewage, or other waste by depositing, or permitting or suffering the same to be
deposited, on any public street or on any property whether it be private or
public which constitutes a health hazard, or which fosters the breeding or
feeding grounds of animals, rodents or insects within the Town of Ashley,
Indiana. (Ord. No. 631, § 1, 7-15-63)
   b.   Any person who violates any provision of this Section shall be subject
to a Class B fine as set forth in Section
2-62.
   c.   The Town Marshal or his or her designee is hereby authorized by the
Town Council of the Town of Ashley, Indian to address violations of this
Section according to the procedures set forth herein without further
authorization of the Town Council of the Town of Ashley. The Town Marshal or
his or her designee shall be authorized to cause written notice to abate to be
served upon the owner of the property in question, granting that owner a
minimum of five (5) calendar days in which to remove the garbage or refuse.
This notice shall be served by the Town Marshal or his or her designee, by
certified mail to the owner, or by a “notice” placard conspicuously posted on
the property. Such written notice or placard shall contain the following
information:
      1.   The address of the property;
      2.   The date of the notice;
      3.   The address and telephone number of the Town Marshal; and
      4.   A warning that if the garbage, refuse and/or health hazard is not
removed within five (5) calendar days of posted notice (seven (7) calendar days
if written notice is mailed), the Town will enter upon the land and remove the
garbage, refuse and/or health hazard, and seek recovery of the actual costs
involved in the removal thereof, in addition to fines assessed as allowed by
this Section.
   d.   The Town Marshal or his or her designee, after posting a notice to
abate, shall serve the owner of the property with a copy of the notice by first
class United States mail, postage prepaid. Any failure to accept or receive
such written notice or removal of such posted notice shall not constitute a
defense to any action to enforce the provisions of this Section.
      1.   The Town Marshal shall make a report to the Town Council setting
forth any costs of abating or removing the garbage, refuse and/or health
hazard.
      2.   The Town Council of the Town of Ashley, Indiana will determine if
and in what amount a lien should be placed upon the real estate for the costs
associated therewith. Such lien may be collected according to the laws of the
State of Indiana. (Ord. No. 63-1, § 2, 7-15-63; Ord. No. 2005-08, § 1, 8-8-05;
Am. Ord. No. 2006-18, §§ 1, 2, 12-11-06)
Sec. 6-20.1   Collection of Garbage and Refuse.
   a.   The current contract for collection of garbage and refuse within the
Town shall be continued.
   b.   New garbage and collection rate adjustments will be at a rate of $10.50
the first three years (2014-2016) and 2017 and 2018 with a maximum of 2.5%
increase each year.
(Ord. No. 2007-1, 1-8-07; Ord. No. 2007-14, 11-12-07; Am. Ord. No. 2008-06, §§
1, 2, 10-13-08; Am. Ord. No. 2009-07, §§ 1, 2, 12-14-09; Am. Ord. No. 2013-07,
§§ 1, 2, 10-14-13)
Sec. 6-21   Weeds and Noxious Plant Regulation.  7
   a.   Purpose
      The purpose of this ordinance is to promote public health, safety and
welfare by requiring owners of real property within the Town of Ashley to
control the growth of weeds and other rank vegetation. (Ord. No. 94-01, § 1, 2-
14-94)
   b.   Statutory Authority
      Indiana Code, § 36-7-10.1 et seq. is adopted by the Town of Ashley,
Indiana, as authority for the removal of weeds and rank vegetation. (Ord. No.
94-01, § 3, 2-14-94)
   c.   Application
      This ordinance applies to all real property within the Town of Ashley.
(Ord. No. 94-01, § 4, 2-14-94)
   d.   Definitions
      1.   Owner - The word Owner shall mean any one or more of the following:
         A.   The fee simple owner or owners of a parcel of real estate
including the life tenant or tenants if any; or
         B.   The record owner or owners as reflected by the most current
records in the DeKalb County Auditor's office or Steuben County Auditor's
office; or
         C.   The purchaser or purchasers of such real estate under any
contract for conditional sale thereof.
      2.   Private Property - All real estate within the Town, except
governmental property.
      3.   Governmental Property - Real Estate within the Town which is owned,
leased, controlled, or occupied by the United States, the State of Indiana, or
any political subdivision thereof.
      4.   Weeds & Vegetation
         A.   Any shrubs, bushes, grass, voluntary plants, and other vegetable
growth or vegetation either planted and not maintained, or not planted or
cultivated, except tress.
         B.   Any weeds, including but not limited to jimson, burdock, thistle,
cocklebur, ragweed, poison ivy, poison sumac, poison oak, or other poisonous
plant or other weeds or a like kind, or plants detrimental to health. (Ord. No.
94-01, § 5, 2-14-94)
         C.   Grass, plants or other rank vegetation, allowed to grow to a
height exceeding six inches (6") other than trees, bushes, flowers or other
ornamental or agricultural plants on any lot that contains an improvement or
structure. (Ord. No. 94-14, § 1, 8-8-94)
         D.   Any accumulation of dead weeds, grass or brush on private or
governmental property that has been allowed to become a health or safety
hazard. (Ord. No. 94-01, § 5, 2-14- 4)
         E.   Grass plants, or other rank vegetation, allowed to grow to a
height exceeding ten inches (10") on any lot or tract of unplatted real estate
containing no improvements or structures thereon. (Ord. No. 94-14, § 2, 8-8-94)
   e.   Public Nuisance - Weeds and/or rank vegetation permitted to grow or
remain on an owner's property in violation of this ordinance are declared to be
a public nuisance and shall be unlawful. (Ord No. 94-01, § 6, 2-14-94)
   f.   Exemptions - The following areas shall not be governed by this
ordinance:
      1.   Areas for agriculture;
      2.   Interior fields, wooded lots, the banks of streams and open drains,
areas maintained in their natural state in public parks, and outdoor nature
laboratories maintained by schools. (Ord. No. 94-01, § 7, 2-14-94)
   g.   The Ashley Town Marshal is authorized and empowered to enforce this
Section within the Town of Ashley. (Ord. No. 94-01, §8, 2-14-94; Ord. No. 2005-
11, § 1, 10-10-05)
   h.   Violations - A violation of this ordinance shall be construed as
willful or negligent failure to abide by the rules and regulations contained
within this ordinance. (Ord. No. 94-01, § 9, 2-1494)
   i.   Determination of Violation
      1.   Complaint - Violations under this chapter shall be cited by any
department of the Town which receives a complaint regarding public nuisance on
any property within the Town, and they shall forward that complaint to the Town
Marshal who, after investigation, shall notify the land owner of the violation.
   j.   Notice to Abate - When a report addresses private property the Town
Marshal shall cause a written Notice to Abate to be served upon the owner of
the property in question, granting that owner a minimum of five (5) calendar
days in which to remove the environmental nuisance. Notice, along with a copy
of this ordinance, shall be mailed regular mail (not certified) and served by a
law enforcement officer upon the owner or occupant. In the event that any such
real estate is unoccupied and the owner is a non-resident of the Town, in lieu
of the notice provided above, a written notice, accompanied by a copy of this
ordinance (via regular mail, not certified), shall be sent to the owner or
owners as they appear on the tax duplicates in the Office of the Treasurer of
either DelKalb or Steuben County, by the Town Marshal by mail to the address on
file in the Office of the County Auditor. Upon failure of the non-resident
owner to cause the public nuisance to be removed or destroyed within eight (8)
days after the mailing of the Notice, the Street Department of the Town shall
cause the public nuisance to be removed or destroyed. The same charge shall be
made therefor as provided below. Any failure to give such written notice shall
not constitute a defense to any action to enforce the provisions of this
ordinance.
      A.   Notices - All notices shall contain the following information:
         1.   The address of the property;
         2.   The date of the notice;
         3.   The address and telephone number of the Town Council;
         4.   A warning that if the environmental public nuisance is not
removed within five (5) calendar days [eight (8) calendar days for non-
residents] after notice, the Town will abate the nuisance and seek recovery;
and
         5.   A copy of this ordinance.
      B.   Inspection - Following the expiration of the Notice to Abate, the
Town Marshal shall visually inspect the property to determine whether a public
nuisance exists. If a public nuisance exists, actions shall be taken to abate
that nuisance in accordance with this ordinance.
      C.   Lien on Real Estate - It shall be the duty of the Town Marshal to
supervise the administration of this Ordinance in order to remove or cause to
be removed all weeds, grass, and plants within the corporate limits of the Town
or located on the streets, alleys, or other public places within the Town which
abut the premises. The expense provided for in this Section of the Code for
cutting and removing shall be charged to and paid by the owner or occupant of
the premises and shall constitute a lien on the premises. The Clerk-Treasurer
shall file, within fifteen (15) days of the cutting or removal by the Street
Department, a lien with the County Recorder of the charges assessed, if the
same are not paid. (Ord. No. 94-01, § 10, 2-14-94)
   k.   Penalties
      1.   Fees and Costs - Any person who violates any provision of this
Section shall be subject to a Class A fine as set forth in Section
2-62. (Ord. No. 2005-11, § 1, 10-10-05; Am. Ord. No. 2006-18, §§1, 2, 12-11-06)
      2.   Failure to Pay - If the owner fails to pay the amount within fifteen
(15) days after receiving a statement, a copy of all costs shall be filed by
the Clerk-Treasurer of the Town of Ashley in the Office of the County Recorder
for the purpose of placing the amount claimed on the tax duplicate against the
property, so that the amount claimed can be collected in the same manner as
taxes are collected, subject to the limitations above. (Ord. No. 94-01, § 11,
2-14-94)
   l.   Appeal.
      Any person accused of a violation shall have the opportunity to appeal
said accusation to the Town Council of Ashley, at a regularly scheduled
meeting. The appeal must be presented to the Clerk-Treasurer in writing at
least five (5) days prior to the meeting at which the appeal is requested.
The appealing party must appear in person or by counsel to present his/her
case. If not present, the question will be decided in his/her absence.
Notwithstanding the appealing party's right of future appeal to any court, the
determination of the Town Council shall be final. Enforcement shall abate
during the appeal procedure to the Town Council. (Ord. No. 94-01, § 12, 2-14-
94)
 
Notes
7 7   I. C., § 36-7-10-3, authorizes a Town to charge for the removal of weeds and
  rank vegetation and have the same collected as taxes.
Sec. 6-22   Burning Regulations.
   a.   Outdoor Open Fires:
      1.   No person, firm, or corporation shall kindle or maintain any
bonfire, rubbish fire or other outdoor fire of any type, other than a cooking
fire, within the Town of Ashley, effective January 1, 2008.
      2.   Any outdoor open fire in the Town shall be done so only pursuant to
a permit issued by the Town Marshal, or his or her designee; the Town Marshal
or his or her designee shall take into consideration the health, safety and
welfare of the citizens of the Town, the location of the fire, the material to
be burned and any other such things as the Town Marshal may deem appropriate in
considering issuance of the permit.
      3.   The fee for burn permits shall be five dollars ($5.00), or as
hereafter amended.
   b.   Enforcement
      1.   The Police Department shall enforce this Section. Notification of a
fire being maintained in violation of this Section shall be made first by oral
notification by the Town of Ashley Officer, and require the party maintaining
the fire to douse the same immediately. The police officer shall then mail to
the violator a written notification, delivered by ordinary, first-class United
States Mail, and providing information as to the penalty being imposed and
collection pursuant to Section c. herein.
   c.   Penalties
      1.   Any person who violates any provision of this Section shall, upon
determination of violation of this Section, be fined in a sum not less than
twenty-five dollars ($25.00) and not exceeding five hundred dollars ($500.00).
Each time the violation continues or reoccurs shall constitute a separate
offense. (Ord. No. 94-12, §1, 9-12-94; Ord. No. 2001-12, § 1, 10-8-01; Ord. No.
2003-08, § 1, 12-17-03; Ord. No. 2007-05, § 2, 3, 5-14-07)
Sec. 6-23   Fireworks Regulations. 8
   a.   It shall be unlawful within the Town of Ashley to ignite any type of
firework or firework product that has been deemed by the Indiana State Fire
Marshall Association to be illegal for use within the State of Indiana. (Ord.
No. 99-08, § 1, 11-8-99)
   b.   Any person found to be violating this Section by igniting an illegal
firework shall be fined fifty dollars ($50.00) for each ignition. As an
additional penalty for violation of this Section, law enforcement officials
shall seize any and all illegal fireworks. (Ord. No. 99-08, § 2, 11-8-99)
   c.   Should the person or persons found to be in violation of this Section
by igniting such illegal fireworks be a minor child, said minor child's parents
or guardians shall be responsible for payment of such fines associated with the
violation hereof. (Ord. No. 99-08, § 3, 11-8-99)
   d.   Consumer Fireworks
      1.   Definition: Consumer Fireworks - A small firework that is designed
primarily to produce visible or audible effects by combustion, and that is
required to comply with the construction, chemical composition, and labeling
regulations promulgated by the United States Consumer Product Safety Commission
under 16 CFR 1507. The term also includes some small devices designed to
produce an audible effect, such as whistling devices, ground devices containing
fifty (50) milligrams or less of explosive composition, and aerial devices
containing one hundred thirty (130) milligrams or less of explosive
composition. Propelling and expelling charges consisting of a mixture of
charcoal sulfur, and potassium nitrate are not considered to be designed to
produce and audible effect. Consumer fireworks include:
         A.   Aerial devices, which include, but are not limited to: sky
rockets, missile type rockets, helicopter or aerial spinners, roman candles,
mines and shells;
         B.   Ground audible devices, which include, but are not limited to:
firecrackers, salutes and chasers; and
         C.   Firework devices containing combinations of the effects described
in divisions (A) and (B) above.
         D.   Consumer Fireworks do not include the following fireworks as
referenced in I.C. 22-11-4-8(a):
            1.   Dipped sticks or wire sparklers, however, the total
pyrotechnic composition may not exceed one hundred (100) grams per item; and,
devices containing chlorate or per chlorate salts may not exceed five (5) grams
per item;
            2.   Cylindrical fountains;
            3.   Cone fountains;
            4.   Illuminating torches;
            5.   Wheels;
            6.   Ground spinners;
            7.   Flitter sparklers;
            8.   Snakes or glow worms;
            9.   Smoke devices; and
            10.   Trick noisemakers that include party poppers, booby traps,
snappers, trick matches, cigarette loads and auto burglar alarms.
      2.   Use of Consumer Fireworks - No person within the corporate
boundaries of the Town of Ashley shall use, ignite or discharge or permit to be
used, ignited or discharged any type of consumer fireworks on any day or time
other than the following:
         A.   June 29th through July 9th between the hours of 4:00 p.m. and
midnight;
         B.   December 31st and January 1st between the hours of 4:00 p.m. and
1:00 a.m.
      3.   Enforcement - The town of Ashley Town Marshal, and his or her
designee, shall be charged with enforcing the provisions of this ordinance.
      4.   Penalty - Any person, firm or corporation violating the terms of
this ordinance commits a Class A infraction as established by Ordinance No.
2006-09.
      5.   The Town of Ashley may permit fireworks displays on occasion by
occasion basis for events including, but not limited to fall festivals and 4th
of July events and that these events are dissimilar from consumer fireworks
permitted by this ordinance. Other displays of fireworks shall be regulated and
keeping with both the Indiana Code of Ordinances and the Indiana Commission
Code and are not affected by this Ordinance. (Ord. No. 2008-04, 8-11-08)
 
Notes
8 8   I.C., §§ 22-11-14-1 through 22-11-14-9, sets forth Regulations of
  Fireworks by the Fire Marshal.
Sec. 6-24   Snow Removal Regulations.
   No person shall allow any snow and/or ice to accumulate higher than four (4)
feet near an intersection or street, which by such accumulation constitutes an
obstruction to traffic and visibility thereby causing a traffic hazard.
Sec. 6-25   Abandoned or Junked Vehicles Prohibited. 9
   a.   The Town Council of the Town of Ashley, Indiana finds that abandoned
vehicles are public vehicles, and are a public nuisance, and a health and
safety hazard.
   b.   The Town Council adopts by reference, as if set forth verbatim, I.C., §
9-22-1 et seq. as it presently exists and is hereafter amended.
   c.   The Town Marshal is designated as the local agent given the
responsibility for removal, storage and disposal of abandoned vehicles to the
extent permitted under I.C., § 9-22-1 et seq. as it presently exists and is
hereafter amended.
   d.   The maximum charge allowed for towing of abandoned vehicles under this
Section shall be one hundred dollars ($100.00); the maximum charge for storage
of abandonment vehicles shall be twenty-five dollars ($25.00) per day.
   e.   Any person who shall maintain, continue or establish a public nuisance
with abandoned or junked vehicles shall be fined the sum of fifty dollars
($50.00).
   f.   Each day such nuisance(s) occur(s) or continue(s) shall be deemed a
separate offense.
(Ord. No. 94-15, § 1, 8-8-94)
 
Notes
9 9   I.C., § 9-22-1 et seq., sets forth the State's abandoned vehicle law.
Sec. 6-26   Nuisances in General.
   a.   Any person who shall erect, maintain, continue, or establish any public
nuisance to the injury, annoyance, of the public health, safety, or welfare of
the citizens or the property of the Town of Ashley, shall be fined a sum not
exceeding fifty dollars ($50.00).
   b.   Each day such nuisance(s) occur(s) or continue(s) shall be deemed a
separate offense. The Town Marshal may abate such nuisances upon order of the
Town Council.
Sec. 6-27   Removal of Animal Waste.
   a.   Animal owners shall be required to immediately remove their animal's
waste when such animal waste is deposited upon property belonging to another
individual or party, including a public or municipal property or park. (Ord.
No. 2003-03, § 1, 7-14-03)
   b.   Animal owners failing to immediately remove their animal's waste shall
be subject to a Class A fine as set forth in Section
2-62. (Ord. No. 2003-03, § 2, 7-14-03; Am. Ord. No. 2006-18, §§1, 2, 12-11-06)
Sec. 6-28   Requiring Installation and Use of Appropriate Trash Receptacles
During Construction.
   a.   Property owners shall be required to install and use appropriate trash
receptacles to contain construction debris while such property is under
construction.
   b.   Any person who violates any provision of this Section shall be subject
to a Class B fine as set forth in Section
2-62.
   c.   The Town Marshal, or his or her designee, of the Town of Ashley,
Indiana shall enforce this Section. (Ord. No. 2005-05, §§ 1-3, 4-11-05; Am.
Ord. No. 2006-18, §§ 1, 2, 12-11-06)
Sec. 6-29   Synthetic Cannabinoid.
   a.   It is hereby declared to be unlawful for any person to use, possess,
purchase, attempt to purchase, sell, publicly display for sale or attempt to
sell, give, or barter any one or more of the following chemicals within the
boundaries of Ashley, Indiana:
      1.   2–[(1R, 3S)–3–hydroxycyclohexy 1] –5–92-methylopctan–2–yl) phenol {'
{'}also known as CP 47,497 and its C6, C7, C8, and C9 homologues{'}'}
      2.   (6aR, 10aR)–9–(hydroxymethyl)–6, 6–dimethyl–3–(2–methyloctan–1–
yl)–6a, 7, 10, 10a–tetrahydrobenzo [c] chromen–1–01 {'{'}also known as HU–210
{'}'}
      3.   Naphthalen–1–yl–(1–butylindol–3–yl) methanone {'{'}also known as
1–Pentyl–3– (1–naphthoyl) indol or JWH–018{'}'}
      4.   Napthalen–1–yl–(1–butylindol–3–yl) methanone {'{'}also known as
1–Buryl–3–(1–naphthoyl) indole or JWH–073{'}'}
   b.   This Section shall be enforced by the Ashley Town Marshall. If any of
the substances listed in Subsection a. herein are found in the possession of
any person, they may be confiscated and destroyed by law enforcement officials.
   c.   It is not an offense under Subsection a. herein if the person was
acting at the direction of an authorized law enforcement agent to enforce or
ensure compliance with this law prohibiting the sale of the aforementioned
substance.
   d.   This Section does not apply to any person who commits any act described
in this Section pursuant to the direction or prescription of a licensed
physician or dentist authorized to direct or prescribe such act. This Section
likewise does not apply to the inhalation of anesthesia for a medical purchase
or dental purpose.
   e.   Any business found to be in violation of this Section will be subject
to a civil fine of two thousand five hundred dollars ($2,500.00.) Any person
found in violation of this Section will be guilty of a civil fine not to exceed
one thousand dollars ($1,000.00).
   f.   The Town Attorney shall have the authority to seek an injunction to
close any business which refuses to or fails to comply with this Section.
   g.   If any provision of this Section is held invalid, such invalidity shall
not affect the remaining provisions of the Section, which shall remain
effective absent the invalid provision, and to this end, the provisions of this
Section are declared to be severable.
(Ord. No. 2010-04, 9-13-10)
Sec. 6-30   Tobacco products.
   a.   No one may use tobacco products within 30 feet of any public place as
defined in this section.
   b.   “Public place” means an enclosed area of a structure in which the
public is invited or permitted, as defined by Indiana Code 7-1.1-5-12. This
definition shall further include any pavilion in a town park, bleachers, and
dug outs in a town park, or concession stands within a town park.
   c.   Any violation of this section shall be a Class B infraction.
(Ord. No. 2012-04, 6-11-12)
Sec. 6-31 through Sec. 6-35 Reserved for Future Use.
ARTICLE 4. ANIMAL CONTROL REGULATIONS.
Sec. 6-36   Vicious, Dangerous or Ferocious Animals.
   No person shall bring into the Town of Ashley, Indiana, or keep within the
Town of Ashley, any vicious, dangerous, or ferocious animal or any animal sick
with hydrophobia or liable to communicate a contagious or infectious disease.
(Ord. No. 94-09, § 1, 3-14-94; Ord. No. 2000-06, § 1, 6-12-00)
Sec. 6-37   Animal Noises.
   No person owning or having possession of any animal shall permit such animal
to disturb the peace and quiet of any neighborhood within the Town of Ashley by
barking or emitting other loud noises. (Ord. No. 94-09, § 2, 3-14-94; Ord. No.
2000-06, § 2, 6-12-00)
Sec. 6-38   Impounding Animals - Fees.
   No person owning or having possession of any animal shall permit such animal
to run at large within the Town of Ashley, Indiana. The Town Marshal and his or
her designees shall have the authority to impound any animal found running at
large within the Town of Ashley, Indiana. The Humane Shelter shall take
possession of all impounded animals that do not have identification. The owner
of any animal in possession of the Humane Shelter shall be responsible for
payment of any costs assessed by the Humane Shelter. (Ord. No. 94-09, § 3, 3-
14-94; Ord. No. 2000-06, § 3, 6-12-00)
Sec. 6-39   Penalty.
   Any person who violates any provision of Sections
6-36 through
6-40 shall be subject to a Class B fine as set forth in Section
2-62. (Ord. No. 94-09, § 4, 3-14-94; Ord. No. 2000-06, § 4, 6-12-00; Am. Ord.
No. 2006-18, §§1, 2, 12-11-06)
Sec. 6-40   Authority of Town Marshal.
   The Town Marshal and his or her designees shall have the authority to
destroy a vicious, dangerous, or ferocious animal on sight if said animal is
attacking the Officer or other persons. The Town Marshal and his or her
designees shall have the authority to have a vicious, dangerous, or ferocious
animal destroyed if said animal attacks or kills another domestic animal. (Ord.
No. 2000-06, § 5, 6-12-00)
Sec. 6-41   Prohibiting the Keeping and Maintenance of Certain Animals Within
the Corporate Limits of the Town.
   a.   The keeping and maintenance of any rabbits, wild animals, livestock,
cattle, horses, mules, burros, donkeys, ponies, bear, sheep, swine (including
but not limited to pigs, hogs, boars, sows and pot-bellied pigs), goats,
reptiles in excess of two (2) pounds, crocodiles and alligators of any weight
or size, poisonous creatures or insects, fowl (including but not limited to
chickens, ducks, geese and turkeys), and exotic animals (including but not
limited to large game cats from the tiger and lion family) within the corporate
limits of the Town of Ashley, Indiana is prohibited.
   b.   The Town Marshal is authorized to enforce this Section and to serve
notice of violation of this Section upon the residents of the Town of Ashley,
Indiana found to be in violation thereof.
   c.   Any person who violates any provision of Section shall be subject to a
Class A fine as set forth in Section
2-62. (Ord. No. 2004-13, §§ 2-4, 12-13-04; Am. Ord. No. 2006-18, §§1, 2, 12-11-
06)
Sec. 6-42 through Sec. 6-45 Reserved for Future Use.
ARTICLE 5. CIVIL DEFENSE, DISASTERS, EMERGENCIES. 10
 
Notes
10 10   The State's Civil Defense and Disaster Law is located at I.C., §§ 10-4-1-
   1 through 10-4-1-27.
Sec. 6-46   Title.
   This Article shall be known as the “Air Raid Ordinance” and its provision
shall be liberally construed in order to accomplish its purpose and put into
effect in the Town of Ashley, Indiana, a system and method of precaution from
the occurrence of disasters and emergencies of unprecedented size and
destructiveness resulting from man-made or natural causes. (Ord. No. 69, § 1,
8-2-43)
Sec. 6-47   Definitions. 11
   a.   The term “Air Raid Period”, when used in this Article, shall mean that
interval of time between the sounding of a public “Air Raid Warning” signal and
the sounding of a public “All Clear” signal;
   b.   The term "Blackout" when used in this Article, shall mean that interval
of night time occurring within a period designated by an order of the Chief of
Police;
   c.   The term "Air Raid Warning", when used in this Article, shall mean a
public signal indicating the danger of immediate disaster or emergency, which
shall consist of the display of a hooded red light or lights at the point or
points designated by the Chief of Police, provided that such red light or
lights are not so displayed as to be visible from operating aircraft and shall
conform with all military regulations; such signal may be sounded by the use of
a siren and shall consist of the sounding of distinct blasts of fifteen (15)
seconds each, to be repeated at four (4) minute intervals.
   d.   The term "All Clear" when used in this Article, shall mean the public
signal indicating that immediate danger of the disaster or emergency has
passed, and a fifteen (15) second blast of the siren.
   e.   The word "Person", when used in this Article, shall include every
individual, person, partnership, corporation, company, association, or any
other group or combination acting as a unit.
   f.   The term "Emergency", when used in this Article, shall mean that period
of time between any proclamation of the Town Council President, or in his
absence, any member of the Town Council, or if none are available, the Town
Marshal that: a) an emergency exists, and b) that such emergency has ceased to
exist.
   g.   The terms "Town Council" and "Chief of Police", when used in this
Article, shall mean the Town Council and Chief of Police of the Town of Ashley,
Indiana.
   h.   The term "Air Raid Warden", when used in this Article, shall mean any
person officially appointed and designated as such by the Chief of Police,
subject to the approval of the Town Council, and while wearing the official Air
Raid Warden insignia or uniform. When utilized in this Article, the term "Air
Raid Warden" shall also mean and comprehend any Deputy Air Raid Warden
officially appointed by the appointing authority of said Town. Such Air Raid
Wardens shall serve without pay and shall not be considered employees of the
Town of Ashley, Indiana.
   i.   The term "Auxiliary Fireman", when used in this Article, shall mean any
person officially appointed and designated as such by the same authority which
has the power to appoint and control the regular members of the Fire Department
of this Town, and while wearing the official Auxiliary Fireman's insignia or
uniform, such Auxiliary Fireman shall serve without pay and shall not be
considered employees of the Town of Ashley, Indiana.
   j.   The term "Auxiliary Policeman", when used in this Article, shall mean
any person officially appointed and designated as such by the same authority
which has the power to appoint and control the regular members of the Police
Department of this Town, and while wearing the official Auxiliary Policeman
insignia or uniform. Such Auxiliary Policemen shall serve without pay and shall
not be considered employees of the Town of Ashley, Indiana. (Ord No. 69, § 2,8-
2-43)
 
Notes
11 11   I.C., § 10-4-1-3, addresses the definitions of the State's Civil Defense and
   Disaster Law.
Sec. 6-48   Publication of Authorized Signals.
   "Air Raid Warning" and "All Clear" public signals shall be deemed to have
been described and proclaimed when a copy of said description and proclamation
has been published once by posting copies with the Town Clerk-Treasurer of the
Town of Ashley, Indiana. (Ord. No. 69, § 3, 8-2-43)
Sec. 6-49   Rules and Regulations for Conduct of Persons during Emer-gencies.
2
   a.   The Town Marshal, subject to the approval of the Town Council, is
authorized, directed and empowered to prepare and promulgate such rules and
regulations and revisions, and amend-ments thereof, as may, in his discretion,
be necessary for the conduct of persons during "declared emergencies".
   b.   Said rules and regulations shall include rules and regulations
governing traffic movements of emergency and other vehicles and persons,
evacuation of persons, congregation of persons on the public streets and
sidewalks and in public places or buildings, but this enumeration shall not be
taken as a limitation on the power to promulgate orders, rules and regulations
governing any other subject, persons or property which must be regulated in
order to insure the proper execution of any duly authorized protection measure,
   c.   Practice blackouts and practice air raid drills may be carried out at
such times and for such purposes as the Town Marshal, with the approval of the
Town Council, shall deem necessary and appropriate, subject, always, to the
regulations of the County Civil Defense Advisory Council, and the County Civil
Defense organization.
   d.   The Town Marshal, subject to the approval of the Town Council, may
appoint auxiliary police to take the place of any now serving in case of
absentees at the time of an emergency.
   e.   All persons appointed pursuant to this Article shall serve without
compensation and shall not be considered employees of the Town of Ashley,
Indiana, and may be dismissed from service by the appointing authority without
any hearing whatsoever.
   f.   The failure of any person to obey the lawful order of any peace
officer, fireman, auxiliary fireman, auxiliary policeman, disaster workers, air
raid warden, or member of the Indiana State Guard, given in order to enforce
any of the provisions of this Article, shall be a violation thereof. (Ord No.
69, § 4, 8-2-43)
 
Notes
2   I.C., § 10-4-1-10, addresses County and Local civil defense organizations
  and their powers.
Sec. 6-50   Display of Lights during "Blackout" Prohibited.
   During a "Blackout", it shall be unlawful, except as otherwise specified
under the rules and regulations adopted as provided in Section
6-49 for any person:
   a.   To cause, display, operate, maintain or permit any lights whatever,
except within an opaque enclosed structure.
   b.   To cause, maintain or permit any reflection or leaks of light from any
structure.
   c.   To fail to prevent the display, operation, maintenance, reflection or
leakage of light from premises occupied, supervised or controlled by such
person. (Ord. No. 69, § 5, 8-2-43)
Sec. 6-51   Prohibited Lighting during Emergency.
   For the duration of an emergency, it shall be unlawful to display the
following types of illumination:
   a.   Any decorative street lighting.
   b.   Illuminated house numbers, except when under the immediate manual
control of some responsible person over the age of eighteen (18) years.
   c.   Any type of exterior flood lighting that projects light upward.
   d.   All billboard lighting or exterior building lighting, including outline
lighting, unless such light or lighting is at all times under immediate control
of some responsible person over the age of eighteen (18) years.
   e.   All exterior illuminated signs, all interior illuminated signs visible
from the exterior, whether in a private home, commercial establishment or any
other structure, which are not at all times under immediate manual control of
some responsible person over the age of eighteen (18) years.
   f.   No person shall leave a light on or burning in or upon any structure
during the daytime, which during the night time will not be under the immediate
manual control of some responsible person over the age of eighteen (18) years.
   Provided further, that additional restrictions may be placed on lights and
illuminations by rule or regulation adopted and published as provided in
Section 6-74. (Ord No. 69, § 6,8-2-43)
Sec. 6-52   Unlawful Lights a Nuisance - Abatement.
   Any light displayed contrary to the provisions of this Article, or any
violation of the rules and regulations proclaimed in Section
6-49, constitutes a public nuisance and the same may be summarily abated by any
fireman, auxiliary fireman, peace officer, auxiliary policeman, officer or
member of the Indiana State Guard, or air raid warden using reasonable force,
if necessary, for the purpose of abating such nuisance by the extinguishment or
obscuring of such light. Any entry made for the purpose of abating,
extinguishing or obscuring such nuisance must be reported by the person making
such entry to the Chief of Police for such purpose within a reasonable time,
but in no case later than twenty-four (24) hours after such entry. (Ord No. 69,
§ 7, 8-2-43)
Sec. 6-53   Regulation of Vehicles.
   a.   From the time any official air raid signal is given continuously until
the official all clear signal is given thereafter, only the following types of
traffic shall be permitted to move:
      1.   Vehicles of the Armed Forces of the United States of America;
      2.   Ambulances, police and fire vehicles, and vehicles being officially
used by the several branches of the civilian defense administration, including
air raid wardens, demolition squads, and bomb removal squads actually in
emergency service, and vehicles controlled or operated by the Post Office
Department of the government of the United States of America when actually in
use in transporting or enroute to transport the United States mails;
      3.   Vehicles actually in emergency service for the repair or control of
public utility equipment, whether privately or publicly owned;
      4.   Vehicles under the actual control of officers or enlisted men of the
Indiana State Guard and actually in official or emergency service, or actually
enroute to reporting for official or emergency duties;
      5.   Such other vehicles as may be permitted to move on special order of
the Town Marshal or military authorities.
   b.   Vehicles described in this section V and 'b* of the preceding paragraph
shall be deemed emergency vehicles and as such shall have general right of way
over all other traffic, except that ambulances, police and fire vehicles shall
have the right of way over other emergency vehicles.
   All vehicles in emergency use not already visibly remarked as such shall be
lettered on the front, sides, and back with the letter "E" painted in white to
a height of not less than one (1) foot.
   c.   Operators of all other vehicular traffic shall:
      1.   Immediately draw to the side of the road or street and stop in such
a manner and in such a place as not to obstruct the reasonable use of the road
or street, or any intersecting road or street, fire hydrant, or police or fire
station driveway, or other emergency driveway (during the period of such air
raid alarm, parking regulations pertaining to lights, time limits, loading
zones, distance from intersections and parking in prohibited zones shall be
suspended except insofar as their violation constitute a violation of this
Article);
      2.   Extinguish all lights;
      3.   Lock the ignition of such vehicle, but shall not, in any case, lock
the doors of such
vehicle;
      4.   Set the hand brake of such vehicles;
      5.   In case of horse drawn vehicles, immediately halter the horse or
horses thereof firmly and securely to a fixed object, if one is available, and
if none is available, to the vehicle itself, after unhitching said horse.
   d.   Nothing in this Article contained shaU operate to limit the authority
of any police officer, fireman, auxiliary fireman, auxiliary policeman, air
raid warden, or other duly authorized officer to prescribe the place and manner
of the parking or storage of such vehicle or vehicles, in which event operators
of vehicles shall immediately comply with the lawful directions of such officer
or officers.
   e.   During blackouts, no person, firm or corporation shall operate any
vehicle upon the public streets or highways which is not equipped with lights
so shielded as to prevent said lights or the reflections thereof from being
visible at such altitude as may be prescribed by the United States Army.
   f.   Operations of vehicles moving during blackouts shall observe the
following rules and regulations:
      1.   No person shall drive or operate a vehicle at a speed in excess of
twenty (20) miles per hour, nor in a manner so as to endanger the life, limb or
property of any person;
      2.   Operators shall obey and conform to all officially placed traffic
signs, signals and markings, whether the same be of a permanent, emergency, or
temporary nature;
      3.   Where special routes have been officially established, operators
shall conform to such route designations both as to direction and type of
vehicles;
      4.   Where speed of less than twenty (20) miles per hour are designated
by official signs or markers or by directions of a police officer or other
authorized officer, operators shall not drive vehicles in excess of such
lowered speeds;
      5.   No operator of a vehicle shall drive to the left of the center line
of the roadway except in cases where the right hand side roadway is impassable
and then only in such manner as not to endanger other traffic then and there
only in such manner as not to endanger other traffic then and there lawfully
upon such roadway;
      6.   No operator of a vehicle shall pass any other vehicle proceeding in
the same direction and shall not drive within a distance of fifty (50) feet
from the vehicle immediately ahead proceed-ing in the same direction, except in
cases where the pavement is of sufficient width to accommo-date more than a
single lane of travel in the same direction and where the operator of such
following vehicle is in another lane than that in which he is overtaking;
      7.   Any operator of a vehicle may elect to operate at a speed of less
than fifteen (15) miles per hour, but when operating his vehicle at such
reduced speed, he shall, upon signal from the vehicle which may be immediately
following, turn over to the extreme right hand side of the roadway, stop, and
allow the vehicle following to pass on his left;
      8.   No operator of a vehicle shall turn said vehicle around on any
roadway so as to proceed in the direction from whence he came;
      9.   During blackouts, no person afoot shall cross or attempt to cross
any roadway at any place other than an established crosswalk except in
compliance with the directions of an official sign or marking, or under the
direction of a police officer or other authorized officer;
      10.   At all established crosswalks where traffic is not controlled by a
police officer or other authorized officer,
      11.   At all established crosswalks where traffic is not controlled by a
police officer or other authorized officer or by any official sign or signal,
pedestrians shall come to a stop before entering upon the street or roadway;
      12.   In cases where pedestrians overhead crossing or tunnels have been
provided, pedestrians shall use said overhead crossing instead of crossing on
pavement;
      13.   No domestic animals shall be allowed to roam or graze upon the
right of way of any public street or highway during blackouts.
   g.   Nothing in this Article shall be construed so as to regulate traffic
upon the public street and roadways at time other than during air raids,
blackouts and declared emergencies. Under all other conditions, laws and
ordinances now in force or hereinafter enacted shall remain in force and be
effective. During the period of air raids, blackouts, and declared emergencies,
all matters with reference to the control and regulation of traffic which are
not specifically legislated upon herein shall be governed by other prevailing
laws and ordinances which are now and may hereafter be effective,
   h.   The fact that special rules and regulations with reference to the
operation of vehicles are prescribed in this Article shall not operate as a
limitation on the power of fee Town Marshal, with the approval of the Town
Council, to prescribe additional rules and regulations with regard to
operations of vehicles from time to time as may be necessary, and the violation
of any such additional rules and regulations shall be deemed to be a violation
of this Article. (Ord. No. 69, § 8, 8-2-43)
Sec. 6-54   Unauthorized Interference with Public Forbidden.
   It shall be unlawful for any person, other than a fireman, disaster persons,
auxiliary firemen, peace officer, auxiliary policemen, air raid warden, or
member of the Indiana State Guard, or member of the Armed Forces of the United
States of America when acting under order of a superior officer, to control or
attempt to control traffic on the city streets, or to in any way molest or
interfere with any other person during an air raid, blackout period or declared
emergency. (Ord. No. 69, §9, 8-2-43)
Sec. 6-55   Unauthorized Warning or All Clear Signals Prohibited.
   Any unauthorized person who shall operate a siren, bell, whistle or other
device so as to stimulate a blackout signal, air raid, or declared emergency,
or the termination of a blackout or air raid, or declared emergency shall be
deemed guilty of a violation of this Article and shall be subject to the
penalties imposed herein. (Ord. No. 69, § 10,8-2-43)
Sec. 6-56   No Unnecessary Noise.
   It shall be unlawful for any person to create or directly cause to be
created or to assist in creating any unnecessary or confusing noises, or to
create any disturbances or in any manner create a state of confusion during a
blackout, air raid period, or declared emergency. (Ord. No. 69, § 11, 8-2-43)
Sec. 6-57   No Municipal or Private Liability.
   This Article is an exercise by the Town of Ashley, of its governmental
function for the protection of the public peace, health and safety, and neither
the Town of Ashley, the agent, officers or representatives of the Town, or any
air raid warden, auxiliary fireman, auxiliary policeman, or any peace officer
or any member of the Indiana State Guard, or other authorized volunteer, or any
individual, receiver, firm, partnership, corporation, association, or trustee,
or any of the agents thereof, in good faith carrying out, complying with, or
attempting to comply with this ordinance, or with any order, rule or regulation
promulgated pursuant to the provisions of this Article, shall be liable for any
damage sustained to person or property as the result of said activity. (Ord.
No. 69, § 12, 8-2-43)
Sec. 6-58   Conflicting Ordinances, Order, Rules and Regulations Suspended.
   At all times when the orders, rules and regulations made and promulgated
pursuant to this Article shall be in effect, they shall supersede all existing
ordinances, orders, rules and regulations insofar the latter may be
inconsistent therewith. (Ord. No. 69, § 13,8-2-43)
Sec. 6-59   No Conflict with State or Federal Statutes.
   This shall not be construed so as to conflict with any State of Federal
statute, or with any military or naval order, rule or regulations. Any
provision of this Article which may conflict witn Indiana Code, § 10-4-1-1, et
seq., as it may be amended from time to time shall be void with the State Law
provision prevailing. (Ord No. 69, § 14, 8-2-43)
Sec. 6-60   Penalties for Violation.
   Any person, firm, or corporation violating any of the provisions of this
Article or any order, rule or regulation issued pursuant thereto shall be
deemed guilty of an ordinance violation and shall be find a sum not exceeding
three hundred dollars ($300.00). (Ord No. 69, § 15, 8-2-43)
Sec. 6-61    Coordination of Effort.
   It shall be the duty of the Town Marshal and the Town Council to confer
with, arid when possible, to act in concert with the Director of the Civilian
Defense Council of Steuben and DeKalb Counties, Indiana, and with the Sheriffs
of said counties and state, to the end that all methods of precaution against
enemy air attack, all blackouts, and declared emergencies in the Town of
Ashley, Indiana may be uniformly executed It is enacted that the public policy
of the Town of Ashley, Indiana shall be to adopt the recommendations of the
Indiana Defense Council. The insignia adopted by the Office of Civilian Defense
are adopted as the official insignia to be utilized by trie emergency and
auxiliary forces or services serving the Town under the provisions of this or
any regulations adopted hereafter. (Ord. No. 69, § 16,8-2-43)
Sec. 6-62 through Sec. 6-65 Reserved for Future Use.
