Sec. 6-66   Adoption by Reference.
   a.   Indiana Code § 36-7-9, “Unsafe Building Law”, is adopted as part of the
town of Ashley Code of Ordinances, the same as if set out in full herein.
   b.   the enforcement authority for the town shall be the Town of Ashley
Planning Department.
   c.   The hearing authority for the ordinance codified herein shall be the
duly elected Town Council.
   d.   The definition of “substantial property interest” as found at I.C. 36-
7-9-2 is adopted as part of this section. (Ord. No. 2013-05, 9-9-13)
Sec. 6-67 through Sec. 6-79 Reserved for Future Use.
ARTICLE 7. Litter in Public Places.
Sec. 6-80   Litter in Public Places.
   No person, while a driver or passenger in a vehicle, shall throw or deposit
litter upon any street or other public place or upon private property within
the Town. (Ord. No. 90-06, § 1,8-13-90)
Sec. 6-81   Truck Loads Causing Litter.
   No person shall drive or move any truck or other vehicle within the Town
unless the vehicle is so constructed or loaded as to prevent any load,
contents, or litter from being blown or deposited upon any street, alley, or
other public place. Nor shall any person drive or move any vehicle or truck
within the Town, the wheels or tires of which carry onto or deposit in any
street, alley, or other public place, mud, dirt, sticky substances, litter, or
foreign matter of any kind. (Ord. No. 90-06, § 2, 8-13-90)
Sec. 6-82   Hauling Loose Material; Debris on Street; Removal.
   Every person hauling or causing to be hauled dirt, sand, gravel, cement,
fill dirt, or loose material of any kind in or upon any street, alley,
sidewalk, or other public place shall haul it, or cause it to be hauled in
vehicles provided with tight boxes or beds so constructed or loaded as to
prevent any of the contents from falling or being thrown, blown, or deposited
upon any street, alley, sidewalk, or other public place. Any materials which
fall from, or which are thrown, blown, or deposited from any vehicle upon any
street, alley, sidewalk, or other public place, shall be removed immediately by
the person in charge of the vehicle. (Ord. No. 90-06, § 3, 8-13-90)
Sec. 6-83 Dropping Litter from Aircraft.
   No person in an aircraft shall throw out, drop or deposit within the Town
any litter, handbill, or any other object. (Ord. No. 90-06, § 4, 8-13-90)
Sec. 6-84   Sweeping Litter into Gutters Prohibited.
   No person shall sweep into or deposit in any gutter, street, or other public
place within the Town the accumulation of litter from any building or lot or
from any public or private sidewalk or driveway. Persons owning or occupying
places of business within the Town shall keep the sidewalk in front of their
business premises free of litter. (Ord. No. 90-06, § 5, 8-13-90)
Sec. 6-85   Merchants to Keep Sidewalks Free of Litter.
   No person owning or occupying a place of business shall sweep into or
deposit in any gutter, street, or other public place within the Town the
accumulation of litter from any building or lot or from any public or private
sidewalk. Persons owning or occupying places of business within the Town shall
keep the sidewalk in front of their business premises free of litter. (Ord No.
90-06, § 6, 8-13-90)
Sec. 6-86   Posting Notices Prohibited.
   No person shall post or affix a notice, poster, or other paper or device
which is calculated to attract the attention of the public, to any lamp post,
public utility pole, or shade tree, or upon any public structure or building,
except as may be authorized by law. (Ord. No. 90-06, § 7, 8-13-90)
Sec. 6-87   Litter on Private Property.
   No person shall throw or deposit litter on any occupied private property
within the Town, whether owned by that person or not, except that the owner or
person in control of private property may maintain authorized private
receptacles for collection in such a manner that litter will be prevented from
being carried or deposited by the elements upon streets, sidewalks, or other
public places, or upon any private property. (Ord. No. 90-06, § 8,8-13-90)
Sec. 6-88   Owner to Maintain Premises Free of Litter.
   The owner or person in control of any private property shall at all times
maintain the premises free of litter and outside storage However, this section
shall not prohibit the storage of litter in authorized private receptacles for
collection. (Ord. No. 90-06, § 9, 8-13-90)
Sec. 6-89   Vehicles Placed between Street and Sidewalk.
   No person shall place any finished or unfinished vehicle, equipment, or
machine in any parkway or public area between the paved surface of the street
and sidewalk, crosswalk, or private property line for any time unless it is
paved expressly for parking pursuant to prior authority granted by the Town
Council. (Ord. No. 90-06, § 10,8-13-90)
Sec. 6-90   Litter on Vacant Lots.
   No person shall throw or deposit litter on any open or vacant private
property within the Town whether owned by that person or not. (Ord. No. 90-06,
§ 11, 8-13-90)
Sec. 6-91    Clearing of Litter from Open Private Property by Town.
   a.   Notice to remove - The Marshal or any deputy is authorized and
empowered to notify the owner of any open or vacant private property within the
Town, or the agent of such owner, to properly dispose of litter located on the
owner's property, which is dangerous to public health, safety, or welfare. A
notice shall be sent by registered or certified mail, addressed to the owner at
his last known address, or the notice shall be delivered to the residence of
the owner as disclosed by the Auditor's office in DeKalb or Steuben County or
may be deposited on the premises in a conspicuous place.
   b.   Action upon noncompliance - Upon the failure, neglect, or refusal of
any owner or agent so notified to properly dispose of litter dangerous to the
public health, safety, or welfare within ten (10) days after receipt of written
notice, or within ten (10) days after the date of the notice in the event it is
returned to the Town by the U.S. Post Office Department because of its
inability to make delivery, provided the notice was the last known address of
the owner or agent, the work of disposing of the litter shall be done or caused
to be done by the Town, All authorized officers, employees, and contracting
agents of the Town are expressly authorized to enter into and upon private
property for the purpose of removing and disposing of the litter. No person
shall interfere with, hinder, or refuse to allow any person so authorized to
enter into and upon private property.
   c.   Cost constitutes lien and placing on tax duplicate - The actual cost to
the Town for removing and disposing of the litter shall be a lien in favor of
the Town against the property, and all such cost, together with any penalty
applicable thereto, shall be collected in the manner hereinafter set forth. In
all cases where the full amount due the Town is not paid to the Clerk-Treasurer
by the owner of the property within thirty (30) days after removal and disposal
of the litter, the costs shall become delinquent, and a penalty of ten percent
(10%) of the amount of the costs shall attach thereto and shall be included in
the lien and shall be collectible in addition to the cost. Whenever a
delinquency occurs for nonpayment of the cost, the Clerk-Treasurer shall file
in the appropriate County Recorder's office a notice of lien setting forth the
name or names of the owner or owners of each property on which the cost has
become delinquent and further setting forth the description of the property as
shown by the records of the appropriate County Auditor's office, the amount of
the delinquent cost, and the amount of penalty thereon. The lien shall attach
to the property described in the notice of lien from the time of the recording
of the notice of lien. The Gerk-Treasurer is further directed to certify to the
appropriate County Auditor a true copy of the notice of lien, and the amount of
the delinquent cost and penalty thereon shall be charged to the property on the
tax duplicate and shall be collected in the same manner that taxes are
collected by law. The notice of lien so filed, recorded, and certified in
accordance with the provisions hereof shall be prima facie evidence that the
provisions of this section or Chapter have been fully complied with and that
the work has been done in accordance with the provisions hereof. Such notice
shall be full notice to any person that the amount of the lien constitutes a
charge and lien against the property therein described and that the charge is
due and collectible. Upon collection of the cost and penalty, the appropriate
County Auditor or other appropriate County official shall pay over to the
Clerk-Treasurer of the Town the amount of the cost so collected, together with
one-half (½) of the penalty. He shall retain for the use and benefit of the
County the remaining one-half (½) of the penalty as a fee for the collection.
(Ord. No. 90-06, § 12, 8-13-90)
Sec. 6-92   Penalty.
   Whoever violates any of the provisions of this Article shall be fined an
amount not exceeding three hundred dollars ($300.00). Each day the violation is
committed or permitted to continue shall constitute a separate offense. (Ord.
No. 90-06, § 13, 8-13-90)
Sec. 6-93   Collection and Disposal of Brush.
   a.   Brush shall be defined as tree limbs and related tree material no
greater than four (4) inches in diameter, created by acts of God. (Ord. No.
2000-08, § 1, 8-14-00)
   b.   The Street Department of the Town of Ashley shall remove brush on the
second and fourth Wednesdays of each month beginning in April of each year and
ending in September of each year. This schedule is subject to change without
notice at the discretion of the Town Council. (Ord. No. 2000-08, § 2, 8-14-00)
   c.   Yard and garden waste, including but not limited to grass clippings,
hedge or shrubbery clippings, flowers, or other greenery, pine needles, tree
bark, corn stalks, tomato and pepper plants do not meet the definition of brush
and will not be accepted by the Town of Ashley Street Department. It shall be
the property owners' responsibility to dispose of miscellaneous yard and garden
waste, as well as tree material over four inches in diameter. (Ord. No. 2000-
08, § 3, 8-14-00)
   d.   Brush created by storm damage will be removed at the very earliest
convenience of the Town of Ashley Street Department, regardless of the regular
brush removal schedule. (Ord. No. 2000-08, § 4, 8-14-00)
   e.   Property owners shall stack all brush to be removed neatly near the
street. Brush shall not be placed in the street. All brush containing yard and/
or garden waste, or other items not meeting the definition of brush established
herein, will not be removed by the Ashley Street Department. Including these
items with brush to be removed by the Town of Ashley Street Department shall be
considered a violation of this ordinance. (Ord. No. 2000-08, § 5, 8-14-00)
   f.   Brush created by a citizen's removal of a tree shall not be removed by
the Town of Ashley Street Department. Placing brush created by tree removal for
the Town of Ashley Street Department to remove shall be considered a violation
of this ordinance. (Ord. No. 2000-08, § 6, 8-14-00)
   g.   Any person who violates any provision of this Section shall be subject
to a Class A fine as set forth in Section
2-62. It shall be the duty of the Marshal of the Town of Ashley, or his
designee, to enforce this ordinance. (Ord. No. 2000-08, § 6, 8-14-00; Am. Ord.
No. 2006-18, §§1, 2, 12-11-06)
Sec. 6-94 through Sec. 6-95 Reserved for Future Use.
ARTICLE 8. SMOKE DETECTORS IN FAMILY LIVING UNITS.
Sec. 6-96   Definitions.
   For the purposes of this Article, the following definitions shall apply:
   a.   Alarm Signal - An audible signal indicating the detection of visible or
invisible particles or products of combustion other than heat.
   b.   Authority having jurisdiction - The Ashley Fire Department shall have
enforcement responsibility for this Article.
   c.   Family Living Unit - That structure, area, room, or combination of
rooms in which a family (or individual) lives. This is meant to cover the
living area only and not common usage areas in multi-family buildings such as
corridors, lobbies, basements, etc.
   d.   Labeled - Equipment or materials to which has been attached a label,
symbol or other identifying mark or an organization acceptable to the
“authority having jurisdiction”.
   e.   Listed - Equipment or materials included in a list published by an
organization acceptable to the “authority having jurisdiction” and which
product meets appropriate standards or has been tested and found suitable for
use in a specified manner.
   f.   NFPA74 - Standard 74 of the National Fire Protection Association, which
is located in Batterymarch Park, Quincy, MD 02269.
   g.   Rental Agent - Any person, partnership or corporation who rents,
subleases, lets or otherwise grants for a consideration the right to occupy
premises not owned by the occupant. This term shall not be construed to mean a
real estate agent who is employed for the sole purpose of selling residential
units.
   h.   Sleeping areas - The area or areas of the family living unit in which
the bedrooms (or sleeping rooms) separated by other use areas, such as kitchens
or living rooms (but not bath-rooms), shall be considered sleeping areas.
   i.   Shall indicates a mandatory requirement.
   j.   Smoke Detector - Shall be defined as a device which detects visible or
invisible particles or products of combustion other than heat, as approved by
Underwriter's Laboratories, Inc. or Factory Mutual. The smoke detector shall be
equipped with a test button, and it shall produce an alarm signal upon
detection of any visible or invisible particles or products of combustion. It
may be either batter powered with a minimum 9 volt or it may be powered by a
110 volt alternating current. (Ord. No. 89-1, § 1, 4-10-89)
Sec. 6-97   Basic Requirements.
   All family living units within the corporate limits of the Town of Ashley,
Indiana, shall be equipped with a minimum of one (1) functional, properly
located, labeled and listed, smoke detector, or its equivalent or better, as
described in the NFPA74. (Ord. No. 89-1, § 2, 4-10-89)
Sec. 6-98   Installation and Location.
   a.   A minimum of one (1) smoke detector or its equivalent or better as
described in the NFPA74 shall be installed in each family living unit within
the corporate limits of the Town of Ashley, Indiana.
   b.   All smoke detectors must be installed according to the manufacturer's
instructions and subject to the approval of the “authority having
jurisdiction”.
   c.   The smoke detector shall be installed to protect the sleeping areas and
shall be located outside the bedrooms but in the immediate vicinity of the
sleeping areas, within fifteen (15) feet of all rooms used for sleeping areas.
   d.   The smoke detector shall be installed on or near the ceiling, not less
than six (6) inches from any wall, or on a wall, not less than six (6) inches
nor more than twelve (12) inches from the ceiling, and its installation shall
be subject to approval by the "authority having jurisdiction". No detector
shall be recessed into the ceiling.
   e.   All smoke detectors shall be accessible for servicing and testing.
   f.   If a smoke detector is AC powered, it must be directly attached to
junction box not controlled by any switch other than the main power supply. The
installation of AC powered detectors shall conform to all electrical standards
adopted by the Town of Ashley. A smoke detector required under this Chapter
shall be installed according to the directions and specifications of the
manufacturer, but if in conflict with any County electrical standard, the
County electrical standard shall take precedence (Ord. No. 89-1, § 3, 4-10-89)
Sec. 6-99   Maintenance.
   It shall be unlawful for any person to tamper with or remove any smoke
detector, except when it is necessary for maintenance or inspection purposes.
Any smoke detector removed for repair or replacement shall be reinstalled or
replaced so that it is operable and in place during normal sleeping hours.
   a.   Rented residential dwelling unit - Each smoke detector may be tested in
accordance with manufacturer's recommendations, but shall be tested at six (6)
month intervals in every individual residential dwelling unit, and maintained
as necessary, to ensure it is in operable condition. At any change of tenancy,
smoke detectors shall be tested and be in operable condition before the unit is
reoccupied.
   b.   Owner-occupied dwelling units - Each smoke detector may be tested in
accordance with manufacturer's recommendations, but shall be tested at six (6)
month intervals in every individual residential dwelling unit, and maintained
as necessary, to ensure it is in operable condition. (Ord No. 89-1, § 4, 4-10-
89)
Sec. 6-100   Duty of Property Owner, Manager, or Rental Agent.
   Every owner, or the manager or rental agent of such owner of any such
residential dwelling unit shall be responsible for the installation of all
smoke detectors. It is the responsibility of the tenant to maintain all such
smoke detectors provided by the owner in good working order until said tenant
vacates the premises unless said smoke detector requires AC power supply, then
the responsibility for maintaining such smoke detector shall be the
responsibility of the owner, manager or rental agent of the property. (Ord. No.
89-I, § 5, 4-10-89)
Sec. 6-101   Enforcement of Provisions.
   The Ashley Fire Department shall be charged with the duty of enforcing the
terms of this Article of the Chapter. (Ord. No. 89-1, § 6, 4-10-89)
Sec. 6-102   Violation/Penalty.
   a.   Any person, firm or corporation violating any provisions of this
Article of this Chapter, or who shall fail to comply with an order as affirmed
or modified by the authority having jurisdiction shall be subject to a fine of
fifty dollars ($50.00).
   b.   Each day such violation is permitted to continue may be deemed to
constitute a separate offense.
   c.   The violation and penalty as herein described in this Article shall not
be subject to any other fine or penalty within this Chapter. (Ord. No. 89-1, §
7, 4-10-89)
Sec. 6-103   Severability.
   The provisions of this Article of this Chapter are severable, and if any
sentence, section, or other part of this Article shall be found to be invalid,
such invalidity shall not affect the remaining provisions and the remaining
provisions shall continue to be in full force and effect. (Ord. No. 89-1, § 8,
4-10-89)

ARTICLE 1. BUILDING DEPARTMENT. 1
 
Notes
1 1   I. C., §§36-7-9-1, et seq., addresses the enforcement of building
  standards.
Sec. 7-1   Creation of Department of Buildings, Building Commissioner.
   There is established a Department of Buildings and the Office of Building
Commissioner which shall be composed of the Building Commissioner, inspectors
and such other personnel as the Town Council shall determine. (Ord. No. 79-5, §
1, 6-25-49)
Sec. 7-2   Purpose.
   The purpose of this article is to provide for the protection of life, public
safety, real and personal property, energy conservation and access for the
physically handicapped in the design and construction of buildings and
structures in Ashley, Indiana. (Ord. No. 79-5, § 2, 6-25-79)
Sec. 7-3   Compliance with Administrative Building Council.
   Hereafter, all constructions, alterations, additions, repairs, relocations,
use or occupancy of all buildings and structures shall conform with this
article and such ordinances as may be hereafter enacted for such purposes by
the Town Council of Ashley, Indiana, provided, however, that the construction,
alteration, or repair of industrialized building systems such as mobile homes
and manufactured buildings shall also conform to rules and regulations
promulgated by the Administrative Building Council applicable to such systems
(Ord. No. 79-5, § 3, 6-25-79)
Sec. 7-4   Rules, Regulations, and Codes Adopted by Reference.
   The following rules, regulations and codes are adopted by reference as the
rules and regulations governing the construction, addition, alteration, repair,
relocation and use of buildings and structures in Ashley, Indiana:
   a.   Construction Rules and Regulations, Volume I, 1978 Edition, promulgated
by the Administrative Building Council of Indiana (ABC), as it may be amended
from time to time
   b.   Electric Rules and Regulations, Volume ll, 1978 Edition, promulgated by
the Administrative Building Council of Indiana, as it may be amended from time
to time.
   c.   Plumbing Rules and Regulations, Volume III, 1976 Edition, amended 1976,
promulgated by the Administrative Building Council of Indiana, as it may be
amended from time to time.
   d.   Mechanical Rules and Regulations, Volume IV, 1977 Edition, promulgated
by the Administrative Building Council of Indiana, as it may be amended from
time to time.
   e.   The One and Two Family Dwelling Code, 1976, Edition, promulgated by the
Administrative Building Council of Indiana, as it may be amended from time to
time.
   f.   Indiana Swimming Pool Rules, 1982 Edition, 660 IAC 5-2, published
originally as 5 IR 1829 under that title.
   Two (2) copies of the foregoing rules and regulations are on file for
reference in the Ashley Town Hall and in the Steuben and DeKalb County, Court
House. (Ord. No. 79-5, § 4, 6-25-79)
Sec. 7-5   Building Commissioner.
   The Building Commissioner shall have the power to administer and enforce any
and all ordinances or codes adopted now or hereafter by the Ashley Town
Council, that regulate construction, additions, repair, alteration, relocation,
and use of building, heating, ventilation, air conditioning, electrical and
plumbing construction. (Ord. No. 79-5, § 5, 6-25-79)
Sec. 7-6   Personnel.
   For the purpose of carrying out the provisions of this article, the Ashley
Town Council may employ such personnel in the department as may be necessary.
(Ord. No. 79-5, § 6, 6-25-79)
Sec. 7-7   Administration.
   In the administration of this article, and any other ordinances incident
thereto, the Department shall cooperate with, and coordinate its activities
with, all affected or related City, County and State agencies so as to prevent
unnecessary overlapping, duplication and waste in the administrative process.
(Ord. No. 79-5, § 7, 6-25-79)
Sec. 7-8   Building Permit/Improvement Location Permit.
   a.   No construction of any building or structure or the addition,
alteration or repair thereof shall be started until the property owner or the
building contractor has applied for and obtained an Improvement Location Permit
from the Town Zoning Administrator as required by the Town Zoning Ordinance,
Sections I, 1.12 and XI 11.1. Building permits may be obtained from the DeKalb
County Building Commissioner and are separate from this Improvement Location
Permit. (Ord. No. 2002-12, 12-9-02)
   b.   Any party involved in construction, including, but not limited to
clearing, grading, excavation, and other land disturbing activities, which
requires an Improvement Location Permit shall be in compliance with 327 Indiana
Administrative Code, 15-5 et seq., and as hereafter amended. (Ord. No. 2003-02,
§ 1, 7-14-03)
Sec. 7-9   Permit Fees.
   The fee for Improvement Location Permits shall be twenty-five dollars
($25.00) for all zoning districts within the Town. Enforcement and sanctions
for violations of Section
7-8 are as established in the Town Zoning Ordinance, SectionI, 1.11
(Ord. No. 2002-12, 12-9-02)
Sec. 7-10   Appeal Procedure.
   All persons shall have the right to appeal the Building Commissioner's
decision, first through a body appointed by the Town Council, being the Ashley
Board of Appeals, and then through the executive committee of the
Administrative Building Council of Indiana, in accordance with the visions of
Indiana Code, § 22-11-1-12.5, as it may be amended from time to time. (Ord. No.
79-5, § 10, 6-25-79)
Sec. 7-11   Enforcement and Sanctions.
   It shall be unlawful and an ordinance violation for any person, firm or
corporation, whether as owner, lessee, sub-lessee, or occupant, to erect,
construct, enlarge, alter, repair, improve, remove, convert, demolish, equip,
use, occupy or maintain any building or structure, other than fences, in
Ashley, Indiana, or cause or permit the same to be done, contrary to or in
violation of the provisions of this article. (Ord. No. 79-5, § 11, 6-25-79)
Sec. 7-12   Stop Work Order.
   Whenever any work is being done in violation of the provisions of this
article or in variance with the terms of any permit issued for such work, the
Building Commissioner may order all work on the job stopped until such
violations or variance is eliminated and any work or installation made in
violation of this article corrected. Such stop order, if oral, shall be
followed by a written stop order within twenty-four (24) hours (excluding
Saturday, Sunday or holidays). It shall be unlawful to do or perform any work
in violation of such stop order, except as may be necessary to prevent injury
or damage to persons or property, or to correct said violation or variance.
Such stop order may be revoked by the Building Commissioner. (Ord. No. 79-5, §
12, 6-25-79)
Sec. 7-13   Reserved for Future Use.
ARTICLE IA. SINGLE AGENCY FOR BUILDING REGULATION.  2

Sec. 7-14   Building Commissioner of DeKalb County.
   a.   The Building Commissioner of DeKalb County is the single agency
designated to administer building rules and inspection within the boundaries of
the units of government which are parties hereto.
   b.   The Building Commissioner of DeKalb County is authorized and empowered
to make inspections, file reports with the Clerk of the Town and the Plan
Commission of the County. That person shall issue building permits upon the
payment of the fee required by the County Ordinance, and said County Building
Commissioner shall order correction of violations, issue Certificates of
Occupancy, and perform such other ministerial duties as are commonly performed
in the execution of their office, on behalf of the parties hereto as provided
for in the County Ordinance which this Town does now here adopt and approve by
reference.
   c.   Any appeal to a decision by the DeKalb County Building Commissioner
shall lie first with the governing body of the municipal unit that has joined
in this agreement and then to the Fire Prevention and Building Safety
Commission as provided for in Indiana Code, § 22-13-2-7.
   d.   Any judicial remedy sought by the DeKalb County Building Commissioner
to enforce his lawful orders to obtain compliance with the building rules of
the parties hereto shall be brought to the County Attorney for disposition in a
court of general jurisdiction of DeKalb County to be processed according to the
provisions of law. (Res. No.     , § 1-4, 7-10-89)
Sec. 7-15   Fees, Budgets and Appropriations.
   a.   Such permit fees that are collected shall be accounted for and
deposited in the General Fund, and shall be considered full payment for any
inspection services provided by his office on behalf of the parties hereto.
   b.   The Town shall be bound to this participation commencing January 1,
1989, through December 31, 1989, and each calendar year thereafter unless
revoked by ordinance or resolution adopted by the governing body on or before
December 31 of each year, which revocation shall apply beginning with the next
January 1 thereafter.
   c.   The budget and all additional appropriation requests for operation of
the County Building Commissioner's office, including office supplies,
communication expenses, equipment, staff wages, legal costs, travel costs, and
Building Commissioner salary shall be prepared by the DeKalb County
Commissioners and submitted to the DeKalb County Council for approval as
required by law for all County offices. The annual cost of operation shall be
shared by each municipal unit including the County proportionately based upon
the assessed valuation of each such municipal unit participating as it relates
proportionately to the total of all of the assessed valuations of the
participating units.
   d.   That the contact persons for and on behalf of the Town Council of
Ashley, with whom the Building Commission can communicate on a current basis,
are the incumbents of the office of Clerk-Treasurer or the Street and Utilities
Superintendent. (Res. No.~, § 5, 7-10-89)
Sec. 7-16 Reserved for Future Use.
ARTICLE 2. PLACEMENT AND STANDARDS FOR MOBILE HOMES.
Sec. 7-17   Compliance Required.
   This article will apply to all mobile homes located on private property
within the Town of Ashley, Indiana, from June 9, 1964, except that owners of
mobile homes situated on private property at the time of this article is
enacted will not be required to revise their esisting installations to conform
to the provisions herein. However, it shall be mandatory that these provisions
be strictly adhered to if any changes or additions to mobile homes or utility
systems existingatthe time this article is enacted are undertaken by the
owners. (Ore No. 64- 2, § 1A, 6-9-64)
Sec. 7-18   Temporary Permit Required.
   A temporary thirty (30) day permit authorizing the placement of a mobile
home on a private site or for changes or additions to existing mobile homes
within the limits of the Town of Ashley, Indiana, will be issuecL The permit
will authorize the permittee to place a mobile home on a private sfte or to
make a change or addition to an existing mobile home and utility system
provided that the provisions in this article are complied with within the
allotted period of thirty (30) day periods to encompass all provisions in this
article or for-specific provisions contained herein will be at the discretion
of the permitor. A "blanket provIsIon" or "specific provision" extension may be
granted when extenuating circumstances (weather, sickness, etc.) prevent the
permittee from complying with any or all provisions contained herein. (Ord. No.
64-2, § lB, 6-9~64)
Sec. 7-19   Violations.
   It is understood by the permittee that failure to comply with the provisions
in this article shall result in the revocation of the permit thereby
terminating his right to locate a mobile home on a private site and that upon
revocation of a permit for failure to comply, the permittee shall remove the
mobile home from the site designated in the permit voluntarily or legal action
shall be instituted by the permitor to remove the mobile home involuntarily.
(Ord. No. ~2, § lC,
Sec. 7-20   Information Required.
   The permit issued under this article shall specify:
   a.   That the owner of the mobile home is the owner of the property upon
which the mobile home will be located.
   b.   The location and description of the private site.
   c.   The date upon which the mobile home will be located on a private site
   d.   The make, year, model and serial number of the mobile home.
   e.   A signed statement by thepermittee agreeing to comply with all
provisions as stated in this article. (Ord. No. 64-2, § ID, 6-9-64)
Sec. 7-21   Inspections.
   The permitor shall cause an authorized person to make an inspection of the
permittee's mobile home installation on or about the 30th day from date of
issue to determine whether the provisions of this article have been complied
with. Any provision or provisions that have not been complied with shall be put
in writing by the permitor and delivered in duplicate (or sent by certffied
mail) to the permittee within forty-eight (48) hours of the inspection.The
permitor shall have he permittee sign one copy of the provisions (in lieu of
certified mail) which have not yet been but must be complied with and the
permitor shall retain same The permitor shall have ten (10) days to comply with
the provisions not already complied with in lieu of an extension of the
temporary permit which may or may not be issued by the permitor. At the end of
ten (10) days, the permitor shall cause another inspection of the permittee's
installation to be rnade and shall issue a permanent approval of the
installation if all of the provisions have been complied with or shall revoke
the temporary permit and take action under Section
7-19. (Ore No. 64-2, § 1E, 6-9-64)
Sec. 7-22   Definition of Mobile Home.
   Mobile homes authorized for placement on private property shall conform to
the following standards:
   a.   The mobile home shall be no older than ten (10) years at the time the
permit is issued for placement on a private site The age shall be determined by
Indiana State Title issued to the owner.
   b.   The minimum size of the mobile home shall be eight (8) feet in width by
thirty-five (35) feet in overall length (not to include awnings or attachments
thereon).
   c.   The exterior of the mobile home shall be of metal including sides and
roof.
   d.   The mobile home shall have been manufactured by a firm engaged
specifically in the manufacture of mobile homes. (Ord. No. 64-2, § 2, 6-9-64)
Sec. 7-23   Location on Site.
   The mobile home may be placed any where or positioned in any manner on the
sfte except that it may not be located closer to a sidewalk or street than the
structures existing on either side of the property on which the mobile home is
located. (Crd. No. 64-2, § 3, 6-9-64)
Sec. 7-24   Attached Structure.
   a.   No wooden frame entry ways or additional rooms shall be placed by or
attached to the mobile home structure Commercially manufactured patio awnings
or car ports specifically designed for mobile home attachment may be attached
to or placed by the mobile home struetur~ A commercially manufactured screened
enclosure may be added to a commercially manufactured patio awning.
   b.   Frame utility buildings or garages may be erected (but not attached to
the mobile home nor within a distance of three (3) feet of the mobile home
body, including awning) upon the private site in accordance with the local
construction ordinance& (Ore No. ~2, § 4, 6-9-64)
Sec. 7-25   Foundation and Blocking.
   The mobile home will be blocked up in a manner which will minimize setting
and sliding of the structure. The following methods will be adhered to:
   a.   Cement stringers may be poured the length of the longitudinaI chassis
members of the mobile home with a minimum width of sixteen (16) inches for each
stringer and the home shall be supported by concrete building blocks crosswise
of each frame member according to the schedule outline in `c' below or a
complete cement pad the size of the mobile home body may be poured and the
mobile home blocked as above (or);
   b.   A sixteen (16) inch square base of concrete (>r concrete block shall be
leveled as a base for each individual pier and concrete building blocks put on
top of each base up to the frame of the mobile home. A maximum of two (2)
inches of wood shall be placed between the top pier block and the chassis
member. The mobile home shall be supported by concrete building blocks
crosswise of each frame member according to the schedule outlined in `c' below.
   c.   The number of piers used in blocking the mobile home shall be
determined by the length of the mobile home as set forth in the following
schedule:
      Length                     TotalPiers
      35 to 45'                  10 piers (5 to each side)
      45 to 55'                  12 piers (6 to each side)
      55 to 65'                  14 piers (7 to each side)
      Each pier shall rest on a concrete stringer as designated in (a) above or
on a sixteen (16) inch square concrete base as designated in `b' above.
   d.   No cracked or broken concrete blocks, railroad ties, travel trailer
jacks, logs, fabricated horses either of wood or steel shall be used in the
blocking of any mobile home.
   e.   Mobile homes may be anchored to the ground by cable or chain attached
to dead weights dug into the earth in a manner so as not to be visible when the
mobile home is skirted around the bottom.
   f.   Within sixty (60) days after it is located on a private site within the
town limits of Ashley, Indiana, each owner must enclose the bottom exposed
portion of his mobile home with a factory manufactured skirt or one crafted of
weather resistant material. Each skirt shall be insta1ledin a manner to
compliment the appearance of the mobile home and run true vertically and
horizontally with the sides of the mobile home. Corrugated material, plywood,
or masonite properly treated and framed will be acceptable as enclosure& Bales
of hay, cardboard or wooden sheets, tar paper, canvas and other materials not
specifically designed and crafted for usage as a skirt enclosure will not be
acceptable.
   g.   Each mobile home enclosure shall have at least four (4) ventilators,
one each side, one each end, of an area sixteen (16) inches square to allow air
circulation and furnace combustion air to enter underneath the mobile home.
(Ord. No. 64-2, § 5, 6-9-64)
Sec. 7-26   Utilities.
   a.   Water connection to the mobile home shall be brought up from the supply
line at frost level by a minimum of one-half('h~ inch pipe inside of a ten (10)
inch clay tile with a shut off located in the vertical Pipe twenty-four (24)
inches below the ground level and a shut off located at the top of the vertical
pipe at ground leveL The connecting line between the vertical pipe and the
mobile home shall be a minimum thr~eighth (318) inch copper tubing or
acceptable piping wrapped in a manner to prevent freezing during winter
periods.
   b.   Sewerage connection from the mobile home to the ground tile shall be of
a minimum three (3) inch vinyl or four (4) inch orangeburg, or similar
acceptable sewerage tile and connected in such a manner as to insure against
leakage occurring between the mobile home and ground tile connections. Flexible
tubing with wire reinforcement shall not be used on permanent mobile home
installation&
   c.   Fuel System.
      1.   Fifty-five (55) gallon fuel drums feeding gravity type furnaces will
be mounted on a commercially manufactured oil tank rack or metal legs properly
braced and with legs flared out towards the bottom to prevent upset. The foot
of each leg shall rest on a properly leveled four (4) inch by eight (8) inch
concrete building block dug in the ground level.
      2.   Elevated two hundred seventy-five (275) gallon tanks feeding gravity
type furnaces will have one and on-half (1112) inch iron pipe legs mounted in
poured concrete to a depth of eighteen (18) inches to prevent upset and shall
have "X" braces connecting each leg to the other in a manner to prevent rocking
or tipping of the drum.
      3.   Two hundred seventy-five (275) gallon tanks and fi -five (55) gallon
tanks fe&ling gun type furnaces with pump systems may be mount eled concrete
base in a manner that will prevent upset.
   d.   Bottled Ga& LP gas tanks of twenty (20) to twenty-five (25) pound
capacity will be mounted on the mobile home "A Frame" in a manufactured tank
rack with gas regulators securely fastened to the vertical upright above the
tanks. ~ gas tanks of sixty (60) pound capacity or greater will be placed on a
level concrete foundations or commercially hooded gas tank standard. Tanks
standing directly on dirt will not be acceptable Gas feed lines shall be of
three-eighth (318) inch or onehalf (`/2) inch copper tubing or onehalf (112)
inch iron pipe with flared or standard pipe connection&
   e.   Electrical Servce.
      l.   Electrical service to the mobile home shall be provided by a weather
proof minmum thirty (30) amp capacity fuse box at the pole and below the meter
for mobile homes equipped with 110 volt inside service box.
      2.   Electrical service to the mobile home shall be provided by a minimum
of fifty (50) amp fused weather proof boxes at the pole below the meter for
mobil e homes equipped with 220 volt inside service boxes.
      3.   For mobile homes permanently located on private sites, UF type
feeder wire with a minimum size of number 8 shall be used and wired directly
into the pole box. A #8 UF ground wire shall be connected to the skin of the
mobile home and the pole ground.
      4.   No plug-in type connections shall be used at the pole to connect
electrical service wire and a shut off shallbe Provided at the pole either by
means of a lever type throw switch on the box or a catrridge type fuse switch
in the service box.
   f.   Pole, meter and pole service box installations will be in accordance
with standards set by the utility company servicing the owner's site. (Ord. No.
64-2, § 6, 6-9-64)
Sec. 7-27   Penalties.
   Any person who shall violate any provisions of this article shall. be fined
ten dollars ($10.00), provided; however, that each day such violation continues
shall be deemed a separate offense. (Ord. No. 64-2, § 7, 6-9-64)
Sec. 7-28 and Sec. 7-29 Reserved for Future Use.
ARTICLE 3. STREET ADDRESS NUMBERS.
Sec. 7-30 Definitions.
   a.   Residence is any structure wherein persons live, as distinguished from
any structure wherein business is conducted.
   b.   Street Address Numbers are those identifying numerals which are
consistent with identification as recognized by the United States Postal
Service, the Plan Commission or the Utility Department.
   c.   House is considered as a residence, and may contain one or more
residences.
   d.   Apartments are structures which may include one or more residences.
   e.   Business is an establishment for the purveyor of goods or services,
located in some structure.
   f.   Commercial or Industrial Establishment is located in a structure where
one or more persons are employed at least one day in any calendar year. (Ord.
No. 89-10, § 1, 11-13-89)
Sec. 7-31   Minimum Requirements.
   a.   Every house, residence, apartment, business, commercial, or industrial
establishment within the corporation borders of the Town of Ashley, Indiana,
shall have numbers identifying the location. These numbers are herein referred
to as Street Address Numbers for all structures subject to this ordinance.
   b.   Ml Street Address Numbers shall be a minimum of four and on-half (4-1/
2) feet above the ground, sidewalk, driveway, or any other surface reasonably
presumed to be a reference point.
   c.   All Street Address Numbers shall be of a color which, when viewed from
the street in a vehicle, can be seen easily. It is required that said numbers
are to be of a color contrasting or nearly contrasting with the color of the
background surface upon which they are mounted.
   d.   There shall be no obstruction to preclude the Street Address Numbers
from being seen as noted in Subsection 'c' above.
   e.   All Street Address Numbers shall be a minimum of three (3) inches in
height and one and one-half (1-1/2) inches in width, and shall be installed
prior to issuance of an occupancy permit. (Ord. No. 89-10, § 2, 11-13-89; Ord.
No. 2004-01, § 1, 2-9-04)
Sec. 7-32   Penalties.
   a.   Failure to meet the minimum requirements as prescribed in Section 2 of
this article will result in a fine of no more than forty dollars ($40.00).
   b.   Each day that a violation of Section
7-31 exists is considered a new offense. (Ord. No. 89-10, § 3, 11-13-89)
Sec. 7-33   Enforcement.
   a.   It shall be the responsibility of the Town Police Department to enforce
this article.
   b.   Enforcement will be accomplished as follows:
      l.   Upon notice of violation of Section
7-31, an initial letter advising of the violation will be sent to the offending
party.
      2.   The violator will be allowed thirty (30) days to correct or cure the
violation.
      3.   If the violation is not corrected or cured within the thirty (30)
day period, a notice of imposition of penalty shall be delivered to the
responsible violator.
   c.   The Ashley Clerk-Treasurer or designee shall collect all paid penalties
through the Collection Bureau.
   d.   The Town of Ashley shall initiate suit for collection in the DeKalb
Superior Court, Small Claims Division, or in the Steuben Superior Court, Small
Claims Division (whichever has applicable jurisdiction) for all penalties
assessed yet unpaid. (Ord. No. 89-10, § 4, 11-13-89)
Sec. 7-34 Through Sec. 7-39 Reserved for Future Use.
ARTICLE 4. STANDARDS FOR SIDEWALK MAINTENANCE.
Sec. 7-40   Compliance by Property Owners.
   It shall be the duty of all property owners abutting the public ways of the
Town to keep their respective sidewalks, curbs, or gutters in repair, in safe
condition, and in compliance with the Code of Ordinance of Ashley, Indiana, and
with the law. (Ord. No. 93-03, § 1, 7-12-93)
Sec. 7-41   Minimum Design Standards in Sidewalks.
   The minimum design standards for sidewalk construction, within the public
right-of-ways in the Town of Ashley shall be:
      (1)   Minimum surface width shall be four (4) feet.
      (2)   Walk cross slope shall be:
         (i)   Minimum one-quarter (1/4) inch per feet.
         (ii)   Maximum three-eighths (3/8) inch per feet. (Ord. No. 93-03, §2,
7-12-93)
Sec. 7-42   Inspections.
   In determining that sidewalks, curbs, or gutters, are in an unsafe
condition, the Town of Ashley Zoning Inspector, or other designee of the Town
Council, shall consider for purposes of inspection items including but not in
limitation of the following: high joints, weathered surface, chipped surface,
cracked walkways, scaled surface, poor alignment, and poor grade. (Ord. No. 93-
03, § 3, 7-12-93)
Sec. 7-43   Notice to Repair.
   The Town of Ashley Clerk-Treasurer may require, by mailed notice, a Town of
Ashley property owner to repair or replace existing sidewalks, curbs, and
gutters in compliance with this Ordinance This notice shall be done through
United States mail, with proper postage affixed; the property owner shall be
determined by use of the tax records in the office of the Auditor of
DeKalbCounty or Steuben County, State of Indiana. If said property owner fails
to make or initiate the requested repairs within thirty (30) days from the Town
of Ashley's notice, the Town may do so and charge the same against the property
owner. (Ord. No. 93-03, §4, 7-12-93)
Sec. 7-44   Bond - When Not Required.
   When any property owner repairs or replaces his sidewalk, curbs or gutters
abutting the public ways of the Town so as to restore them to a safe condition
in compliance with this code or pursuant to a notice according to the
provisions of this Ordinance, then said owner may make the necessary repairs
and replacements without a bond filed with the Town of Ashley and without
obtaining a building permit on condition that said repair or replacement
conforms to any building codes or ordinances then existing pursuant to
specifications, size and shape of sidewalks, curbs or gutters. (Ord. No. 93-03,
§ 5, 7-12-93)
Sec. 7-45   Lien Upon Property - Foreclosure.
   Upon failure of the owner to pay the charge for installation, repair or
replacement of sidewalks, curbs, or gutters levied by the Town within ten (10)
days after the Town completion of the work, the Clerk-Treasurer shall file in
the office of the Recorder of DeKalb County and Steuben County, Indiana, for
recordation in the Miscellaneous Records a notice that the Town claims a lien
upon the real estate upon which work was done, and from and after the filing of
the notice, such charge shall be a lien upon the real estate and may be
enforced by foreclosure in the same manner in which mechanic's and
materialmen's liens are enforced under the laws of the State of Indiana
Foreclosure proceedings shall be at the cost of the defendant owner or owners
and with attorney fees. The town may also deliver the delinquent account to the
Town Attorney for collection. (Ord. No. 93-03, § 6, 7-12-93)
Sec. 7-46 Removing Existing Sidewalks.
   A property owner may remove, dig up or excavate an existing sidewalk. Prior
to the removal, digging up or excavation of an existing sidewalk the property
owner must give notice to the Town of Ashley Town Council by certified mail,
return receipt requested, to the Town Clerk-Treasurer. Upon receipt of the
certified notice the Town of Ashley will then assume the responsibility for
removal of the debris within fifteen (15) days. The property owner digging up,
removing or excavating his sidewalk will be responsible for payment of the
costs incurred. The Town of Ashley shall assume the cost for removal of
sidewalk debris. (Ord. No. 93-03, § 7, 7-12-93)
Sec. 7-47 Thirty (30) Day Requirement to Install New Sidewalk.
   The property owner shall be responsible for installing a new sidewalk within
thirty (30) days from any sidewalk removal. The liability for the state of
disrepair between the removal, digging up and excavation, and the installation
of the new sidewalk shall be that of the property owner.
      (a)   Should the property owner fail to install a new sidewalk within
thirty (30) days, the Town of Ashley may undertake the process of installing
the same, and shall collect the expenses for the same, in compliance with §7-45
of this Ordinance. (Ord. No. 93-03, § 8, 7-12-93)
Sec. 7-48   Sidewalks Required in New Plats.
   All new P1ats presented or to be considered by the Town Council of the Town
of Ashley, shall provide and contain sidewalks for the benefit of pedestrians
according to Town specifications. (Ord. No. 93-03, § 9, 7-12-93)
Sec. 7-49 through Sec. 7-54 Reserved for Future Use.
ARTICLE 5. ENTRANCES FOR DWELLING.
Sec. 7-55   Placement of Front Entrances.
   a.   Main entrances to dwellings, as determined by the Town of Ashley Plan
Commission, shall be placed on the side of the dwelling facing the street on
which the dwelling has been located. (Ord. No. 99-07, § 1, 11-8-99)
   b.   Main entrances, as determined by the Town of Ashley Plan Commission,
for dwellings located on corner lots shall be placed on the side of the
dwelling facing the street for which the lot has been assigned a house number.
(Ord. No. 97-5, 8-11-97; Ord. No. 99-07, § 2, 11-8-99)
   c.   The means for ingress and egress (i.e. front door) for each structure
must be within the principal building located on the address site, and not
through an adjoining building. (Ord. No. 2001-13, § 1, 11-12-01)
Sec. 7-56 through Sec. 7-65 Reserved for Future Use.

ARTICLE 1. SPEED LIMIT DESIGNATIONS.  1

1 seq. Local authorities are specifically granted authority to regulate speed
  limits pursuant to I.C., § 9-21-5-1, et seq.
Sec. 8-1   Thirty (30) Miles Per Hour.
   a.   Pursuant to Indiana Code, § 9-21-5-6, it shall be unlawful for any
vehicle to exceed thirty (30) miles per hour on the following designated roads:
All existing streets within the Town except where posted otherwise.
   b.   Upon posting of this speed limit designation, pursuant to Indiana Code,
§ 9-21-1-3, it shall be an infraction, with the appropriate penalty being
imposed upon conviction.
Sec. 8-2   Thirty-Five (35) Miles Per Hour.
   a.   Pursuant to Indiana Code, § 9-21-5-6, it shall be unlawful for any
vehicle to exceed thirty-five (35) miles per hour on the following designated
roads: On State Street from six hundred (600) feet west of South Harrison
Avenue to two hundred (200) feet east of South Garrison Street.
   b.   Upon posting of this speed limit designation, pursuant to Indiana Code,
§ 9-21-1-3, it shall be an infraction, with the appropriate penalty being
imposed upon conviction.
Sec. 8-3   Forty-Five (45) Miles Per Hour.
   a.   Pursuant to Indiana Code, § 9-21-5-6, it shall be unlawful for any
vehicle to exceed forty-five (45) miles per hour on the following designated
roads: Reserved.
   b.   Upon posting of this speed limit designation, pursuant to Indiana Code,
§ 9-21-1-3, it shall be an infraction, with the appropriate penalty being
imposed upon conviction.
Sec. 8-4   Twenty (20) Miles Per Hour.
   a.   There shall be a posted speed limit of twenty (20) miles-per-hour When
Children Present, in the following locations:
      1.   On Union Street, between Hobart and Ruby Streets; and
      2.   On Chapel Lane. (Ord. No. 94-16, § 2, 8-8-94)
   b.   Any person who violates any provision of this Section shall be subject
to a Class A fine as set forth in Section
2-62. (Am. Ord. No. 2006-18, §§1, 2, 12-11-06)
Sec. 8-5   Forty (40) Miles Per Hour.
   a.   Pursuant to Indiana Code, § 9-21-5-6, it shall be unlawful for any
vehicle to exceed forty (40) miles per hour on the following designated roads:
      1.   On South Gonser Avenue; and
      2.   On Angle Drive.
   b.   The Town Marshal, or his or her designee, is authorized to post signs,
or other appropriate signage, to accomplish the directives of this Section.
   c.   The Town Marshal, or his or her designee, is authorized to remove
signage and road markings inconsistent with the directives of this Section,
including but not limited to removal of school crossing and school zone signs.
   d.   The Town Marshal, or his or her designee, is authorized to enforce this
Section and issue fines for violation of this Section as per the Indiana Code

ARTICLE 2. SPECIFIC TRAFFIC AND PARKING REGULATIONS.
Sec. 8-9      U-Turns Prohibited.  2
   U-turns are not permitted upon any street in the town.
(Ord. 2015-02, 6-8-15)
 
Notes
2 2   I.C., § 9-21-8-22, addresses U-Turns.
Sec. 8-10   Stopping, Standing, or Parking.   3
   a.   No person shall stop, stand, or park a vehicle, except when necessary
to avoid conflict with other traffic, or to avoid conflict with law or the
directions of a police officer or traffic control device in any of the
following places:
      1.   On a sidewalk;
      2.   In front of a public or private driveway;
      3.   Within an intersection;
      4.   Within fifteen (15) feet of a fire hydrant;
      5.   On a crosswalk;
      6.   Within twenty feet (20') of a crosswalk at an intersection;
      7.   Within thirty feet (30') upon the approach to any flashing beacon,
stop sign, or traffic-control signal located at the side of a roadway.
      8.   Between a safety zone and the adjacent curb or within thirty feet
(30') of points on the curb immediately opposite the ends of a safety zone
unless the traffic authority indicates a different length by signs or markings.
      9.   Within fifty feet (50') of the nearest rail of a railroad crossing.
      10.   Within twenty feet (20') of the driveway entrance to any fire
station and on the side of a street opposite the entrance to any fire station
within seventy-five feet (75') of said entrance when properly sign posted;
      11.   Alongside or opposite a street excavation or obstruction if
stopping, standing, or parking would obstruct traffic.
      12.   On the roadway side of any vehicle stopped or parked at the edge or
curb of a street;
      13.   Upon a bridge or other elevated structure upon a highway or within
a highway tunnel.
      14.   At any place where official signs prohibit stopping; and
      15.   On the west side of Adams Court or on the east side of Franklin
Court.
   b.   It shall be unlawful for the driver of a vehicle to stand a passenger
vehicle for a period of time longer than is necessary for the loading or
unloading of passengers, not to exceed three (3) minutes, and for the driver to
stand any freight carrying vehicles for a period of time longer than necessary
to load, unload, and deliver materials, not to exceed thirty (30) minutes, at
the loading zone which is marked as such.
   c.   No vehicle shall be parked with the left side of such vehicle next to
the curb, except on one-way streets, and it shall be unlawful to stand or park
a vehicle in a street other than parallel with the curb and with the two right
wheels of the vehicle within twelve (12) inches of the regularly established
curb line, except upon those streets that have been marked for angle parking,
where vehicles shall be parked at an angle to the curb indicated by such marks.
   d.   The Town Council shall authorize persons to cause signs to be posted in
all areas where parking is limited or prohibited, indicating such limitations
or prohibitions.
   e.   It shall be unlawful for the owner, driver, or operator thereof to
permit any truck, tractor, semi-trailer, trailer, or other freight vehicle to
remain upon any public street in the town, for a longer period than one hour,
and then only if such vehicle is actually being loaded or unloaded. This
Section shall not apply to vehicles whose primary function is the carrying of
passengers.
   f.   Whenever a vehicle is parked in violation of any provision of any
section, statute, or the Town Code, the Town Marshal or any Deputy Marshal of
the town is authorized to cause any such vehicle to be towed away by any firm
having towing vehicles equipped to tow any vehicle. Neither the town nor the
firm engaged to do the towing shall in any way be held liable for any damage or
loss of any towed vehicles (or its contents). The vehicle may not be redeemed
until the violator has paid all fees accrued as a result of the towing.
   g.   1.   The President of the Town Council or in the absence or
unavailability of the President, then the Vice-President, and in the absence or
unavailability of both the President and the Vice-President of the Council,
then any member of the Town Council, after consultation with the Town Marshal
and the head of the Street Department, may declare a snow emergency by
executive order, when in the opinion of the President of the Town Council,
Vice-President of the Town Council or other Town Council member, as the case
may be, such order would be in the best interest of the public safety and
welfare of the residents of the town. Upon the declaration of a snow emergency,
parking is prohibited upon all streets and alleys that are dedicated to public
use and upon all town parking lots.
      2.   Publication and broadcast of a snow emergency declaration order
shall be made or caused to be made by the President of the Town Council or
whichever public official declares the snow emergency, by issuing a press
release to all area law enforcement agencies, fire departments, hospitals and
news media.
   h.   Any person who violates the provisions of this Section commits a "Class
C Infraction'' and a judgment of up to five hundred dollars ($500.00) may be
entered for a violation constituting a "Class C Infraction".
(Ord. No. 93-02, §1, 6-14-93; Ord. No. 2004-05, § 1, 7-12-04; Ord. No. 2015-02,
6-8-15)
                                      
2   I.C., § 9-21-8-22, addresses U-Turns.
3   I.C., § 9-21-1-3, addresses stopping, standing and parking regulations.

Sec. 8-11   Parallel Parking Required.
   a.   On all streets and/or portions thereof, vehicles shall stand, stop, or
park parallel with the street so that both front and rear right wheels shall be
within twelve (12) inches of the curbing; however, this regulation shall not
apply where diagonal parking is permitted and so designated by proper signs or
markings.
   b.   Violation of this section shall be subject to a fine of two dollars
($2.00) for each violation payable to the Clerk-Treasurer.
Sec. 8-12   Stop Signs. 4
   a.   The Town may designate intersections as a stop intersection and require
all vehicles to stop at one or more entrances to such intersection.
   b.   The Town will post signs at which designated intersections, giving
notice of the designation as a stop intersection.
   c.   It shall be unlawful for any person to fail to obey the markings of
signs posted under this Section.
   d.   Every operator of a vehicle shall observe all "stop" signs and signals
erected by the Town of Ashley.
   e.   The Town Council believes that it is in the interest of public safety
and for the welfare of the public to install stop signs at the following
locations:

10-13-03; Am. Ord. 2013-04, 8-12-13; Am. Ord. 2015-02, 6-8-15)
      (3)   There shall be a three-way stop sign placed at the intersections of

   c.   The penalty for violating this Section shall be a fine of no more than

Sec. 8-14   Vehicle Noise Prohibited.
   a.   No person shall operate or use a motor vehicle of a type subject to
State registration on the public streets and highways of this community at any
time or under any condition of grade, or load or acceleration or deceleration
or so which is out of repair in such a manner as to create loud and unnecessary
grating, grinding, rattling, roaring, screeching, squealing or other noise
which shall unduly disturb the peace and quietude of the community, regardless
of whether such noise be emitted from the engine or exhaust system or tires on
the roadway.
   b.   No person shall operate or use a motor vehicle of a type subject to
State registration on the public streets and highways of this community that
creates any noise which disturbs the peace and quietude of the community. In
addition, the use of jake brakes within the Town of Ashley is prohibited. (Ord.
No. 99-04, § 1, 9-13-99)
   c.   Upon offense of this section, the driver shall be fined not to exceed
twenty-five dollars ($25.00). Thereafter, if the said driver should commit the
offense in the same manner, the driver shall be fined not less than fifty
dollars ($50.00) per offense. (Ord. No. 99-04, § 2, 9-13-99)
Sec. 8-15   Specific Parking Regulations.
   a.   There will be "Two Hour Parking" on both sides of State Road 4 from
Wabash Avenue to Gonser Avenue.
      (1)   Signs are to be posted stating that "Two Hour Parking" is allowed
in this area. (Ord. No. 93-02, § 1, 6-14-93)
   b.   Parking shall be prohibited in the driveway which is located on the
following described real estate: Lots numbered four (4) and five (5) in Block
numbered twenty-one (21) in Original Plat of the Town of Ashley, DeKalb County,
State of Indiana. (Ord. No. 95-11, § 1, 11-13- 95)
   c.   Parking shall be prohibited on and along the West side of Union Avenue
from the Right-of-Way for State Road 4 through eighty (80) feet North of that
point.
   A twenty feet (20') wide driveway, thirty feet (30') North of the Right-of-
Way of State Road 4, shall be permitted for the owner of Lot 9 in Block 14 of
the Original Plat of the Town of Ashley, as recorded at Plat Book #1, at page
75. (Ord. No. 95-08, §§ 1,2, 6-12-95)
   d.   Parking shall be prohibited along the south side of Ashton Street,
within the Town of Ashley, Indiana.
   e.   (1)   Parking shall be prohibited along H.L. Thompson Drive, within the
Town of Ashley, Indiana.
      (2)   The Town Marshal is hereby authorized to cause signs to be posted
within the Town of Ashley, Indiana in compliance with this division e.
      (3)   The Town Marshal is authorized to enforce the provisions of this
division e. with fines and penalties as permitted by the Indiana Code for
enforcement of ordinances.
   f.   Parking shall be prohibited along Industrial Drive and along Family
Dollar Parkway within the Town of Ashley.
      (1)   The Town Marshal is hereby authorized to cause signs to be posted
within the Town of Ashley, Indiana, in compliance with this division f.
      (2)   The Town Marshal is authorized to enforce the provisions of this
division f. with fines and penalties as permitted by the Indiana Code for
enforcement of ordinances.
   g.   Violations of this Section shall be subject to the fine as per the
Indiana Code for a similar infractions set forth in Section
2-65. (Ord. No. 93-02, § 1, 6-14-93; Am. Ord. No. 2003-09, § 1, 12-8-03; Am.
Ord. No. 2006-18, §§1, 2, 12-11-06; Am. Ord. No. 2008-08, §§ 1, 2, 3, 12-8-08;
Am. Ord. No. 2012-03, 5-14-12)
Sec. 8-16   Parking by Town Hall and Parking of Fire Vehicles.
   a.   Individuals shall be prohibited from parking their vehicles at any
location in the alley located to the North of the Town Hall, between Union
Street and Grand Avenue. The alley being more specifically described as
follows:
      The unnamed alley located in Lot 1, Block 21 of the Original Plat of the
Town of Ashley. (Ord. No. 95-02, § 1, 2-13-95)
   b.   Emergency or Fire Department vehicles shall be allowed to park in the
restricted area of the above-referenced alley provided that they do not
prohibit traffic flow through the alley. (Ord. No. 95-02, § 2, 2-13-95)
   c.   Regular and Volunteer fire fighters shall be allowed to park their
vehicles in the restricted area of the above-referenced alley during such times
as they are on an emergency call in their capacity as fire fighters, provided
that they do not prohibit traffic flow through the alley. (Ord. No. 95-02, § 3,
2-13-95)
Sec. 8-17   No Passing Streets and Roads.
   a.   All streets and roadways whether now located within the corporate
limits of the Town of Ashley, Indiana, or later annexed thereto, are hereby
designated as no passing, unless otherwise indicated by posted signage or
ordinance.
   b.   The Town Marshal, or his or her designee, is authorized to post no-
passing zone signs, or other appropriate signage, to accomplish the directives
of this Section.
   c.   The Town Marshal, or his or her designee, is authorized to enforce this
Section and issue fines for violation of this Section per the Indiana Code for
a similar infraction. (Ord. No. 2004-08, §§ 1-3, 8-9-04; Am. Ord. No. 2006-18,
§§ 1, 2, 12-11-06)
Sec. 8-18 through Sec. 8-20 Reserved for Future Use.
ARTICLE 3. SNOW EMERGENCY REGULATIONS.
Sec. 8-21   Snow Emergency Defined.
   A "snow emergency" is declared to be a period of time prior to a forecast by
the United States Weather Bureau, during and after a snow fall, during which
vehicular traffic is expected to be particularly hazardous or congested due to
the elements, and during which period of time the parking of such vehicles
could hinder, delay, and obstruct the safe flow of traffic and the proper
cleaning, clearing and making safe of certain heavily traveled public streets
of this Town, which streets shall be designated snow control routes and listed
and maintained on file in the office of the Clerk-Treasurer of the Town of
Ashley.
Sec. 8-22   Proclamation of Snow Emergency.
   A snow emergency shall commence by order, determination and proclamation by
the Town Marshal or Town Council Member before, during or after a snow fall
when, in his or her sound judgment and discretion, the circumstances warrant
the determination of such an emergency for the public safety of the Town. Such
snow emergency shall continue in effect until the Town Marshal determines that
an emergency no longer exists and accordingly terminates such emergency.
Sec. 8-23   No Parking on Snow Control Routes.
   It shall be unlawful for the owner, driver, or operator of an vehicle to
park or stop the same or to permit the same to be parked or to stand at any
time during the period of an snow emergency on any of the routes or streets
listed as snow control routes on file in the office of the Clerk-Treasurer of
the Town. Upon failure to remove a motor vehicle from one of e the snow control
routes after 24-hour notice, the owner of the vehicle shall have committed an
infraction and shall be penalized up to one hundred dollars ($100.00) per
incident, and the vehicle may be towed at the owner’s expense. (Am. Ord. 2014-
03, 4-14-14)
Sec. 8-24   Towing of Vehicles.
   Any police officer, upon discovering any such vehicle parked or stopped in
violation of this Article, may remove such vehicle or cause the same to be
removed to any Town-owned property or to a private garage or place where so
authorized pursuant to contract, where such vehicle shall be impounded and
retained and shall be released only as provided by law.
Sec. 8-25 through Sec. 8-27 Reserved for Future Use.
ARTICLE 4. TRUCK REGULATIONS. 5
 
Notes
5 5   I.C., § 9-20-1-3, et seq., addresses size weight, and use restrictions and the
  local authorities power to enact ordinances.
Sec. 8-28   Trucks, generally.
   a.   For purposes of this article, a truck is any motor vehicle designed,
used, or maintained primarily for the transportation of property and which has
three (3) or more axles or license to carry combined body and weight exceeding
twenty-six thousand (26,000) pounds.
   b.   Except as provided below, it shall be unlawful for the operator of any
truck to travel upon any street which is not a truck route within the Town.
   c.   The operation of a truck is permitted on local streets for pick-up,
delivery or service only if the truck has a point of origin or destination
within the Town which is not on a truck route. The operator of the truck with a
point of origin within the Town may travel by local streets using the
physically shortest distance between the point of origin and a truck route. The
operator of the truck with a point of destination within the Town may travel by
local streets using the physically shortest distance between the truck route
and the point of destination.
   d.   The operator of any truck subject to this chapter that travels on a
local street shall produce evidence if stopped by a law person or officer while
driving on a Town street which is not a truck route that it has a proper place
of origin or destination within the Town. In the event the operator of the
truck cannot produce such a document, a citation of violating this subsection
may be issued.
   e.   Notwithstanding any other provision of this Section, the operator of a
truck may operate said truck upon any detour officially established as a
substitute for those streets identified as truck routes herein or by direction
of any law enforcement officer or pursuant to any special temporary emergency
use permit issued by the controller's office.
   f.   Exceptions: The provisions of this Section do not apply to trucks that
are:
      1.   Owned or operated by the Town;
      2.   Engaged in picking up solid waste within the Town; or
      3.   Used as an ambulance, fire truck, school bus, or in the law
enforcement capacity by any governmental agency or governmental unit.
(Ord. 2015-02, 6-8-15)
Sec. 8-29   Semi-Trailers Restricted.
   a.   Pursuant to Indiana Code, § 9-4-17.1, et seq., known as the Uniform Act
Regulating Traffic on Highways, as may be amended from time to time, the
operation of semi-trailers pulled by a tractor is prohibited within the Town
limits of the Town of Ashley, except on the following streets:
      1.   State Street - State Road 4;
      2.   South Gonser Avenue;
      3.   North Grand Avenue;
      4.   North and South Wabash Street;
      5.   South Harrison Street;
      6.   West Garfield Street. (Ord. No. 81-6, § 1, 10-12-81)
   b.   The only exceptions to the above prohibition of semi-trailer traffic
within the Town limits of the Town of Ashley shall be for delivery or pick-up.
(Ord. No. 81-6, § 2, 10-12-81)
   c.   All streets where semi-trailers are prohibited shall be properly posted
with signs indicating that truck traffic is prohibited except for local
deliveries or local pick-ups.
Sec. 8-30   Penalty.
   Any person who violates any provision of this Article shall be deemed to
have committed a Class B infraction. The expense of towing the vehicle or
storage costs of any vehicle, if any, shall be added to the fine assessed.
(Ord. No. 81-6, § 3, 10-12-81)
Sec. 8-31   Truck Route Established.
   a.   Commercial vehicles defined in Indiana Code § 9-13-2-31.5 shall be
restricted to the following streets and roads within the Town of Ashley,
heading north to Interstate 69 from County Road 27 and heading south from
Interstate 69:
      1.   State Road 4;
      2.   H.L. Thompson Drive;
      3.   Industrial Drive;
      4.   South Gonser Street from Industrial Drive to County Road 27.
   b.   The Town Marshal is authorized to enforce the provisions of this
section with fines and penalties as permitted by the Indiana Code for
enforcement of ordinances. (Ord. No. 2012-05, 6-11-12)
Sec. 8-32   through Sec. 8-35 Reserved for Future Use.

2001-21, § 1, 12-10-01; Ord. No. 2005-04, § 1, 5-9-05)
Sec. 8-38   Golf Cart Operation.
   a.   Golf cart, as used in this section, is defined as a four (4) wheeled
motor vehicle originally and specifically designed and intended to transport
one (1) or more individuals and golf clubs for the purpose of playing the game
of golf on a golf course.
   b.   A person may operate, drive, or park ("operate") a golf cart on the
streets, alleys, and properties under the jurisdiction of the Town of Ashley
subject to the rules and restrictions set forth herein.
   c.   Operators of golf carts must have a valid driver's license and shall
obey all state, federal, and local laws, regulations, and ordinances governing
passenger motor vehicles, including but not limited to laws, regulations, and
ordinances pertaining to licensing of operators, and traffic regulation and
shall be registered annually with the Ashley Police Department. A five-dollar
($5.00) annual fee shall be imposed at the time of registration.
   d.   Golf carts shall be operated only from dawn to dusk from March 15 to
November 15 of each calendar year and must not travel at more than 20 mph.
   e.   No person shall operate a golf cart on a sidewalk or other area
designated for pedestrian traffic.
   f.   No person shall operate or permit the operation of a golf cart without
proof of liability insurance financial responsibility.
   g.   No person shall operate a golf cart unless the driver and any and all
passengers of the golf cart are seated in a seat attached to the golf cart as
manufactured.
   h.   No person shall operate a golf cart unless the golf cart is equipped
with and displays a triangular slow moving vehicle emblem or safety flag that
is entirely visible from the rear of the golf cart at all times.
   i.   No person shall operate a golf cart in a reckless manner. Reckless is
defined, for this purpose, as operation that would place the occupants of the
golf cart, pedestrians, any person or property, or other motor vehicle
operators in position to risk bodily injury.
   j.   No person shall operate a golf cart on the following streets: State
Street, South Gonser Avenue, and North Grand Avenue, H L Thompson Jr. Drive,
Industrial Drive, Family Dollar Parkway, Angle Drive and Archery Way. The above
listed streets may be crossed in a perpendicular manner so as to cross the
streets, but may not be driven upon for any other reason.
   k.   Any person, firm, or corporation who violates, or permits a violation
of any provisions of this section shall be guilty of a class A ordinance
violation and be subject to the fines as defined in the Town of Ashley's fine
schedule.
   l.   1.   Licensed drivers shall be permitted to operate golf carts on the
streets, alleys and highways within the Town subject to the following
conditions:
         a)   That no more than one (1) operator and one (1) passenger shall be
permitted on a golf cart designed for two (2) people when operating at any
time, and no more than one (1) operator and three (3) passengers shall be
permitted on a golf cart designed to transport four (4) people when operating
at any time;
         b)   That the golf cart be registered with the Clerk-Treasurer of the
Town of Ashley, Indiana;
         c)   That an initial registration fee of twenty-five dollars ($25.00)
is paid by the registering party, with an annual renewal fee of ten dollars
($10.00);
      2.   That nothing in this division (l) should be construed to permit any
operator of a golf cart to operate upon any state highway.
      3.   Any golf cart registered with the Town of Hudson, Indiana shall be
permitted to operate upon the streets, alleys, and highways of the Town of
Ashley, Indiana, subject to all terms of this division (l) except proper
registration.
      4.   Anyone operating a golf cart in the Town of Ashley, Indiana, in
violation of this division (l) shall be chargeable with a civil penalty of
fifty dollars ($50.00).
(Ord. No. 2009-04, §§ 1-14, 8-10-09; Ord. No. 2015-06, §§ 1-11, 12-14-15; Am.
Ord. 2017-1, 5-8-17)
Sec. 8-39   Seat Belts Required.
   All front seat occupants of motorized vehicles are required to properly use
a seat belt at all times while a motor vehicle is moving.
(Ord. 2015-02, 6-8-15)
Sec. 8-40    Operation of Off-Road Vehicles
   The definition of the term “Town Roadways” is hereby defined as follows:
“Town Roadways” shall include all streets and adjacent right of ways within the
Town, except federal and state roads, federal and state right of ways.
   Definition of off-road vehicle: The section adopts the Off Road Vehicle
Definition provided by Indiana law.
   A.   A person shall not operate an off-road vehicle:
      1.   With disregard for traffic control signs and signals.
      2.   At a rate of speed greater than is reasonable and proper for the
type of off-road vehicle and road condition.
      3.   On any private property without consent of the landowner or tenant.
      4.   At a speed exceeding five (5) miles per hour within one hundred
(100) feet of an individual on foot (not in or upon a vehicle).
      5.   Without a valid motor vehicle driver’s license.
      6.   Without liability insurance for the off-road vehicle consistent with
the minimum requirements of the State of Indiana for motor vehicle insurance.
      7.   Before sunrise or after sunset unless it has at least one headlight
and one tail light.
      8.   Without adequate brakes capable of producing deceleration of 15 feet
a second at a speed of 20 miles per hour. (Ord. 2022-01, 7-11-22).

if service is being provided to a mobile home, that is not in a mobile home
park, to the titleholder of the mobile home.

within a Mobile Home Park shall be defined as the titleholders of the Mobile

Sec. 9-11   Fluorides into the Water Supply. 2
   a.   The Water Works Superintendent is authorized and directed to have plans
and specifications prepared for the purchase and installation of equipment to
add sodium fluoride to the water being distributed by the Town Water Works, and
to submit them to the Indiana State Board of Health for approval. (Res. No. 82-
4, § 1, 5-10-92)
   b.   Upon the approval of these plans and specifications by the Indiana
State Board of Health, such equipment and supplies shall be purchased and
installed in the manner provided by State law. The fluoride compound shall be
added to the public water supply in sufficient quantities to bring the total
amount of fluoridations (F-) present in the finished water to the optimum
concentration recommended by State Board of Health but not exceeding 1.5 parts
per million by weight. (Res. No. 82-4, § 2, 5-10-92)
