Sec. 9-12   Water Works Superintendent.
   Reserved.
Sec. 9-13   Monthly Billing Frequency.
   Water bills shall be sent to each customer on a monthly basis.
Sec. 9-14   Conditions for Water Service Disconnection; Objection.
   a.   Water service shall be disconnected after two (2) delinquent billings,
not necessarily non- consecutive, and after ten (10) days from the posting of
written notice on the property where the Town Council informs the customer that
the water shall be disconnected unless the past due amount and the delinquency
charges are paid in full. Re-connect charges shall be assessed for all service
disconnected pursuant to this section.
   b.   Any request to submit an objection or any request for the right to be
heard prior to a water service disconnection shall be made in writing to the
Town Clerk of Ashley, Indiana, and the written request shall set forth all
reasons as to why water service disconnection should not occur. (Am. Res. 2014-
04, 12-8-14)
Sec. 9-15   Service Deposit.
   a.   A deposit of one hundred dollars ($100.00) shall be required prior to
commencement of water and sewer utility service within the Town.
   b.   The Consumer Deposit Fund shall be amended to allow for deposit of the
joint sewer and water deposit.
   c.   The joint sewer and water deposits shall be held by the Clerk-Treasurer
of the Town in the Consumer Deposit Fund for a period of twenty-four (24)
months.
   d.   During the twenty-four (24) month period that the Clerk-Treasurer is
authorized to hold the deposit, if the sewer and water utility consumer becomes
delinquent in the payment of the sewer and/or water utility fee, the Clerk-
Treasurer is authorized to apply so much of the consumer's individual deposit
as necessary to bring such account current. The Clerk-Treasurer shall apply the
deposit first to delinquent water fees then to delinquent sewer fees.
   e.   At the conclusion of the twenty-fourth (24th) month that the Clerk-
Treasurer has held an individual consumer's deposit, the Clerk-Treasurer shall
return any unused deposit to the consumer.
   f.   If a user discontinues service, the Clerk-Treasurer shall return the
portion of said consumer's unused deposit within forty-five (45) days from
discontinuation of service. The consumer is responsible for providing the
Clerk-Treasurer with an address to which such unused deposits shall be
returned.
(Ord. No. 2002-14, 12-9-02; Am. Ord. No. 2013-02, 2-11-13)
Sec. 9-16   Removal from Indiana Utility Regulatory Commission.
   a.   The Town Council of the Town of Ashley determines to remove the
municipal waterworks from the jurisdiction of the Indiana Utility Regulatory
Commission pursuant to Indiana Code, § 8-1.5-3-9.1.
   b.   The Town Council finds that written notice of this meeting has been
provided by mail to all rate payers of the municipal waterworks and to the
Indiana Utility Regulatory Commission in accordance with Indiana Code, § 8-1.5-
3-9.1.
   c.   All ordinances in conflict herewith are repealed.
   d.   This ordinance shall be effective sixty (60) days after adoption by the
Town Council, provided that a petition is not filed with the Town Council
requesting that the question of removal from Commission jurisdiction be
submitted to the registered voters of the Town at the next election, all in
accordance with Indiana Code, § 8-1.5-3-9.1. (Ord. No. 89-4, § 1-4, 6-12-89)
Sec. 9-17   Reconnection Charges.
   a.   There shall be a seventy-five dollar ($75.00) reconnection fee charge
for turning on water service at the place of service for any user who has had
the water service terminated for non-collection of charges due.
   b.   There shall be a seventy-five dollar ($75.00) charge to turn on water
service at the place of service for any inspection purposes that is not
mandated by the Town of Ashley. One business days notice prior to inspection is
required to be given to the Clerk-Treasurer of the Town of Ashley. (Ord. No.
93-01, § 1, 4-12-93; Am. Ord. No. 2011-03, 8-8-11; Am. Ord. No. 2013-01, 2-11-
13; Am. Ord. No. 2018-04, 11-12-18)
Sec. 9-18   Refunding Water Deposits.
   a.   Thirty-day Refund. A deposit made for water service that is no longer
in use shall be refunded to the party making the deposit within thirty (30)
days from the date of payment of the final bill, provided that the party
responsible for the water bill has made the final payment and there is no
outstanding ba1ance. In the event there is an outstanding balance, then the
deposit shall be credited to the final bill. (Res. No. 92-04, § 1, 11-9-92)
   b.   Two-Year Refund. After the initial connection of water service to a
user, the initial deposit made for water service to that user shall be refunded
after two (2) years, provided that the party responsible for the water bill has
made payments as agreed for twenty-four (24) months, and there are no
delinquencies or late payments during that period. (Res. No. 92-04, § 2, 11-9-
92)
   c.   Authorization. The Clerk-Treasurer is authorized to make such refunds
as above set out. (Res. No. 92-04, § 3, 11-9-92)
Sec. 9-19   Cross-Connection Control.
   a.   A cross connection shall be defined as any physical connection or
arrangement between two otherwise separate systems, one of which contains
potable water from the Town of Ashley water systems, and the other, water from
a private source, water of unknown or questionable safety, or steam, gases, or
chemicals, whereby there may be a flow from one system to the other, the
direction of flow depending on the pressure differential between the two
systems.
   b.   No person, firm or corporation shall establish or permit to be
established or maintain or permit to be maintained any cross connection. No
interconnection shall be established whereby potable water from a private,
auxiliary, or emergency water supply other than the regular public water supply
of the Town of Ashley may enter the supply or distribution system of said
municipality, unless such private, auxiliary, or emergency water supply and the
method of connection and use of such supply shall have been approved by the
Town of Ashley water and sewer departments and by the Indiana Department of
Environmental Management in accordance with 327 IAC 8-10.
   c.   It shall be the duty of the Town of Ashley water and/or sewer
departments to cause inspections to be made of all properties served by the
public water system where cross connections with the public water system is
deemed possible. The frequency of inspection and reinspections based on
potential health hazards involved shall be as established by the Town of Ashley
water and/or sewer departments.
   d.   Upon presentation of credentials, the representatives of the Town of
Ashley water and/or sewer departments shall have the right to request entry at
any reasonable time to examine any property served by a connection to the
public water system of the Town of Ashley for cross connections. On request,
the owner, lessee, or occupant of any property so served shall furnish to the
inspection agency any pertinent information regarding the piping system or
systems on such property. The refusal of access or refusal of requested
pertinent information shall be deemed evidence of the presence of cross
connections.
   e.   The Town of Ashley water and/or sewer departments are hereby authorized
and directed to discontinue water service to any property wherein any
connection in violation of this section exists, and to take such other
precautionary measures deemed necessary to eliminate any danger of
contamination of the public water system. Water service shall be discontinued
only after reasonable notice is served on the owner, lessee, or occupants of
the property or premises where a violation is found or suspected to exist.
Water service to such property shall not be restored until the cross connection
(s) has been eliminated in compliance with the provisions of this section.
   f.   If it is deemed by the Town of Ashley water and/or sewer departments
that a cross connection or an emergency endangers public health, safety, or
welfare and requires immediate action, and a written finding to that effect is
filed with the Clerk of the Town of Ashley and delivered to the consumer's
premises, service may be immediately discontinued. The consumer shall have an
opportunity for hearing within ten days of such emergency discontinuance.
   g.   All consumers using toxic or hazardous liquids, all hospitals,
mortuaries, wastewater treatment plants, laboratories, and all other hazardous
users install and maintain a reduced- pressure-principle backflow preventer in
the main water line serving each building on the premises. The backflow
preventer must be installed in an easily accessible location not subject to
flooding or freezing.
   h.   This section does not supersede the State Uniform Plumbing Code or any
Town of Ashley Ordinance.
(Ord. 97-7, passed 10-13-97)
Sec. 9-20   Penalties.
   10% on the first $3.00 and 3% on the excess over $3.00.
(Ord. 2022-02, § 1, 9-12-22)

Division I. In General 4
 
Notes
  4   Editor's Note: Res. No. 95-10 was adopted on August 7, 1995, which noted
4 the Town's action to maintain compliance with the IDEM Compliance Maintenance
  Annual Report.
Sec. 9-21   Authority to Operate.
   Indiana Code, § 36-9-2-17, authorizes a Town to collect, process, and
dispose of waste substances and domestic or sanitary sewage; and to establish,
maintain, and operate sewers, collect and disposal Systems, and systems to
collect and dispose of waste substances.
Sec. 9-22   Industrial Waste Cost Recovery.
   a.   The Town of Ashley agrees to assure the Environmental Protection Agency
(EPA) that a cost recovery system, satisfactory to EPA, will be enacted if
industrial wastes should be found to be significant in the future. (Res. No. 3-
81, § I, 5-18-81)
   b.   The cost recovery system, if found to be required in the future, will
satisfy those requirements of applicable sections of the Code of Federal
Regulations, namely: 40 CFR Part 35.925-12 and 35.925, and 35.935-13, as they
may be amended from time to time. (Res. No. 3-81, § 2, 5-18-81)
Sec. 9-23   Definitions.
   Unless the context specifically indicates otherwise, the meaning of terms
used in the ordinance shall be as follows:
   (a)   "Ammonia[ll]" (or NH -N) shall have the same meaning as defined in the
Sewer Use Ordinance.
   (b)   "Board" shall mean the Town Council of the Town of Ashley, or any duly
authorized officials acting in its behalf.
   (c)   "Bod" (or Biochemical Oxygen Demand) shall have the same meaning as
defined in the Sewer Use Ordinance.
   (d)   "CBOD" (or Carbonaceous Biochemical Oxygen Demand) shall have the same
meaning as defined in the Sewer Use Ordinance.
   (e)   "COD" (or Chemical Oxygen Demand) shall have the same meaning as
defined in the Sewer Use Ordinance.
   (f)   "Local Capital Costs" shall mean the average annual principal and
interest payments on all proposed revenue bonds or other long-term capital
debt.
   (g)   "Excessive Strength Surcharge" shall mean an additional charge which
is billed to users for treating sewage wastes with an average strength in
excess of "normal domestic sewage."
   (h)   "Industrial Wastes" shall mean the wastewater discharge from
industrial, trade or business processes as distinct from employee wastes or
wastes from sanitary conveniences.
   (i)   "NPDES (National Pollutant Discharge Elimination System) Permit" shall
have the same meaning as defined in the Sewer Use Ordinance.
   (j)   "Normal Domestic Sewage" (for the purpose of determining surcharges)
shall mean wastewater or sewage having an average daily concentration as
follow:
      5.5.   not more than 220 mg/l
      BOD not more than 220 mg/l
      Ammonia not more than 60 mg/l
   As defined by origin, wastewaters from segregated domestic and/or sanitary
conveniences as distinct from industrial processes.
   (k)   "Operation and Maintenance Cost" include all costs, direct and
indirect, necessary to provide adequate wastewater collection, transport and
treatment on a continuing basis and produce discharges to receiving waters that
conform with all related Federal, State, and local requirements. (These costs
include replacement.)
   (l)   "Other Service Charges" shall mean tap charges, connection charges,
area charges, and other identifiable charges other than excessive strength
surcharges.
   (m)   "Person" shall mean any and all person, natural or artificial,
including any individual, firm, company, municipal or private corporation,
association, society, institution, enterprise, governmental agency or other
entity.
   (n)   "Replacement Costs" shall mean the expenditures for obtaining and
installing equipment, accessories or appurtenances which are necessary during
the useful life of the treatment works to maintain the capacity and performance
for which such works were designed and constructed.
   (o)   "S.S." (or suspended solids) shall have the same meaning as defined in
the Sewer Use Ordinance.
   (p)   "Shall" is mandatory; "May" is permissive.
   (q)   "Sewage" shall have the same meaning as defined in the Sewer Use
Ordinance.
   (r)   "Sewer Use Ordinance" shall mean a separate and companion enactment to
this Ordinance, which regulates the connection to and use of public and private
sewers.
   (s)   "Town" shall mean the Town of Ashley acting by and through the Town
Council.
   (t)   "User Charge" shall mean a charge levied on users of the wastewater
treatment works for the cost of operation and maintenance of such works
pursuant to Section 204(b) of Public Law 92-500.
   (u)   "User Class" shall mean the division of wastewater treatment customers
by source, function, waste characteristics, and process or discharge
similarities, (i.e. residential, commercial, industrial, institutional, and
governmental in the User Charge System).
      Residential User - shall mean a user of the treatment works whose
premises or building is used primarily as a residence for one or more person,
including all dwelling units, etc.
      Commercial User - shall mean any establishment involved in a commercial
enterprise, business or service which, based on a determination by the Town,
discharges primarily segregated domestic wastes or wastes from sanitary
conveniences.
      Institutional User - shall mean any establishment involved in a social,
charitable, governmental, religious, and/or educational function which, based
on a determination by the Town, discharges primarily segregated domestic wastes
or wastes from sanitary conveniences.
      Industrial User - shall mean any manufacturing or processing facility
that discharges industrial waste to a wastewater treatment works. (Ord. No. 95-
05, § 1, 11-13-95; Am. Ord. No. 2006-15, § 1, 11-13-06)
Sec. 9-24   Four (4) Classes of Users of Sewage Works.
   Every person whose premises are served by said sewage works shall be charged
for the service provided. These charges are established for each user class, as
defined, in order that the sewage works shall recover, from each user and user
class, revenue which is proportional to its use of the treatment works in terms
of volume and load. User charges are levied to defray the cost of operation and
maintenance (including replacement) of the treatment works. User charges shall
be uniform in magnitude within a user class.
      (a)   User charges are subject to the rules and regulations adopted by
the U.S. Environmental Protection Agency published in the Federal Register
February 17, 1984 (40 CFR 35.2140). Replacement costs, which are recovered
through the system of user charges, shall be based upon the expected useful
life of the sewage works equipment.
      (b)   The various classes of users of the treatment works for the purpose
of this Ordinance, shall be as follows:
      Residential
      Commercial
      Institutional
      Industrial
(Ord. No. 95-05, § 2, 11-13-95)
Sec. 9-25   Basis of Sewage Rates and Charges.
   For the use of the service rendered by sewage works, rates and charges shall
be collected from the owners of each and every lot, parcel of real estate or
building that is connected with the Town's sanitary sewer system or otherwise
discharges sanitary sewage, industrial wastes, water or other liquids, either
directly or indirectly, into the sanitary sewage System of the Town. Such rates
and charges include user charges, debt service costs, which rates and charges
shall be payable as hereinafter provided and shall be in an amount determined
as follows:
   The sewage rates and charges shall be based on the quantity of water used on
or in the property or premises subject to such rates and charges as the same is
measured by the water meter there in use, plus a billing and collection charge
pre bill except as herein otherwise provided. For the purpose of billing and
collecting the charges for sewage service, the water meters shall be read
monthly and the users shall be billed each month (or period equaling a month).
The water usage schedule on which the amount of said rates and charges shall be
determined is as follows. (Ord. No. 95-05, § 3(a), 11-13-95)
